1201 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Garces v. R&K Spero Co., LLC


CV095025895S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN AT NEW HAVEN


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1507



May 29, 2009, Decided 
May 29, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former employee sued defendant employer for intentional infliction of emotional distress, negligent infliction of emotional distress, wrongful discharge, breach of implied covenant of good faith, unjust enrichment, sexual harassment, religious discrimination and invasion of privacy. The employer moved to strike several of those counts for failure to state a cause of action.


OVERVIEW: A store supervisor and manager spoke "badly" about the employee to other employees, mocked her because she lacked fluency in English and denied her use of the bathroom on several occasions, on one occasion when the employee explained that she was undergoing her menstrual cycle. Shortly after that incident, the employee was removed from the work schedule. She initially did not receive any explanation. She was subsequently informed that she was terminated because her religious obligations were in conflict with the employer's needs. The court held that requiring the employee to beg for a bathroom key to the point where she bled through her clothing could lead an average member of the community to exclaim, "Outrageous." Making her wait over 48 hours before telling her that she was fired" was sufficiently wrongful and therefore, satisfied the pleading requirements for negligent infliction of emotional distress. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-60(a)(8) made clear, without allegations of any unwelcome sexual advances or requests for sexual favors or any conduct of a sexual nature, the employer could not have committed sexual harassment, as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The employers motion to strike was denied as to the counts for intentional infliction of emotional distress, negligent infliction of emotional distress, and invasion of privacy. It was accepted as to the count asserting sexual harassment.

 

1202 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


St. Paul Travelers Cos. v. Kuehl


CV064025559S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1473



May 27, 2009, Decided 
May 27, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by St. Paul Travelers Cos. v. Kuehl, 299 Conn. 819, 2011 Conn. LEXIS 13 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: St. Paul Travelers Cos. v. Kuehl, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 465 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 19, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurance company brought an action against defendant widow, seeking a declaration that 2005 Conn. Acts 230 § 2 was unconstitutional. Defendant law firm intervened. The insurance company moved for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The insurance company argued, inter alia, that 2005 Conn. Acts 230 § 2, which allowed the widow to apply for workers' compensation survivor's benefits, was unconstitutional as a public emolument. The court agreed. Legislation seeking to remedy a procedural default for which the state was not responsible did not serve a public purpose and ran afoul of Conn. Const. art. I, § 1. It was clear that 2005 Conn. Acts 230 § 2 was designed to benefit the widow individually, even though it did not mention her by name. The class of persons benefitted were those dependents of a deceased employee seeking compensation arising out of the death of the deceased employee, whose date of injury was between June 1, 1991 and June 30, 1991 and whose death was between November 1, 1992 and November 30, 1992. This was indeed a thinly constricted category. The insurance company provided sufficient evidence to support its assertion that 2005 Conn. Acts 230 § 2 was narrowly drawn and passed to provide a benefit to only a single person, the widow. It was highly unlikely that another individual would have benefitted. Cases cited by the widow in opposition benefitted classes of persons, not individuals.


OUTCOME: The motion for summary judgment was granted.

 

1203 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Simmons


LLICR071245152


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD AT LITCHFIELD


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3273



May 27, 2009, Decided


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with sexual assault in the second degree, risk of injury to a minor and delivery of alcohol to a minor. A jury failed to delivery a unanimous verdict and a mistrial was declared. Defendant moved to dismiss the information.


OVERVIEW: In support of his motion, defendant argued that the State will not produce new evidence and, therefore, the information should be dismissed for insufficient evidence. The court disagreed, finding that defendant did not conclusively establish that the court had before it all the State's evidence. The court also found no overriding equitable considerations necessitating a dismissal of the information under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-56. Defendant also argued that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 was void for vagueness as applied to the circumstances of the case. The court disagreed, finding that § 53-21 required the State to establish that defendant had a general intent to engage in the proscribed act that resulted in the sexual assault of the victim. The court also found that a person of ordinary intelligence would know that sexual intercourse was likely to impair the morals of a minor child and thus, § 53-21 was not void for vagueness on the "morals" provision. The court noted that defendant made no plausible argument that he acted in reliance on the belief that his conduct was lawful or that a person of ordinary intelligence would have no reason to know he was engaging in prohibited conduct.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion to dismiss was denied.

Parrott v. State

1205 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Roszkowski


FBTCR06218479T


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD AT BRIDGEPORT


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1401



May 26, 2009, Decided 
May 26, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of capital felony, and the State sought a death sentence. Defendant provided notice that, during the penalty phase hearing, he intended to offer evidence in the nature of expert psychiatric testimony by certain mental health professionals. The State filed a motion in limine seeking to preclude such evidence. The State also requested that the court conduct a Porter hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant wished to present the evidence at issue for the purpose of establishing a statutory mitigating factor pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a(h)(3). The State sought to preclude such evidence as, inter alia, unreliable. The court found, however, that the plain language of § 53a-46a(c) drew a clear distinction between mitigation evidence and aggravation evidence offered in a capital felony penalty phase hearing. Mitigation evidence needed only to have been relevant in order to have been admissible, whereas aggravation evidence needed to have comported with the rules which governed the admission of evidence in criminal trials. On its face, the language of the statute authorized a judge presiding over a penalty hearing to exclude mitigating evidence only on the basis of a lack of relevancy. The Supreme Court of Connecticut had declined to read into the statute a foundational requirement of reliability for admissibility of mitigating evidence at a capital felony phase hearing. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a(c) should have been applied as written, and was not unconstitutional in allowing the State to rebut mitigation evidence under a "relevancy only" standard.


OUTCOME: The motion in limine was denied.

 

1206 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hanton v. Warden


CV084002247S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND AT ROCKVILLE


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1405



May 21, 2009, Decided 
May 21, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus seeking to challenge a determination of the Connecticut Board of Pardons and Paroles that he committed a parole violation and the resulting revocation of his parole. Respondent warden moved to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The habeas court held that any due process violations that might have occurred pertaining to a 2005 remand to custody and parole violation were supplanted by the inmate's release to parole on May 14, 2007 and the ensuing parole violations in December 2007. The December 2007 parole violations resulted in an April 2008 conviction. The inmate was not confined due to any due process violations that might have occurred between 2005 and 2007. The claim of fabricated reasons for the 2005 parole revocation failed to state a claim and was moot. The Board appeared to not have adhered to time frames specified by state regulations. However, these failures did not render the inmate's confinement illegal. The Board had several bases for revoking the inmate's parole. The delays in ultimately arriving at the parole revocation determination did not weaken, undermine, or render unlawful the parole revocation itself as based on the inmate's violations of the conditions of his release to parole. The due process claim failed to state a claim upon which habeas corpus relief could be granted and was moot. The petition was dismissed under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 23-29(3) and (4).


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss the petition in its entirety was granted. Judgment was entered dismissing the petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

1208 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


In re Vicente S.


U06CP04004779A, U06CP04004780A, U06CP04004781A, U06CP06005466A


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, CHILD PROTECTION SESSION AT MIDDLETOWN


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1451



May 18, 2009, Decided 
May 18, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner commissioner of the department of children and families (DCF) filed petitions for the termination of the rights of respondents, a mother and a father, alleging violations of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(j)(3)(B) as to both parents, and § 17a-112(j)(3)(A) and (D) as to the father.


OVERVIEW: The court found that DCF proved, by clear and convincing evidence, the allegations of the termination petition and that termination of respondents' parental rights was in the best interest of the children. Among other things, the court found that respondents were failed to achieve such degree of personal rehabilitation as would encourage the belief that within a reasonable period of time they could assume a responsible position in the children's lives. While DCF made reasonable efforts as to the mother and the mother complied with some of the steps ordered, the mother did not maintain suitable employment, was discharged from a supportive housing program, missed scheduled visitations, continued involvement with the criminal system, and did not follow through with counseling. The court also found that DCF made reasonable efforts as to the father under the circumstances of his unavailability due to being incarcerated. The father also abandoned the children, in that he failed to maintain a reasonable degree of interest, concern, or responsibility as to their welfare. The court also noted that the children were receiving love, nurturing and appropriate care from their foster parents.


OUTCOME: The parental rights of the mother and the father were terminated. The commissioner of DCF was appointed statutory parents of the children.

 

1209 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


McCorison v. McCorison


FA074032877S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1294



May 13, 2009, Decided 
May 13, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife filed an action for dissolution of marriage against defendant husband. The husband moved for DNA testing of the four children born during the marriage. The motion was granted and the youngest child was found not to be the husband's biological child. Before the court was the husband's motion for access with the youngest child. The youngest child's biological father was added as a party to the instant action.


OVERVIEW: During a deposition, the wife admitted having sexual relations with another man during the parties' marriage, prompting the husband's request for DNA testing. The youngest child, who was five years and three months old at the time of trial, believed that the husband was her father until she was there years and nine months old. Following the results of the DNA testing, the wife and the biological father refused to allow the child to visit with the husband. The child was made aware that the biological father was her father, not the husband. The court concluded that it would be in the child's best interest to have visitation with the husband. The court found that the sudden and total removal of the husband from the child's life, without a substantially valid reason, exposed the child to psychological harm. While the bond between the child and the husband diminished during the year the husband was not permitted access to the child, the child and the husband had a strong and appropriate parent-child attachment before that time. In addition, the court credited the guardian ad litem's testimony that the child wanted to visit the husband when her brothers visited him.


OUTCOME: The husband's motion for access was granted. The wife's motion to dismiss was denied. An evaluation of the child was ordered prior to the court entering a permanent visitation schedule for the husband.

 

1210 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Lost Trail, LLC v. Town of Weston


FSTCV055000500S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK AT STAMFORD


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1191



May 8, 2009, Decided 
May 8, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, Dismissed by, in part Lost Trail, LLC v. Town of Weston, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1483 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 9, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Lost Trail, LLC v. Town of Weston, 485 F. Supp. 2d 59, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 29586 (D. Conn., Apr. 19, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner filed suit against defendant town, alleging inverse condemnation and seeking a judgment that its land be recognized not as a subdivision but as two adjacent lots and that zoning and building permits be issued for the same. The town filed a motion to dismiss, arguing that the inverse condemnation claim did not meet the final decision requirement and that the declaratory judgment claim was not ripe for adjudication.


OVERVIEW: The owner alleged that town official approved the dividing of the property into four lot, but the town refused to allow the development of the property and required subdivision approval. The owner contended that applying for zoning permits would be futile. The superior court held that the actions of the town did not amount to a confiscation of the owner's property. A final decision on the owner's plan had not been rendered. The owner's unsupported allegations were insufficient to show that applying for subdivision approval would have been futile. The complaint was devoid of any specifics as to how the town's actions rendered the property unusable for any practical purpose or resulted in the deprivation of value to the land. The superior court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the declaratory judgment matter because the owner failed to exhaust its administrative remedies. It neither filed an application for subdivision approval, nor an application for zoning permits. Although the owner claimed that any action would have been futile, it failed to claim that the town would not hear its argument, review its application, or not be able to provide the relief requested.


OUTCOME: The superior court granted the town's motion to dismiss.

 

1211 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


In re Giovanni C.


H14CP06008809A, H14CP060088010A, H14CP06008811A


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, CHILD PROTECTION SESSION AT MIDDLETOWN


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1260



May 7, 2009, Decided 
May 7, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by In re Giovanni C., 120 Conn. App. 277, 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 115 (2010)
Affirmed by In re Giovanni C., 120 Conn. App. 274, 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 117 (2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Commissioner of the Department of Children and Families (DCF), filed petitions to terminate the parental rights (TPR) of respondents, a mother and father, over their three children based on their failure to rehabilitate pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(j)(3)(B). The children had been previously adjudicated as neglected.


OVERVIEW: The father had a lengthy history of alcohol abuse and violence. After an episode of physical violence between the parents, wherein the police were called, the children were adjudicated as neglected and their temporary custody was granted to DCF. Specific steps were issued to each parent to facilitate possible reunification. Thereafter, DCF sought TPR pursuant to § 17a-112(j)(3)(B). The court found that reasonable efforts to reunify the children with their parents were not successful because the parents had not completed their specific steps in a timely manner pursuant to § 17a-112(j)(3)(B) and Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 35a-7A. Both parents minimized their problems and failed to obtain treatment for them, the mother was not consistent in her attempts at rehabilitation, and the father did not believe that he had any problems. Services were offered to each parent and to the children, and it was determined that reasonable efforts by DCF were made with respect to the mother. Such efforts were not required as to the father under § 17a-112(j). Noting that the children were in stable non-relative foster placements, the court found that TPR was in the children's best interests.


OUTCOME: The court granted DCF's petition and terminated the parental rights of the mother and father. DCF was appointed as the statutory parent of the children.

 

1212 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Watson v. Kasanowski


FA094041690


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1218



May 7, 2009, Decided 
May 7, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father moved to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction applicant maternal grandmother's application for visitation with the father's five-year-old child under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 46b-56 and -57, and the appointment of a guardian ad litem to represent the child.


OVERVIEW: The child's mother and the father shared joint legal custody, and exercised a shared parenting arrangement. The mother died. The trial court held that the grandmother did not plead sufficient facts to establish a parent-like relationship and that denial of visitation would cause harm to the child analogous to the harm contemplated in the abuse and neglect statutes, namely Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 46b-120 and -129. The application set forth an apparently delightful relationship between the grandmother and the child, but it did not meet the parent-like standard. Furthermore, there were no facts alleged that could be construed to meet the harm requirement. The trial court considered only the pleadings and did not consider the factual submissions proffered by the father's or the grandmother's affidavits. However, even if all of the affidavit entries had been included in the grandmother's initial pleadings, the Roth requirements were not met. The law had recognized the fundamental parental rights under the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and had fashioned a method to preserve those rights, recognizing the enormous responsibilities and concomitant privileges of parenthood.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted.

 

1213 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


A. Gallo & Co. v. McCarthy


CV094043592S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1258



May 5, 2009, Decided 
May 5, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Summary judgment granted by, in part, Judgment entered by, in part, Summary judgment denied by A. Gallo & Co. v. McCarthy, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 984 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 23, 2010)
Related proceeding at A. Gallo & Co. v. McCarthy, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1788 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 12, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, distributors of beer and soft drinks, sought a temporary injunction prohibiting defendants, the Commissioner of the Department of Environmental Protection (Connecticut), the attorney general, and the governor, from enforcing portions of 2009 Conn. Pub. Acts 09-01, which the distributors alleged violated the 5th and 14th Amendments of the United States Constitution and Conn. Const. art 1, § 11.


OVERVIEW: The distributors opened and funded special accounts in the State. 2009 Conn. Pub. Acts 09-01 required them to pay revenue generated from beverage container deposits to the Connecticut Department of Environmental Protection. The distributors asserted a vested property interest in the money they deposited in the accounts and sought to enjoin defendants from requiring them to pay, arguing that the payment constituted an unconstitutional taking of their property. The superior court held that the distributors had an adequate remedy at law and would not suffer irreparable harm if the temporary injunction was not granted. Any damages the distributors could suffer were reducible to monetary compensation. The distributors could seek to recover the amounts at issue by refusing to pay and defending against the attorney general's suit to recover the payments or by paying the amounts and seeking to recover them as just compensation. If the distributors paid the money to the State and were found to have had a vested interest in the money, they could be made whole with money damages. The equities favored the State because it was facing a massive financial crisis involving huge budget deficits.


OUTCOME: The superior court denied the distributors' application for a temporary injunction.

 

1214 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Elsey v. Warden, State Prison


CV054000330


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND AT ROCKVILLE


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1236



May 4, 2009, Decided 
May 4, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Elsey v. Comm'r of Corr., 126 Conn. App. 144, 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 22 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Elsey, 81 Conn. App. 738, 841 A.2d 714, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 82 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner alleged in his petition for a writ of habeas corpus that he was denied the effective assistance of trial counsel and appellate counsel, and that he was denied due process in that the State failed to disclose exculpatory evidence, all in violation of the Fifth, Sixth and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution and Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 8 and 9.


OVERVIEW: Three people were residing in a house when bullets entered the house through the windows and the walls. A woman living next door to the victims' house observed a small fire burning on the side of the victims' house. Two other men saw two or three unidentified men near the victims' house and called the police. The unidentified men ran to a black Pontiac Grand Am car. After a car chase, the police eventually identified the prisoner as one of the occupants of the car. According to the prisoner, the State did not disclose the foregoing information regarding a witness's sentence modifications. The court concluded that the prisoner failed to show that the evidence allegedly suppressed was favorable to him, either because it was exculpatory or impeaching. There was no evidence that the State had an agreement with the witness and that he would derive some benefit in exchange for his testimony. The prisoner failed to show any specific instances that indicated there was such impairment or compromise of his interest for the benefit of another party. Thus, the prisoner failed to demonstrate that his attorney was operating under an actual or potential conflict of interest.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

 

1215 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hayes v. State


X01CV075008002S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT WATERBURY


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1153



May 1, 2009, Decided 
May 1, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient filed suit against defendant State of Connecticut/John Dempsey Hospital and Health Center (State) pursuant to permission granted by the claims commissioner as provided for by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-160. The State moved to dismiss the amended complaint.


OVERVIEW: The reviewing court held that the claims commissioner concluded that the claim accrued only when the harm was discovered by way of an expert opinion. This finding of fact satisfied the timeliness provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-148(a). There had been no constitutional challenge with regard to the claims commissioner's decision as to the accrual date. The Connecticut general assembly had not passed a special act allowing the patient to sue the State, for which the Public Emoluments Clause, Conn. Const. art. I, § 1, would have allowed review. The reviewing court lacked jurisdiction to hear appeals from the claims commissioner because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-164a expressly exempted the claims commissioner from the operation of the Connecticut Uniform Administrative Procedure Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-183, the provision of that permitted an appeal to the reviewing court. The State sought to accomplish such an appeal in its motion to dismiss. However, the reviewing court did not have that authority, since the claims commissioner performed a legislative function directly reviewable only by the general assembly.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1216 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Decaro v. Town of Greenwich


FSTCV084013485S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK AT STAMFORD


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1166



April 30, 2009, Decided 
April 30, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner filed a declaratory judgment action against defendants, a town and town condemnation commission, seeking a declaration that the certification of the cost of new sewer construction in the section of town where he lived was inaccurate, contained inappropriate cost items, and improperly excluded applicable credits. The town and town condemnation commission moved to dismiss the declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: The property owner filed two separate lawsuits relating to sewer assessments for new sewers built in his area of town. The first case, in which he was not the named plaintiff, was an appeal by property owners from the levy of sewer assessments. The second case, in which he was the named plaintiff, involved the filing of a declaratory judgment action seeking a determination that certification of the sewer construction costs should not have occurred. The filing in both cases was based on Greenwich, Conn., Municipal Code § 259(a) allowing aggrieved parties to appeal assessments to the trial court. The town and town condemnation commission sought dismissal of the declaratory judgment action. The trial court found dismissal unwarranted because (1) the appeal of the assessment was permitted pursuant to Greenwich, Conn., Municipal Code § 259(a); (2) he could use a separate declaratory judgment to appeal despite the similar issue being considered in the first case; and (3) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-250 did not provide his exclusive remedy for appealing the assessment, especially since that statute applied to the water pollution control authority, and not sewer assessments.


OUTCOME: The trial court denied the motion to dismiss in its entirety.

 

1217 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Housatonic Valley Radiology Assocs., P.C.


CV074034061


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1118



April 28, 2009, Decided 
April 28, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19a-642, plaintiff office of health care access (OHCA) sued defendant provider to enforce the certificate of need (CON) process to operate imaging equipment. The provider alleged special defenses under U.S. Const. amend. V and Conn. Const. art. 1, § 11; and that 2006 Conn. Pub. Acts 06-28 (the Act) was unconstitutional. The OHCA moved to strike the provider's special defenses.


OVERVIEW: The OHCA sought a permanent injunction, barring the use of the equipment until the provider complied with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19a-639. The trial referee found that the provider did not allege facts to support the defense that an injunction would be an unconstitutional taking. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19a-639a(c) was regulatory. The broad application of § 19a-639a(c) to health care entities eliminated the possibility that the provider was unfairly singled out or deprived of economic use of its property in a way that implicated the takings clause of the federal or state constitution. The as-applied challenge failed for the same reason. The Act did not qualify as a bill of attainder; it did not impose punishment without a judicial trial, and it was not a historically recognized form of legislative punishment. No facts were alleged suggesting that the Act was penal in nature and therefore an ex post facto law, or that the Act was a validating act due to the OHCA's unlawful taking of the imaging equipment through legislative action. U.S. Const. amend. V's due process clause did not apply to the States. Conn. Agencies Regs. § 19a-643-17 did not provide for discrimination claims.


OUTCOME: The trial referee granted the motion.

 

1218 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


In re Inayiris P.


H12CP07011254A, H12CP07011255A


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, CHILD PROTECTION SESSION AT MIDDLETOWN


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1025



April 14, 2009, Decided 
April 14, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Department of Children and Families (DCF) (Connecticut), filed termination of parental rights (TPR) petitions against respondent parents, based on both parents' failure to rehabilitate in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(j)(3)(B). The petitions also alleged that the mother had abandoned each child and that she had no parent-child relationship in violation of § 17a-112(j)(3)(A) and (D).


OVERVIEW: Due to substance abuse problems of the mother, DCF filed neglect petitions concerning both children, and temporary custody orders were granted to it. A possible reunification plan for the parents was ordered, and thereafter, both children were deemed neglected. DCF's permanency plans for the children, which were approved by the court, proposed termination of parental rights and adoption. The court found that DCF made reasonable efforts to achieve each of the plans under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-111b(a). Thereafter, DCF sought TPR. The mother was absent from Connecticut for a period of time, failed to visit or maintain contact, and had endured domestic violence from the father. Both parents had substance abuse issues and had failed to financially support the children. There was clear and convincing evidence that DCF offered services to the parents and made reasonable efforts towards reunification. The evidence supported the grounds for termination under § 17a-112(j)(3)(B), (A), and (D), and that the best interests of the children were served by termination. They were thriving in a loving, nurturing environment with non-relative foster parents.


OUTCOME: The court granted DCF's petition and ordered the parental rights of the mother and the father terminated. The court appointed the DCF Commissioner as the statutory parent for the children.

 

1219 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


In re Christine B.


H12CP07011454A, H12CP07011455A, H12CP07011456A, H12CP07011457A


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, CHILD PROTECTION SESSION AT MIDDLETOWN


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 956



April 8, 2009, Decided 
April 8, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The department of children and families (DCF) filed petitions for termination of respondent mother's parental rights, alleging that the mother failed to rehabilitate in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(j)(3)(B), violated § 17a-112(j)(3)(C) as to the third child, and inflicted serious bodily injury on the other children in violation of § 17a-112(j)(3)(F).


OVERVIEW: Over a period of nine years, the mother was offered and/or received an extensive number of and exhaustive list of individual services relating to her four children, from or facilitated by DCF for purposes of reunification with the children. The four children were last removed from the mother's care following reports that the mother was physically abusing the children. The court found that DCF proved, by clear and convincing evidence, that DCF made reasonable efforts to reunify the mother and the children, but that the mother was unable or unwilling to reach a point where reunification was in the best interests of the children. The mother had pervasive psychological problems that impeded the mother's ability to effectively parent the children, the mother's home was unsafe, and the mother did not cooperate with therapy for the children. In addition, DCF proved, as to the third child, that she suffered serious physical and emotional injury while living with the mother and was diagnosed with post-traumatic stress disorder. The court found it in the best interest of the children to terminate the mother's parental rights.


OUTCOME: The parental rights of the mother were terminated as to all four children. The commissioner of the DCF was appointed as the statutory parent of the children.

 

1220 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Ayres v. Warden


CV054000532S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND AT ROCKVILLE


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 876



April 2, 2009, Decided 
April 2, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was initially charged with murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a, and ultimately pleaded guilty to manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55a. He was sentenced to 25 years incarceration. The inmate filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, alleging ineffective assistance of counsel under U.S. Const. amend. VI and XIV and Conn. Const. art. I, § 8.


OVERVIEW: The inmate, who shot and killed his estranged wife, alleged (1) that the trial court's plea canvass was deficient, rendering the inmate's pleas not knowing, intelligent, and voluntary; and (2) that he received ineffective assistance of his trial counsel in that counsel failed to file a motion to suppress the inmate's statement to the police, failed to investigate the circumstances surrounding the crime, and failed to apprise the inmate adequately of the advantages and disadvantages of going to trial. The court found that the majority of the inmate's claims could be decided on the unequivocal testimony of the inmate that he would not have proceeded to trial even if he knew he was going to be sentenced to the 25 years he ultimately received. He could not, therefore, hope to demonstrate prejudice resulting from his counsel's ineffective assistance because he could not prove that but for counsel's errors, the inmate would not have pleaded guilty and would have insisted on going to trial. Furthermore, the inmate's claim that the plea canvass was inadequate was procedurally defaulted. Finally, the inmate failed to show ineffectiveness from counsel's failure to file a motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

 

1221 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Passariello v. Connecticut Light & Power Co.


X06CV075005753S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT WATERBURY


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 880



March 31, 2009, Decided 
March 31, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners filed an action against defendant power company, alleging that the company's work overburdened the easements on their respective properties, constituted a trespass on their properties, constituted the creation of a private nuisance, and constituted an inverse condemnation of constitutional taking in violation of U.S. Const. amend. V and Conn. Const. art. 1, § 11. The company moved for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The owners' properties were encumbered by a utility transmission easement granted to the company. The easement had been included in an electric infrastructure project. As part of this project, the company performed work on the property encumbered by the easement. The owners contended that their use of their property had been harmed by the company's excessive use of the easement, including the cutting of trees and the construction of "offensive" towers and poles. They also claimed that the negative perceptions and stigma associated with newly installed high voltage power lines diminished the value of their properties. The company argued that the owners' inverse condemnation counts failed because the owners did not assert a constitutional taking. The superior court agreed, holding that the owners' allegations were insufficient to amount to a "taking" of their property in a constitutional sense. The owners did not allege or offer any evidence indicating that their use or enjoyment of their property had been abridged or destroyed to a substantial or sufficient degree to be confiscatory. The facts involved an alleged excessive or burdensome use of an existing easement.


OUTCOME: The superior court granted the company's motion for summary judgment as to the counts of the complaint alleging inverse condemnation. It denied the company's motion for partial summary judgment as to the counts alleging overburdening, trespass, and nuisance.

 

1222 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Mateo v. Mann


CV085022203


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 873



March 31, 2009, Decided 
April 1, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sued defendants, alleging certain environmental violations. Defendants moved to strike counts two and three of plaintiff's revised and amended complaint.


OVERVIEW: Count two of the complaint alleged that effluent from a greenhouse on defendants' property flowed onto the wetlands on plaintiff's property and contained excessive concentration of phosphorus which were harmful to the wetlands, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-16. Defendants argued that a regulatory scheme was in place, citing Conn. Agencies Regs. § 22a-133k-1 et seq. and annexed appendices. Those regulations listed hazardous chemicals but did not include phosphorus. Thus, defendants claimed that phosphorus was not within the regulatory scheme and its use was therefore not unreasonable. The court found, however, that the absence of a comprehensive legislative and regulatory scheme did not mean an action under § 22-16 was unavailable. Thus, count two stated a valid cause of action without alleging standards that constituted unreasonable pollution. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-16 was not unconstitutional by reason of vagueness. Finally, by alleging, as plaintiff did, that effluent negligently released from defendants' drainage system endangered the wetlands on plaintiff's property, plaintiff stated a valid cause of action of private nuisance.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike was denied.

 

1223 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Buddington Park Condo. v. Shelton Planning & Zoning


CV084009709S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF ANSONIA-MILFORD AT DERBY


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1021



March 30, 2009, Decided 
March 31, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Buddington Park Condo. Ass'n v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n, 125 Conn. App. 724, 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 585 (2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a condominium association and two unit owners, sought review of a decision from defendant, a town planning and zoning commission (PZC), which adopted a resolution that permitted defendant developer's application for seven residential units pursuant to Shelton, Conn., Zoning Regs. § 34.


OVERVIEW: The developer submitted an application to the PZC for development of residential units on its property. After public hearings, the PZC conditionally voted to approve the application, and a resolution permitting it with certain changes was adopted. Plaintiffs sought review thereof. The court initially found that they were aggrieved and had standing to pursue the appeal, based on their ownership of property within the requisite distance of the development. The court found that the planned development district (PDD) complied with § 34. There was no requirement that the PDD provide standards for setbacks and building locations. Adequate notice pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-3(a) was provided to plaintiffs, who appeared and participated in the hearings. The fact that the property was described by an address and referral to the assessor's map rather than by metes and bounds did not render the notice inadequate. Any claim that certain PZC members should have been disqualified was waived. The PDD appeared consistent with the area. The court concluded that there was no abuse of discretion by the PZC's adoption of the resolution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the PZC and dismissed the appeal.

In re Johnson R.


M08CP06010181A, M08CP06010182A, M08CP06010183A


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, CHILD PROTECTION SESSION AT MIDDLETOWN


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 842



March 26, 2009, Decided 
March 26, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by, Stay denied by In re Johnson R., 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2051 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 13, 2009)
Affirmed by In re Johnson R., 121 Conn. App. 464, 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 215 (2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Department of Children and Families (DCF) filed a petition to terminate the parental rights (TPR) of respondents, a mother and father, as to three of their children. The sole ground alleged against each parent in each such petition was failure to rehabilitate in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(j)(3)(B).


OVERVIEW: The children were adjudicated as neglected and were committed to the care, custody and guardianship of DCF. The father was found not to be competent and not restorable to competency. Between the date of the neglect adjudications and dispositions and the date of the end of the TPR hearing, in violation of § 17a-112(j)(3)(B) neither parent was able to rehabilitate herself or himself. The family had not been an intact family for in excess of two years. Thus, the parents did not have the benefit of any presumption that they were fit to care for such children, and, unfortunately for the parents, the evidence was overwhelmingly to the contrary. Over a period of 15 years, the parents had been offered and/or had received a remarkable number of and exhaustive list of individual services and services relating to their children from or facilitated by DCF for purposes of reunification. The court held that DCF had made reasonable efforts to reunite the parents and each of their children. Each child was bonded to the foster parents with whom they resided. It was in the best interest of the children to terminate the parental rights of the biological mother and the biological father.


OUTCOME: The parental rights of the mother and the father were terminated. The Commissioner of DCF was appointed the statutory parent.

Town of Bozrah v. Chmurynski


No. 084008160


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 809



March 20, 2009, Decided 
March 20, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Chmurynski v. Robbins, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 71282 (D. Conn., July 1, 2011)
Reversed by, Remanded by Town of Bozrah v. Chmurynski, 2012 Conn. LEXIS 50 (Conn., Feb. 14, 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a town and a zoning enforcement officer, filed a complaint seeking a temporary injunction to allow for inspection of defendant residents' property by the officer after the officer was informed that the property had zoning regulation violations and the residents declined to allow the officer to inspect the property.


OVERVIEW: The officer received a report that the residents were keeping junk, or maintaining a junkyard, on their property. The officer twice attempted to investigate, but the residents rebuffed his efforts. Nevertheless, the officer spotted vehicles on the residents' lawn that apparently could fit the definition of junk. As a result, the town and officer sought a temporary injunction to overcome the residents' resistance to such an examination, and explained that the town's zoning commission decided how zoning regulations were to be enforced and the officer pursuant to the town zoning regulations was charged with investigating reported violations. The trial court found that the law gave very little indication of the standard that had to be met to obtain a regulatory search warrant. However, it determined that in reviewing the temporary injunction request, the town for the public good and the officer who had jurisdiction needed to be allowed to investigate, as authorized by Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 8-12 and 8-3 to determine what action, if any, could be taken. It also set forth conditions on the granting of that temporary injunction to make the inspection as unobtrusive as possible.


OUTCOME: The trial court ordered that a temporary injunction be issued and set forth conditions regarding it so that an inspection of the property could occur that would be the least intrusive inspection for the residents.

 

1226 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Laliberte v. O'Meara


CV085008140


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY AT WATERBURY


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 699



March 17, 2009, Decided 
March 18, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Commissioner of the Department of Developmental Services, made a motion to dismiss counts three, four, six, and seven of an amended complaint filed by plaintiff mother, individually and on behalf of her son. The counts claimed discrimination in violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 12112 et seq., retaliatory discrimination, a violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-238.


OVERVIEW: The complaint alleged that the son was injured while in the care and custody of the Department when he was allowed to consume peanut butter despite a well-documented peanut allergy and that he was discriminated against by the Commissioner since the occurrence of that incident. The Commissioner sought to dismiss the counts at issue based on sovereign immunity. The mother conceded that count three, alleging disability discrimination, should be dismissed and that counts four and six could only stand in order to obtain injunctive relief. The court dismissed counts three and seven completely and counts four and six in part. Counts four and six could not be pursued to the extent of obtaining money damages as Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-99 did not serve as a waiver of sovereign immunity as to those damages. However, because sufficient facts were pleaded to indicate that the Commissioner, through his agents, discriminated against the son in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-71, injunctive relief could be claimed. Count seven had to be dismissed because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-238 did not establish a cause of action separate from that permitted for negligence by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19a-24.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to dismiss counts three and seven in their entirety and counts four and six only to the extent that money damages were sought. Those counts remained insofar as they sought injunctive relief.

 

1227 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Foote v. Warden


CV054000266S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND AT ROCKVILLE


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 753



March 16, 2009, Decided 
March 16, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Foote v. Comm'r of Corr., 125 Conn. App. 296, 8 A.3d 524, 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 542 (Nov. 30, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Foote, 85 Conn. App. 356, 857 A.2d 406, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 415 (Oct. 5, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was convicted, upon a nolo contendere plea, of transportation of narcotics with the intent to sell by a non-drug-dependent person, after the denial of his motion to suppress. The Connecticut Appellate Court upheld the denial of the suppression motion. The inmate filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus alleging ineffective assistance of counsel under the Sixth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. VI, and Conn. Const. art. I, § 8.


OVERVIEW: The habeas court held that differences in a trooper's testimony and the police report were minor. Defense counsel properly argued credibility, and the suppression court found that the troopers' testimony that consent to the search had been given was more credible. The failure to determine whether there had been a videotape of the stop, or to review the audio or transcripts of the police dispatch call did not constitute ineffective assistance as there was no evidence as to their existence or substance. The decision not to pursue a probable cause hearing was a strategic matter. It was not shown that the appellate brief was substandard. No prejudice was shown in the late filing of the petition for certification. No prejudice was shown in the failure to determine that the inmate was drug-dependent as the inmate entered a nolo contendere plea. The inmate did not establish that he would have proceeded to a trial if he had known of a drug dependency claim. Finally, the inmate failed to show that he would have received a more favorable result had he taken the case to trial.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

Ostroski v. Warden, State Prison


TSRCV044000012S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND AT ROCKVILLE


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 618



March 9, 2009, Decided 
March 9, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Ostroski v. Comm'r of Corr., 2011 Conn. LEXIS 313 (Conn., July 5, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Ostroski, 201 Conn. 534, 518 A.2d 915, 1986 Conn. LEXIS 1011 (1986)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted of murder following a bench trial and was sentenced. Thereafter, petitioner filed a pro se second amended petition for writ of habeas corpus challenging the calculation and application of statutory good time credits, and claiming that trial defense trial counsel failed to provide effective assistance.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with murder after a 19-year-old woman was stabbed to death in 1977. He was found guilty and sentenced to a prison term of not less than 25 years nor more than life. His conviction was reversed on appeal. After a retrial, a jury, in 1983, found him guilty of murder. He received the same sentence as before. Petitioner on appeal raised the issue of ineffective assistance of counsel, but the state supreme court in affirming stated the claim should be raised in a habeas corpus proceeding. About 20 years later, he filed the second amended petition for writ of habeas corpus and raised the effective assistance of counsel issue, less than one year after his trial counsel had died. Petitioner also claimed that his life sentence should have been changed to a 60-year sentence pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-35b. Regarding the sentence, the trial court found that an indeterminate sentence could be applied to pre-1981 offenses and that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-35b only involved determinate sentences imposed after 1981. It then found as to the ineffective assistance claim that his inexcusable delay of 18 years in waiting to raise the issue meant it was forfeited.


OUTCOME: The trial court denied the second amended petition for writ of habeas corpus filed by petitioner.

 

1229 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Castro


CR070213079S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 12 AT MANCHESTER


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 496



March 4, 2009, Decided 
March 4, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of breach of peace in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181(a)(4), disorderly conduct in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-182(a)(2) and harassment in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183(a)(2). Defendant then filed motions to set aside the verdict and enter a judgment of acquittal or, alternatively, to order a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been able to get along with his neighbor, but a dispute led to animosity between the two men. The neighbor, who was white, bought and displayed a Confederate flag. Defendant, who was Hispanic, responded by spray painting a tarp he hung on a fence and the fence itself with the letters "KKK." Defendant was charged with breach of peace in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181(a)(4), disorderly conduct in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-182(a)(2), and harassment in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183(a)(2). Following a trial, the jury convicted him of each of those charges. Defendant then filed posttrial motions to overturn the jury's verdicts. The trial court found that defendant's alleged criminal conduct consisted of pure speech. It then found that for the statutes for each of the crimes to not be found unconstitutional as applied, the statements that defendant expressed had to be able to be understood as "fighting words," which were not constitutionally protected. It concluded that defendant had to be acquitted on each of the three charges because the State did not prove that the statements were "fighting words."


OUTCOME: The trial court granted defendant's motion to set aside the verdict and for a judgment of acquittal as to all counts. It then entered a judgment of acquittal as to all counts and denied the motion for a new trial.

In re Sole S.


F04CP03005606A


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, CHILD PROTECTION SESSION AT MIDDLETOWN


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 546



March 4, 2009, Decided 
March 4, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by In re Sole S., 119 Conn. App. 187, 986 A.2d 351, 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 34 (2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Department of Children and Families (DCF) filed a petition to terminate the parental rights of respondents, a mother and a father, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(j)(3), to their child based on the father's abandonment the mother's failure to achieve such a degree of personal rehabilitation as would encourage the belief that within a reasonable period of time she could assume a responsible position the child's life.


OVERVIEW: While the father was incarcerated, the mother was arrested for risk of injury to the subject child's half-sibling and interfering with a police officer. The child was placed in DCF custody and later found to be neglected. The child was returned to the parents, but entered DCF custody after the parents were both incarcerated. The court found that respondents had failed to, and were unable and/or unwilling to achieve such degree of person rehabilitation as would encourage the belief that within a reasonable period of time, considering the age and needs of the child, they could assume a responsible position the child's life. Among other things, the court found that the parents were offered numerous services. The mother failed to comply with many of the specific steps ordered and made not material effort to comply. While the father attempted to comply with the specific steps ordered, he had been unable to earn sufficient legal income or obtain suitable housing. The court also found that termination of respondent's parental rights was in the child's best interest, noting that the child's foster mother provided love, nurturing, and appropriate care in a stable environment.


OUTCOME: The parental rights of the mother and the father were terminated.

 

1231 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Mallory v. Hartford Roman Catholic Diocesan Corp.


X10UWYCV075007642S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY AT WATERBURY


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 560



February 24, 2009, Decided 
February 24, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part Mallory v. Hartford Roman Catholic Diocesan Corp., 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 590 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 24, 2009)
Related proceeding at, Motion denied by Doe v. Hartford Roman Catholic Diocesan Corp., 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1178 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 2, 2012)
Related proceeding at Hartford Roman Catholic Diocesan Corp. v. Interstate Fire & Cas. Co., 297 F.R.D. 22, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 10029 (D. Conn., 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an alleged sexual abuse victim, sued defendant archdiocese, which had employed the alleged abuser, claiming negligent, reckless, and wanton conduct and violations of the child abuse reporting statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-101a. The diocese moved to strike several allegations of negligence, claiming they were not justiciable as they would involve a constitutionally impermissible involvement in matters of internal church governance.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff alleged, inter alia, the archdiocese was negligent in failing to evaluate the mental fitness of the clergyman who abused him when he was a child; failing to investigate and report his suspicious conduct; and failing to establish a policy of reporting and investigating clergy engaged in sexual misconduct. The court held that the bulk of the allegations attacked by the archdiocese were negligent hiring and supervision claims that could be decided by neutral tort standards without delving into church doctrine or religious practices in violation of the Free Exercise Clause of the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I. But as the constitutional guarantee of the free exercise of religious authority required secular institutions to defer to the decisions of religious institutions in their employment relations with their religious employees, allegations involving the clergyman's fitness to be a priest, as well as his and the archdiocese's relationship with the members of the congregation, impermissibly intruded on church doctrine or practices. As the complaint did not allege any failure to report the priest's abuse of the plaintiff, it failed to state a claim under § 17a-101.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike was granted as to the allegations that the archdiocese violated § 17a-101, the allegations involving the clergyman's fitness to be a priest, and the allegations involving the clergyman's and archdiocese's relationship with members of the congregation. The motion to strike was otherwise denied.

 

1232 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Mallory v. Hartford Roman Catholic Diocesan Corp.


X10UWYCV075007645S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY AT WATERBURY


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 575



February 24, 2009, Decided 
February 24, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff church member claimed that he was sexually abused by a Roman Catholic priest who was the agent, servant and/or employee of defendant church. The church moved to strike several individual allegations of negligence, claiming they would involve impermissible involvement in matters of internal church governance and clergy employment decisions which it claimed were protected by the federal and state constitutional religion clauses.


OVERVIEW: The church member claimed that his injuries and damages were due to the negligence and carelessness of the church in a number of ways. The court held the bulk of the allegations attacked by the church could be subject to neutral tort standards without delving into church doctrine or religious practices. However some would require such an impermissible intrusion. Those allegations involved fitness to be a priest as well as the priest's relationship with the church and the "Catholic faithful." The constitutional guarantee of the free exercise of religious authority required secular institutions to defer to the decisions of religious institutions in their employment relations with their religious employees. Neither of the cited allegations of the complaint referred to the failure to report abuse of the church member, therefore they failed to state a cause of action based on Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-101. Although the church member claimed that his allegation regarding the church's failure to report suspicions of the priest's abuse of minors could include suspicions of the member's abuse by the priest, that was not how the claim was framed.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike was granted as to the allegations which delving into church doctrine or religious practices. The motion was denied as to those allegations involving neutral tort standards.

Mallory v. Hartford Roman Catholic Diocesan Corp.


X10UWYCV075007646S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY AT WATERBURY


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 590



February 24, 2009, Decided 
February 24, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Mallory v. Hartford Roman Catholic Diocesan Corp., 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 575 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 24, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the alleged sexual abuse victim, sued defendant, the Roman Catholic Archdiocese, for injuries and damages resulting from the alleged negligence and carelessness of the Archdiocese and from the alleged reckless and wanton conduct of the Archdiocese. The Archdiocese filed a motion, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 10-39, to strike several individual allegations of negligence.


OVERVIEW: The victim claimed that he was sexually abused by a Roman Catholic priest of the Archdiocese. The Archdiocese claimed that certain of the victim's allegations involved matters of internal church governance and clergy employment decisions which were not justiciable as they were protected from government intrusion by the religion clauses of the United States and Connecticut Constitutions. In addition, the Archdiocese argued that the victim did not have a cause of action based on the failure to report suspected abuse of another child. The court found that the bulk of the allegations attacked by the Archdiocese were subject to neutral tort standards and did not delve into church doctrine or religious practices. However, the allegations involving the priest's fitness to be a priest as well as his and the Archdiocese's relationship with the Catholic faithful required such an impermissible intrusion. As to the claims related to a failure to report under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-101a, neither of the cited allegations of the complaint referred to a failure to have reported abuse of the victim; therefore, they failed to state a cause of action based on the statute.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike was granted as to subparagraphs concerning claims of the Archdiocese's employment relations with the priest and subparagraphs concerning claims of the failure to report. The motion to strike was denied as to subparagraphs concerning allegations of general negligence.

State v. Lombardo Bros. Mason Contrs.


X01-UWY-CV-08-5010658S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT WATERBURY


51 Conn. Supp. 265; 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3192; 980 A.2d 983



February 23, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Corrected by State v. Lombardo Bros. Mason Contrs., Inc., 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 638 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 9, 2009)
Related proceeding at Travelers Cas. & Sur. Co. of Am. v. Neth. Ins. Co., 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1208 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 13, 2011)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Lombardo Bros. Mason Contrs., Inc., 307 Conn. 412, 54 A.3d 1005, 2012 Conn. LEXIS 443 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Memorandum of decision on defendants' motions to strike and for summary judgment.



DISPOSITION: Motions granted in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the State of Connecticut, filed an action against defendants, a construction manager, contractors, and design professionals, to recover for their alleged defective design and construction of a university law library. The manager, contractors, and professionals filed motions to strike counts of the complaint and motions for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The manager entered into a contract with the State to furnish construction management services in connection with the project. The State experienced problems with water intrusion into the library. The superior court held that the manager was entitled to rely upon and receive the benefits of the limitation on suit provision in the contract. The State, by the terms of the contract, agreed to the incorporation of a seven-year period of repose by reference to the period of repose applicable to professional design work under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-584a (1995). It waited more than twelve years after completion of the project, and nearly twice as long as the period of repose agreed to in the contract, to bring the action. The legislature intended the State to abide by the statutes of repose, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§52-577, 52-577a, 52-584 and 52-584a. The breach of contract claims were barred by the statute of limitations set out in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-576. The action was brought six years beyond the six-year limitation period. The State chose not to initiate its action until twelve years after it became aware of the water intrusion. That length of time was unduly burdensome and unexplained.


OUTCOME: The superior court granted the manager's motion to strike, the motions for summary judgment, and the motions to strike the counts of the complaint alleging breach of contract. The motions to strike three special defenses were denied.

FNM Manchester, LLC v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n of the town of Manchester


CV074029630S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 249



January 21, 2009, Decided 
January 21, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Planning and Zoning Commission voted to approve the application for a re-subdivision by defendant developer. Plaintiff abutting property owner commenced an action challenging the developer's decision to approve the application. The appeal challenged only two of the three lots.


OVERVIEW: The re-subdivision was to be into three lots from acreage of 33.10 acres all in a General Business zone. The chief claim of the abutting owner was that the maps or plans submitted by the developer did not show the subjects of the application to be in the proper zone. It was the abutting owner's claim that the property was not entirely in a General Business Zone but that it was partially residential. The court held there was substantial evidence that the subject property was all in a General Business zone including the actual town's Zoning Map which showed the zone line running along the property line. It was clear to the court that the developer included in its approval a modification to conform on the plan the conformity of the zone line and the property line. The court found that with the evidence, the Commission could reasonably have found that the developer had submitted substantial evidence that it had met the regulations, zoning and subdivision, that applied to the application. Moreover, the court found that the decision of the Commission in approving the application for a re-subdivision was reasonable and properly decided. It was not illegal or an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

State v. Edwards

1238 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. Hamilton


HHBCV4016668S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN, TAX SESSION AT NEW BRITAIN


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3362



December 29, 2008, Decided 
January 2, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother filed an administrative appeal from a decision of a Department of Children and Families (DCF) hearing officer that dismissed her efforts to appeal a denial of her request for services for her autistic son. The hearing officer concluded that dismissal was mandatory under regulations that were interpreted as prohibiting voluntary services if a neglect petition was pending.


OVERVIEW: Because the mother's application for services was denied, she was aggrieved for purposes of standing to appeal. The court found that Conn. Agencies Regs. § 17a-11-8(b) did not require denial of voluntary services without exception, but provided for waiver pursuant to Conn. Agencies Regs. § 17a-11-11. A waiver was not considered. The mother was not notified of the decision or of her right to a hearing under Conn. Agencies Regs. § 17-11-11(e) and (g). The agency's failure to follow its regulations prejudiced the mother's substantial rights--she and her son lost a chance to apply for help obtaining services without paying the heavy price of loss of guardianship and commitment. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-129 offered that chance. The hearing officer had express authority to review the denial of the application, including application of the restrictions. The DCF's action in Juvenile Court, at the time of the DCF hearing, sought the commitment of a daughter, not the son. Conn. Agencies Regs. § 17a-11-18(e) was designed to secure order, system and dispatch in proceedings. Inflexible application of the regulations erroneously precluded evaluation of the application's merits.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the appeal and remanded the case for further proceedings consistent with this decision.

 

1239 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Rodriguez v. Testa


CV065002252S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY AT WATERBURY


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3207



December 11, 2008, Decided 
December 11, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Rodriguez v. Testa, 296 Conn. 1, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 142 (2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the lessor of a vehicle involved in an auto accident, filed a motion for permission to file a motion for summary judgment in plaintiff's negligence action, which alleged vicarious liability against the lessor. Consideration was given to both the motion for permission to file and the motion for summary judgment itself. The vehicle was leased by defendant company and was driven by defendant, the owner of the company.


OVERVIEW: As there were no objections to the filing of the motion for summary judgment, the court granted the motion for permission to file. It then granted summary judgment on the merits. 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106(a) clearly preempted the ability of plaintiff to bring a claim under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-15a against the lessor for liability for the damage caused by the leased vehicle and or the lessee. Plaintiff's claim that § 30106 was unconstitutional failed as there was a clear, self-evident relation between interstate commerce and the leasing of motor vehicles. There was no genuine issue of material fact that plaintiff sought to impose vicariously liability upon the lessor pursuant to Conn. § 14-154a, and that plaintiff did not allege any negligence or criminal wrongdoing by the lessor. As a result, the lessor had met its burden to show that, as a matter of law, it was entitled to summary judgment because § 30106 barred the action against the lessor.


OUTCOME: The court granted the lessor's motion for permission to file its motion for summary judgment and then granted the motion for summary judgment.
