Gaines v. Warden, State Prison


CV044000099S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND AT ROCKVILLE


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3170



December 9, 2008, Decided 
December 9, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Gaines v. Comm'r of Corr., 125 Conn. App. 97, 7 A.3d 395, 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 521 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Gaines, 257 Conn. 695, 778 A.2d 919, 2001 Conn. LEXIS 345 (2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. After being appointed counsel, he filed a revised second amended petition, alleging that his convictions for violating Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-54a, -54b(8), and -48 were illegal because they were based on a probable cause hearing in which his public defender was unconstitutionally burdened by a conflict of interest and that trial counsel rendered ineffective assistance.


OVERVIEW: There was no actual conflict of interest that tainted a public defender's representation of the inmate. A witness represented by the public defender's office on unrelated charges may have been under investigation for the same crimes, but he was never arrested or charged. Co-counsel's trial representation was not ineffective because she made no trial decisions. The inmate did not show how he was prejudiced by trial counsel's failure to call an impeachment witness. However, trial counsel was ineffective for failing to investigate possible alibi witnesses. Contacting one of the two people the inmate had named would have led to the discovery of alibi evidence that would have served as a substantial counterweight to the evidence of guilt and was more likely than not to have put a reasonable doubt in the jurors' minds. The inmate met his burden of proving, by a preponderance of the evidence, that had counsel conducted an adequate investigation, he would have discovered the alibi witnesses. Failure to do so constituted deficient performance that prejudiced the inmate, cast appreciable doubt on the case, and undermined the court's confidence in the outcome of the criminal trial.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the conviction and remanded the case to the trial court for a new trial.

In re Justin F. Hailee L.


DOCKET NOS. N05-CP04-004754-D, N05-CP04-004755-D


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUVENILE MATTERS, CHILD PROTECTION SESSION, AT MIDDLETOWN


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3409



December 9, 2008, Decided


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by, in part, Appeal dismissed by, in part In re Justin F., 116 Conn. App. 83, 976 A.2d 707, 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 337 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: In re Justin F., 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 161 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 23, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commissioner of the Department of Children and Families (DCF) filed an emergency motion for modification of visitation by the parents of two children under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-10a. The DCF sought cessation of the parents' visitation with the first child and supervised visitation between them and the second child.


OVERVIEW: The court first stated that although parents had a constitutionally protected right to raise and care for their own children, this right was not free from intervention by the state when its continuing parens patriae interest in the well-being of children was deemed by law to supersede parental interests. The family here had not been intact for over four years, and during that period no judge had determined that there was a basis for immediate reunification and that the children should be returned to the parents. Having the DCF determine, pursuant to § 17a-10a, the requirements of the amount, type and location of visitation that was in the best interest of the children when the DCF had the benefit of its workers' observations, school reports, and the input of the children's therapist did not violate the parents' constitutional rights. Next, the court would continue the hearing with respect to whether visitation with the first child should be suspended. Because § 17a-10a applied to any visitation with the second child, the DCF was expected to act in accordance with its statutory duties, and there was no need or basis to continue the hearing as to the second child.


OUTCOME: The court continued the hearing as to the first child. It did not continue the hearing as to the second child. It held that § 17a-10a did not violate the parents' constitutional rights.

 

1242 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


S. New Eng. Tel. v. Comm'r, DOT


CV055000887


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN AT NEW HAVEN


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3142



December 4, 2008, Decided 
December 8, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff telephone company filed a complaint against defendant, the Connecticut Department of Transportation (DOT), alleging under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-556 that a DOT employe negligently operated a state owned motor vehicle that caused damage to the company's equipment. The DOT filed a motion to dismiss asserting lack of subject matter jurisdiction based on sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: The company's equipment was damaged as a result of the operation of a backhoe in an excavation. Section 52-556 waived sovereign immunity regarding injuries caused by the operation of a vehicle. However, to attain subject matter jurisdiction through § 52-556, the vehicle in question had to be a motor vehicle and it had to be utilized as a motor vehicle at the time of the accident. "Operation of a vehicle" required driving or moving the vehicle. In the instant case, while the backhoe could be operated as a vehicle, there was no evidence to suggest that the backhoe was in motion as a motor vehicle during the excavation. The evidence provided by both sides established that it would be virtually impossible to place the backhoe in motion when the hoe was in operation. The company's complaint itself stated that the damage to its equipment occurred during the course of excavation work. As it was impossible to operate the backhoe as a motor vehicle at the time the damage to the company's property occurred, the doctrine of sovereign immunity deprived the court of subject matter jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted.

Brooks v. Sweeney


CV065005224S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3122



November 28, 2008, Decided 
November 28, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Brooks v. Sweeney, 299 Conn. 196, 9 A.3d 347, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 459 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Brooks v. Sweeney, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1550 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 12, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner sued defendant health inspector for malicious prosecution, intentional infliction of emotional distress and negligent infliction of emotional distress; defendant supervisor for negligent supervision; and defendant towns for liability under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 7-465 and 52-557n. The owner alleged a federal claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 against the inspector and the supervisor. The defendants moved for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The health inspector, pursuant to his duty to enforce the health code, worked with the owner, giving her time to get the owner's septic system fixed. The owner eventually stated that she would not or could not comply with the orders of the health district. The inspector prepared an affidavit in support of an arrest warrant, a judge signed the warrant, and the owner was arrested for failure to comply with an order of the health district. However, the criminal charges were dismissed. The court found that (1) the owner failed to satisfy the elements of malicious prosecution because the prosecution commenced upon a finding of probable cause; (2) the enforcement of the law was not conduct beyond the bounds of decent society; (3) the emotional distress which the owner claimed to have suffered for her arrest was not outside the range of normal experience; (4) the inspector and his supervisor were entitled to qualified immunity on the federal claim; (5) any harm to which the owner was subjected was not imminent; (6) the towns did not have a duty to indemnify under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-465; and (7) liability on a negligence claim under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-557n did not apply to the towns.


OUTCOME: The motions for summary judgment were granted.

 

1244 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Lawrence v. Warden


CV064001264S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3018



November 26, 2008, Decided 
November 26, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Lawrence v. Comm'r of Corr., 125 Conn. App. 759, 9 A.3d 772, 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 583 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Lawrence, 67 Conn. App. 284, 786 A.2d 1227, 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 620 (2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was convicted of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm, carrying a pistol without a permit, and tampering with physical evidence. He petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus, alleging ineffective assistance of trial and appellate counsel. Respondent warden moved for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had been charged with murder. He alleged trial counsel was ineffective for requesting a jury charge on the lesser offense of first degree manslaughter with a firearm (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55a) without also requesting a charge of first degree manslaughter (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55), and that appellate counsel were ineffective for failure to challenge his conviction of manslaughter with a firearm. The court disagreed. The inmate was not prejudiced by counsel's failure to request a charge of first degree manslaughter because he was not entitled to that instruction. To convict him of murder, the State had to prove he intended to cause the death of the victim; that acting with such intent, he did cause the death of the victim; and that he used a firearm to cause the death of the victim. The jury necessarily found he committed all three of these elements before acquitting him of murder by reason of extreme emotional disturbance; therefore, it found that the murder was committed with a firearm. Thus, the jury could not have rationally convicted him of first degree manslaughter instead of first degree manslaughter with a firearm.


OUTCOME: The warden's motion for summary judgment was granted.

 

1245 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rodriguez


F02BCR080231300S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 2 AT BRIDGEPORT


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3136



November 26, 2008, Decided 
November 26, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. Rodriguez, 121 Conn. App. 250, 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 202 (2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In defendant's prosecution for the sale of illegal drugs and possession of controlled substances with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a school, defendant moved to suppress any and all evidence of drugs seized from him on the ground that his arrest was unsupported by probable cause under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 7 and 9.


OVERVIEW: A police officer and other members of a narcotics team were conducting surveillance and saw a vehicle stop in the center of the street. After observing what appeared to be a hand to hand drug transaction between the driver of the vehicle and defendant, who was in another car, the officer then directed another officer to approach defendant's car. The officer approached with his gun drawn and saw defendant holding money and a plastic bag containing smaller bags with a white powder. In denying defendant's motion to suppress, the court rejected defendant's contention that the officer's actions constituted an arrest. The stop was an investigative stop; thus, probable cause was not required. The officer's use of a weapon did not turn the investigative stop into a de facto arrest; instead, his approach of the vehicle with his weapon drawn was not unreasonable in light of the recognized connection between weapons and drug dealing. Reasonable suspicion supported the investigative stop. Given the similarities between the transaction observed by the officer on surveillance and the hundreds of drug transactions he had observed in the past, the officer's suspicions were more than a hunch.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion.

 

1246 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cronin


F02BMV0700412830


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 2 AT BRIDGEPORT


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2899



November 12, 2008, Decided 
November 12, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was arrested and charged with operating a motor vehicle under the influence of alcohol in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a. Defendant moved to suppress any and all evidence of his intoxication.


OVERVIEW: After receiving a broadcast for a hit and run, an officer stopped defendant's vehicle, which was near the accident scene and appeared to match the description of the vehicle involved. After examining defendant's vehicle for damage, the officer approached defendant to explain the purpose of the stop, thank him for his cooperation, and tell him he was free to leave. During that conversation, the officer noticed that defendant's speech was slurred, an odor of alcohol, and a glassy appearance to defendant's eyes. In support of his motion to suppress, defendant claimed that the officer lacked reasonable and articulable suspicion to initiate the stop because his vehicle was larger than that described by a witness and the time lapse between the accident and the stop. The court found that the officer was justified as no make of vehicle was provided in the broadcast and the location was not far from the accident. The court also found that the stop was not unduly prolonged when the officer approached defendant after examining the vehicle to explain. Finally, the court noted that defendant's slurred speech, the odor of alcohol, and his glassy eyes provided support for further investigation.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion to suppress was denied.

 

1247 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


B.J. Alan Co., CT, Inc. v. State


CV084038297


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2686



October 22, 2008, Decided 
October 22, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff vendor filed an application for a temporary injunction against defendants, the State of Connecticut, the Connecticut Department of Public Safety, and its Commissioner, after defendants' warrantless seizure of the vendor's fireworks ("fountains" as defined by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-356(3)).


OVERVIEW: After reviewing chemical composition data sheets, defendants seized fountains from two of vendor's locations, claiming they violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-357 because, inter alia, they contained more than five grams of chlorate or erchlorate salts. The court declined to review a ruling of a court of coordinate jurisdiction as to fountains seized from the vendor's second location. The vendor presented no persuasive evidence it would suffer irreparable harm to its reputation if an injunction was not granted. Money damages were an adequate remedy for any loss. The State's interest in protecting the public from illegal fireworks far outweighed the injuries the vendor complained of. The vendor was unlikely to succeed on the merits: (1) the court could not correct a legislative error in § 29-357, even assuming one existed; (2) federal regulations did not preempt the State's statutory scheme regulating fountains; (3) warrantless inspections of fireworks businesses under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-362 complied with New York v. Burger and thus did not violate the Fourth Amendment; and (4) the post-deprivation hearing mandated by § 29-362 provided due process to vendors.


OUTCOME: The court denied the vendor's application for a temporary injunction.

 

1248 of 1861 DOCUMENTS



Gonzaelez v. State


CV084036260S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2515



October 1, 2008, Decided 
October 1, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state representative filed a complaint to prevent defendant, the Connecticut State Elections Enforcement Commission (SEEC), from conducting a hearing on two complaints alleging that the representative violated elections laws governing absentee voting. The SEEC filed a motion to dismiss two counts of the complaint, under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 10-31(a), for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The SEEC received complaints from citizens alleging that the state representative violated laws governing absentee voting in connection with a primary election and later committed absentee ballot violations in connection with a general election. The SEEC considered the complaint at meetings and found reason to believe that the representative had violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-140b(e). The chairman of the SEEC, who was present at one of the meetings, was assigned to preside over hearings on the complaints. The representative sought an order preventing the SEEC from proceeding further on the complaints because of due process violations; a declaration that the SEEC's enabling statutes, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 9-7a and 9-7b, were facially unconstitutional; and money damages. The court found that the representative failed to articulate how she was to be harmed or prejudiced by awaiting the termination of the hearing process before raising her procedural due process claims. Therefore, the representative's allegations regarding violation of the representative's due process rights were not ripe for adjudication.


OUTCOME: The two counts were dismissed.


 

1249 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hartford Accident & Indem. Co. v. ACE Am. Reinsurance Co.


(X02)CV030178122S, (X02)CV030179514S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT WATERBURY


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2470



September 19, 2008, Decided 
September 19, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hartford Accident & Indem. Co. v. Ace Am. Reinsurance Co., 103 Conn. App. 319, 930 A.2d 701, 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 340 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurers sued defendant reinsurers, alleging breach of contract. plaintiff s filed a motion for the posting of pre-pleading security pursuant to the Connecticut Security Statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38a-27.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to their reinsurance contracts, defendants agreed to accept liability for certain losses incurred by plaintiffs to its own insureds, if those losses exceeded a certain threshold amount. Plaintiffs paid claims of its policyholders allegedly covered by the terms of the reinsurance contracts and billed defendants for those losses. Defendants claimed the losses were not covered under the contracts. This suit followed. The court held that as defendants were unauthorized to conduct insurance business in Connecticut, under § 38a-27, they had to deposit cash or securities in an amount to be fixed by the court sufficient to pay any judgment. Defendants argued that before ordering such a deposit, the court had to find, after an hearing in which they could raise their defenses, probable cause that plaintiffs would prevail. The court held § 38a-27 did not require such a probable cause determination. Defendants' due process rights were met by plaintiffs' submission of some proof that contracts existed, billings were made under them, and the bills remained unpaid, and by defendants' ability to cross-examine plaintiffs' witnesses and present evidence to counter plaintiffs' evidence.


OUTCOME: Plaintiffs' motion was granted. Defendants were ordered to post pre-pleading security, together with pre-judgment interest.

 

1250 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Kopylec v. Town of N. Branford


CV065007662S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN AT NEW HAVEN


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2291



September 10, 2008, Decided 
September 10, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Kopylec v. N. Branford Zoning Bd. of Appeals, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2296 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 10, 2008)
Affirmed by Kopylec v. Town of N. Branford, 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 390 (Conn. App. Ct., July 12, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant husband filed an application to discharge a lien in favor of plaintiff town that was placed on property quit claimed to him by his wife.


OVERVIEW: A lien was placed on the property as a result of a stipulated agreement between the wife and the town's zoning enforcement officer (ZEO) in a prior action after motions for contempt were filed pursuant to an alleged failure to remediate conditions on the property alleged to be a violation of the zoning regulations. Four days before the order was recorded, the husband wrote a letter to the ZEO stating that he would not allow the town to perform the necessary remediation. Approximately a month later, the wife quit claimed her interest in the land to the husband. The court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-351a did not appear to require notice to the husband since he was not a judgment debtor under the lien or the property's owner at the time it was put on the land records. The fact that a debt had not been incurred did not invalidate the lien since it was merely security for future costs for remediation. There was no claim of denial of all economically beneficial or productive use of the land. The physical invasion of the property required by remediation did not require compensation to the husband where it was claimed that zoning regulations or environmental laws had been violated.


OUTCOME: The application was denied.

 

1251 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


David v. Bureau


CV075001460S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WINDHAM AT PUTNAM


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2190



August 21, 2008, Decided 
August 25, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a student and her mother, filed a tort action against defendant teacher, asserted that the teacher touched the student in a wrongful manner during schools hours in the school. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The court granted the motion filed by the state to dismiss the claims for money damages against the teacher in his official capacity. Plaintiffs did not receive a waiver from the claims commissioner to sue the state; thus, the claims were barred by sovereign immunity. As for the claims against the teacher in his individual capacity, they could be reasonably construed to be directed against the teacher in his individual capacity and were not barred by sovereign immunity. To the extent that plaintiffs pleaded reckless or intentional conduct under the wanton, reckless, or malicious exception to statutory immunity under Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 4-165, those counts were properly before the court and beyond the scope of statutory sovereign immunity. The student failed to sufficiently plead that the teacher's conduct occurred outside the scope of employment. Contact with students was incidental to the duties of a teacher, and to the extent that such contact was merely negligent, as opposed to intentional contact made with improper and self-serving motives, it could not be the basis of a lawsuit against a state employee.


OUTCOME: The court granted the state's motion to dismiss all claims against the teacher in his official capacity. It denied the teacher's motion to dismiss the claims of intentional infliction of emotional distress and assault and battery against him in his individual capacity and granted his motion to dismiss the remaining counts.

 

1252 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Antalik v. Thomaston Bd. of Educ.


LLICV075001762S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD AT LITCHFIELD


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2082



August 13, 2008, Decided 
August 13, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Summary judgment denied by Antalik v. Thomaston Bd. of Educ., 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 603 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 12, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a student's parent, sued defendants, a board of education, a town, a superintendent, and a principal, alleging negligence and failure to comply with the state-mandated bullying policy. Defendants moved to strike the negligence counts on grounds of governmental immunity, to strike the breach of state policy counts on grounds of sovereign immunity, and to strike the counts against the town because no claim was asserted against it.


OVERVIEW: The parent alleged that the board, superintendent, and principal knew his child had been harassed at school; that they failed to protect her from a another child who kicked her during recess; that their conduct was negligent; and that they failed to comply with state bullying policy. The court held that as no cause of action had been alleged against the town, the claims against it had to be stricken. The complaint failed to allege facts showing that the harm was imminent and that it should have been apparent to defendants that their conduct likely subjected the student to the alleged harm. The harm could have potentially occurred at any time during the school day. Thus, defendants were entitled to qualified immunity on the negligence claim. The parent alleged defendants failed to implement and follow a bullying policy adopted under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-222d, and that soveriegn immunity did not apply because the board acted on behalf of the town, not the state. The court held board and its employees were acting pursuant to a state-mandated activity set forth in § 10-222d; thus, they were protected by the doctrine of sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: Defendants' motion to strike was granted in its entirety.

 

1253 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Vazquez v. Comm'r of Corr.


CV0447000236


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT SOMERS


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1971



August 11, 2008, Decided 
August 11, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Vazquez v. Comm'r of Corr., 123 Conn. App. 424, 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 371 (2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was convicted of assault and was sentenced to 16 years of confinement, suspended after the service of 8 years, and 5 years of probation. He filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus alleging that he was deprived the effective assistance of counsel when he rejected a pretrial settlement offer extended by the State of 10 years of confinement, suspended after the service of 4 years, and 5 years of probation.


OVERVIEW: The inmate became disenchanted with his first attorney because he recommended an acceptance of a pretrial agreement; the first attorney was replaced. The inmate rejected the plea offer and was convicted by a jury at trial. The trial was not constitutionally suspect or deficient. The second attorney was professional in his trial representation of the inmate when the case was presented to the jury. There were no constitutional infirmities in the actual trial and sentence of the inmate. The inmate argued that his attorneys were ineffective because they did not convince him to accept the State's offer of a pretrial agreement. Rejections of plea bargains could not be reversed even if the rejection resulted from an attorney's incorrect advice. While the inmate received a sentence almost exactly double to that which he could have had if he had elected to accept the pretrial offer, if his claim of self-defense had been accepted, he would have been acquitted.


OUTCOME: The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

Voris v. Middlesex Mut. Assur. Co.


CV074008029S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DANBURY AT DANBURY


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2048



August 7, 2008, Decided 
August 7, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Voris v. Middlesex Mut. Assur. Co., 297 Conn. 589, 999 A.2d 741, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 269 (2010)
Related proceeding at Voris v. Molinaro, 2011 Conn. LEXIS 461 (Conn., Nov. 22, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insureds sued defendants, an insurer and the insurer's agent, claiming breach of contract. The insureds sought a judgment declaring that defendants had a contractual obligation to provide underinsured motorist coverage under an automobile insurance policy the insurer issued, and claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38a-366(g)(1) and a provision in their policy were unconstitutional. Defendants moved for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The insureds sustained injuries in an automobile accident on May 10, 2004, and they contacted their insurer shortly after the accident and sued the driver of the other car almost two years later. Discovery disclosed that the driver of the other car had purchased an automobile insurance policy that provided bodily injury liability coverage in the amount of $ 50,000. After the insureds learned that the other driver had only $ 50,000 in coverage, they notified their insurer that they had a potential claim for underinsured motorist benefits under their automobile insurance policy. Their insurer informed the insureds that any claim they filed would be disapproved because it would be filed more than three years after the date the accident occurred. The insureds sued their insurer and the company's agent, claiming that the provision in their policy that required them to file a claim within three years of the date of the accident and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38a-366(g)(1), the statute upon which that provision was based, were unconstitutional. The court held that § 38a-366(g)(1) was not unconstitutional, and it agreed that any claim the insureds might file was time-barred under their policy.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment.

 

1255 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Dibble Edge Partners, LLC v. Town of Wallingford


CV064006084S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN AT MERIDEN


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2054



August 6, 2008, Decided 
August 6, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner (PO) filed an action against defendants, a town, its planning and zoning commission, and an abutting land owner (ALO), alleging inverse condemnation (IC), damages pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and conspiracy. The matter arose when the town granted the ALO's application to subdivide its property without granting the PO's right-of-way (ROW) request.


OVERVIEW: The PO's ROW request, in order to gain access to an existing town road from his landlocked parcel, was denied when the subdivision application was granted. Thereafter, the town purchased a strip of the ALO's land that abutted the PO's property. Accordingly, the PO brought suit. The trial court held that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the claims under § 1983 and for conspiracy, as they were not ripe for adjudication. The claim under § 1983 did not arise until there was an adverse determination in the IC claim, and the conspiracy claim was based on the allegedly tortious conduct under the § 1983 claim. The court held that the ROW requirement in Wallingford, Conn., Subdivision Regs. VI.A.4 did not apply to a subdivision plan that relied exclusively upon an existing town road on land that was not within the proposed subdivision. However, issues of fact existed as to whether the addition of a cul-de-sac to a road was an on-site or off-site improvement, whether the PO's land constituted "adjoining property susceptible to being subdivided" that constituted a triggering event for the ROW, and whether the PO was deprived of all economically beneficial use of its property.


OUTCOME: The court granted the town's motion to dismiss the claims under § 1983 and alleging a conspiracy. Both parties' motions for summary judgment were denied on the inverse condemnation claim.

 

1256 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Scott v. Lantz


CV084028950S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN AT NEW HAVEN


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1933



July 30, 2008, Decided 
July 30, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmates sought declaratory relief that their prison living conditions due to overcrowding were unconstitutional and injunctive relief that would result in their reclassification and reassignment to other facilities. After filing their complaint for such relief, the inmates were moved to other locations. Defendants, a commissioner, warden, and deputy warden moved to dismiss the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The inmates filed a complaint against the commissioner, as well as the warden and deputy warden of the correctional center where they were confined, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief regarding their confinement conditions. They alleged that their confinement, in a small television room with an improperly ventilated toilet area, with several other inmates, amounted to cruel and unusual punishment. They specifically contended that the conditions violated the Eighth and Fourteenth Amendments, as well as Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 10 and 20. The commissioner, warden, and deputy warden sought dismissal because service of process was not made on them, but, rather, the State. They also alleged that the case was moot because the inmates had been moved to other facilities. The trial court agreed with the commissioner, warden, and deputy warden that proper service had not been made on them. It also found that the only possible exception to mootness was the "capable of repetition, yet evading review" exception. However, the trial court found that exception did not apply because the inmates could not show that they likely would be subjected to the same conditions in the future.


OUTCOME: The trial court granted the motion to dismiss.

 

1257 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Martocchio v. Savoir


TTDFA064006261


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND AT ROCKVILLE


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1894



July 28, 2008, Decided 
July 28, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Martocchio v. Savoir, 130 Conn. App. 626, 23 A.3d 1282, 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 424 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Martocchio v. Savoir, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 776 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 27, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A father was awarded sole custody of his child. The court ordered, inter alia, that the maternal grandparents have limited visitation. The mother, then incarcerated, was also given limited access. There were a large number of motions presented by the parties including the grandparents' motion to modify custody, the mother's motion to open and modify judgment, and the father's motion to allocate GAL fees.


OVERVIEW: The maternal grandparents had a relationship with the child akin to that of parents. The mother suffered from alcohol and substance abuse issues and had no meaningful relationship with the child. The child, 4 1/2 years of age, was severely autistic and nonverbal. The child was receiving extraordinary educational services. The father had immersed himself in the study of autism and the proper treatment and care of his son. The grandparents believed that the child's doctor's methods were damaging to the child. The court found that belief to be unfounded. The court found that the grandparents and mother were able and willing to honor the orders of the court that the father, as sole custodial parent, was to have final decision-making on all aspects of the child's care and upbringing. The father was clearly the more informed and fit parent. The GAL recommended that the father remain as the sole custodial parent with final decision-making on all aspects of the child's life but that the grandparent's access of every other weekend be continued so long as they abided by the father's medical decisions and that the mother's access occur contemporaneously with that of the grandparents.


OUTCOME: The father was to have sole custody of the child. The maternal grandparents were to enjoy visitation every other weekend. The mother could visit during the grandparent's visitation time or at a professional visitation facility if she so chose. Neither the maternal grandparents nor the mother was to interfere with the father's choice of physician or with the father's choice of medication or educational options.

Morgan v. Hartford Hosp.


X03CV075009731S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT HARTFORD


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1827



July 22, 2008, Decided 
July 22, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, Dismissed by, in part Morgan v. Hartford Hosp., 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1324 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 21, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff co-administrators filed a motion to strike the special defense asserted by defendant hospital in their medical malpractice case; the co-administrators claimed that the special defense was legally insufficient because it did not destroy their cause of action.


OVERVIEW: The hospital's special defense stated that the co-administrators' claims were time barred by application of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-555, which afforded it a vested property right to repose. The court found that the factual allegations of the co-administrators' amended complaint showed that they timely filed their medical malpractice action against the hospital within the time frame allowed by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-555 as extended by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-190a(b). The 90-day extension provided in § 52-190a(b) was not unconstitutional. Accordingly, the defendant's single-sentence conclusory special defense was legally insufficient.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike the special defense was granted.

 

1259 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Wellswood Columbia, LLC v. Town of Hebron


TTDCV054003914S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND AT ROCKVILLE


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1811



July 21, 2008, Decided 
July 21, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Wellswood Columbia, LLC v. Town of Hebron, 295 Conn. 802, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 116 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Wellswood Columbia, LLC v. Town of Hebron, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3608 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 21, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a limited liability company and its managing member, filed an action against defendants, a town, the board of selectmen of the town, and the town manager, seeking a permanent injunction preventing them from closing or barricading a road in the town.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs wanted to develop a retirement community on land that abutted the town. The road provided the only access to the property. The superior court held that the town properly exercised its police power in closing the road. The town showed that it had legitimate concerns that plaintiffs' proposed development would have serious negative impacts on the health, safety, and welfare of its citizens. The town sufficiently established that the road would not be an ideal sole access road. Plaintiffs failed to offer any substantial evidence that alternative means of access to its community through an adjoining town would not be possible. They did not demonstrate that they were without an adequate remedy at law. Plaintiffs could have sought damages based on a taking theory of recovery. Because they did not seek money damages, and they failed to show that they suffered a total and permanent loss of a right of access, they were not entitled to compensatory damages under a taking theory. Plaintiffs did not prove that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-55 applied and that they were entitled to a private right-of-way because they failed to show that the town discontinued or abandoned the road.


OUTCOME: The superior court denied plaintiffs' application for a permanent injunction.

 

1260 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Lang v. State


HHBCV074014311


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1829



July 18, 2008, Decided 
July 18, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff teacher appealed a decision of a hearing officer of the Connecticut Department of Children and Families (DCF), which accepted DCF's decision to place the teacher on the Conn. Gen. Stat. §17a-101k(a) central registry after the teacher pled guilty to a Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(1) violation.


OVERVIEW: The reviewing court held that the hearing officer erroneously relied upon DCF policy § 22-12-4 to deny the teacher a hearing on DCF's substantiation of sexual abuse. Section 22-12-4 was based on the doctrine of collateral estoppel. The transcript of the plea hearing did not justify concluding that applying collateral estoppel, or the DCF equivalent, § 22-12-4, was warranted. The teacher admitted guilt to § 53-21(a)(1) only. Section 53-21(a)(1) did not reference illegal sexual activity. The prosecutor stated the charge was based on the victim spending the night with the teacher, and on a number of occasions sleeping with the teacher in his bed. The teacher apologized for mistakes in judgment, endangering the child in question, and for the ordeal the child and family had been subjected to. The admission at the criminal plea hearing could not serve as a justification for denying the teacher a substantiation hearing on DCF's sexual abuse allegations. The matter was not "actually litigated" in criminal court.


OUTCOME: The appeal was sustained. The matter was remanded to DCF for a new full hearing on the substantiation of sexual abuse against the teacher.

 

1261 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Long


CR14308773


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1690



July 7, 2008, Decided 
July 7, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. Long, 301 Conn. 216, 2011 Conn. LEXIS 227 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Long, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3335 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 14, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Connecticut filed a petition for an order of continued commitment of the acquittee under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593(c). The acquittee filed a motion to dismiss. The State's objection to the motion was overruled without prejudice. The evidence concerning both the petition and the motion was heard in a single consolidated proceeding.


OVERVIEW: After a criminal trial to the court, the defendant was found not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-13(a). Thereafter, the acquittee was committed for the maximum period to which he could have been sentenced had he been convicted of the underlying offense. The State of Connecticut successfully petitioned for recommitment of the acquittee on four occasions. The acquittee contended that once he reached his maximum term of recommitment, the State's petition for recommitment pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593(c) was rendered unconstitutional in both procedure and effect. The court, given the expert testimony as to the acquittee's existing mental state, found by clear and convincing evidence that the acquittee was then mentally ill and dangerous to others. Furthermore, § 17a-593(c) was not unconstitutional as applied to the acquittee. Section 17a-593(c) facially applied only to an acquittee who remained a person with psychiatric disabilities, and the acquittee was mentally ill and dangerous. Finally, it was appropriate for the State to discriminate among psychiatrically disabled individuals on the basis of a proven criminal act.


OUTCOME: The acquittee's motion to dismiss was denied. The petition by the State of Connecticut for an order of continued commitment was granted, and the commitment of the acquittee was continued for a period of three years.

 

1262 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Kobyluck Bros., LLC v. Town of Salem Zoning Bd. of Appeals


CV064104122


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON AT NORWICH


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1709



July 3, 2008, Decided 
July 7, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff quarry company claimed that a cease and desist order was improperly issued because the quarry was not violating the Regulations. The quarry also claimed, inter alia, that the limitations on its operations imposed by the cease and desist order deprived it of any reasonable means of obtaining income from its property and was, in effect, a taking of its property under Conn. Const. art. I, §11.


OVERVIEW: The quarry claimed that the limitations imposed by the cease and desist order would make the operation of the quarry economically unviable. However, the court noted that the quarry did not claim that it could not continue to operate with one rock cutter or carry on other operations on its property. Accordingly, there was no unconstitutional taking of the quarry's property. The record was replete with evidence offered by neighbors as to the detrimental effect of the quarry operations on the neighborhood. There was no basis for the claim that the cease and desist order would adversely impact the neighborhood. There was no basis for the claim that the use of more than one rock crusher in the quarry would reduce the threat to public safety. To the contrary, testimony from neighbors attested to the substantial adverse effect the use of an additional rock crusher would have on the quality of life of the neighbors. There were no egregious facts involving the chairman's statement to a neighbor and there was no basis for disqualifying him. Moreover, the quarry did not request that the chairman disqualify himself at the hearing. Thus, it could not subsequently raise an objection.


OUTCOME: The plaintiffs' appeal was dismissed.

 

1263 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Rell


CV085016589S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1751



July 1, 2008, Decided 
July 1, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Johnson v. Rell, 119 Conn. App. 730, 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 75 (2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmates filed an action against defendant, the governor, the Department of Correction Commissioner, and the warden of a correctional institute, alleging that the conditions of the institute subjected them to cruel and unusual punishment in violation of the Eighth Amendment of the United States Constitution and constituted a deprivation of their constitutional rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The superior court held that it was without personal jurisdiction to hear the complaint as to ten of the inmates because they failed to sign the complaint. Only one of the inmates provided a valid signature on the complaint. Because the ten inmate's forged signatures were invalid, those inmates failed to comply with the requirements placed upon pro se litigants under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 8-1, leaving the superior court without personal jurisdiction over defendants as to them. Because the claims against defendants in their official capacities were, in effect, claims against the State, the doctrine of sovereign immunity was implicated, and the superior court was without subject matter jurisdiction to hear those claims. The complaint failed to allege that defendants acted in excess of their statutory authority or pursuant to an unconstitutional statute. The superior court did not have subject matter jurisdiction to hear the claims brought against defendants in their individual capacities. The inmate's allegations were not clear constitutional violations that warranted piercing the protective veil that qualified federal immunity provided to government officials.


OUTCOME: The superior court granted the motion to dismiss.

 

1264 of 1861 DOCUMENTS



Unitrin Preferred Ins. Co. v. Chapman


TTDCV085002551S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND AT ROCKVILLE


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1523



June 12, 2008, Decided 
June 12, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurance filed a two-count, revised complaint asserting subrogation claims arising from a motor vehicle accident. The first count alleged that defendant lessee's negligence in operating the vehicle caused the crash. The second count alleged defendant lessor's vicarious liability for the lessee's alleged negligence. The lessor filed a motion to strike count two of the revised complaint.


OVERVIEW: The lessee allegedly was involved in a motor vehicle accident while operating a vehicle he had leased from the lessor. The insurance company filed a subrogation complaint alleging that the lessee negligently operated the vehicle. Count two alleged that the lessee's negligence was imputed to the lessor. The lessor sought to strike count two. It explained that the United States Congress had enacted 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106, known as the Graves Amendment, which stated that motor vehicle owners in the vehicle rental business bore no vicarious responsibility for damages arising from rental vehicle use by lessees. The trial court found it had to decide whether a state court could find a federal law unconstitutional and, if so, whether the United States Congress exceeded its authority in enacting 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106. It found a state court had the power to find a federal law unconstitutional when that question properly arose in a state court. It then held, however, that the United States Congress under United States Constitution's Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, reasonably could determine that a nonnegligent lessor was not responsible for their lessees' motor vehicle accidents.


OUTCOME: The trial court granted the motion to strike count two of the insurance company's revised complaint alleging the lessor's vicarious liability for the lessee's alleged negligence.


 

1265 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Nipmuc Props., LLC v. City of Meriden


CV074008719S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN AT MERIDEN


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1546



June 12, 2008, Decided 
June 12, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a purported lessee and an LLC, filed an action to quiet title under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 47-31 and for declaratory relief under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-29 against defendants, a city and the State of Connecticut Siting Council. Defendants filed motions to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The lessee sold 845 acres to the LLC, which entered into a contract with a utility to sell it the land, except for a 52-acre parcel. The utility was obliged to quitclaim that parcel to the LLC and lease it to the LLC or its nominee (the lessee). The Council issued a certificate allowing the utility to build a power plant on the 845 acres. The utility assigned its rights under its contract with the LLC to an assignee, which bought the 845 acres, subject to the lease. The Council brought an enforcement action to compel the assignee to transfer 357 acres to the city; this land contained the 52-acre parcel. These parties settled; they stipulated that the 357 acres would be transferred and that the lease would be listed as an encumbrance on the deed to the city. The lessee alleged the city prevented it from taking possession of the land. The court held that as plaintiffs failed to timely appeal the Council's actions under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-183(a), their challenge to the Council's order to transfer land to the city was barred. But as the Council did not make a ruling on the lease's validity, the city's motion to dismiss for failure to exhaust administrative remedies failed.


OUTCOME: The Council's motion to dismiss was granted but the city's motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1266 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Vespera Invs., Inc. v. New Milford Zoning Comm'n


LLICV074006348S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD AT LITCHFIELD


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1414



June 10, 2008, Decided 
June 10, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners challenged a decision of defendant zoning commission, which denied their applications to develop certain land as an active adult community. The commission filed a motion to strike the paragraph of the complaint that alleged an unlawful taking of property in violation of Conn. Const. art. I, § 11 and in violation of the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: In their complaint, the owners alleged that in denying their application to improve a road, the commission's decision effected a taking of their property without compensation in violation of Conn. Const. art. I, § 11 and the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution. The commission argued that that paragraph of the complaint constituted the entirety of the owners' taking claim and did not allege sufficient facts to constitute a taking claim. It contended that the taking claim encompassed allegations contained in preceding paragraphs of the complaint, including allegations that the commission acted illegally, arbitrarily, and in abuse of its discretion and that it interfered with the owners' property rights by precluding improvements to the road, which negatively impacted the value of the property. The superior court held that the disputed paragraph constituted the entirety of the owners' taking claim. The owners' bare allegation that the commission effected a taking of their property by denying them the right to improve the road was not legally sufficient to state a claim for an unconstitutional taking.


OUTCOME: The superior court granted the motion to strike.

Dunham v. New Milford Zoning Comm'n

SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD AT LITCHFIELD

The commission argued that the owner failed to allege sufficient facts to constitute a taking claim and that the taking claim encompassed allegations contained in preceding paragraphs of the complaint. The superior court found that the paragraph in dispute constituted the entirety of the owner's taking claim. It held that the owner's bare allegation that the commission effected a taking of the property by denying him the right to improve the road was not legally sufficient to state a claim for an unconstitutional taking.

1268 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Gartland v. Dep't of Children & Families


CV075003344S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DANBURY AT DANBURY


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1394



June 4, 2008, Decided 
June 4, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff foster parent sued defendants, a child services agency and several of its employees, seeking monetary damages for the intentional infliction of emotional distress and willful, wanton, and reckless misconduct. The action stemmed from the removal of foster children to whom the foster parents were related. The agency moved to dismiss the action on the ground that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The agency argued that the complaint against it was barred by sovereign immunity. The foster parents conceded that they had not received permission to sue the State. Case law recognized two limited exceptions to the State's sovereign immunity, namely, when: (1) the legislature statutorily waived immunity; and (2) in an action for declaratory or injunctive relief, the state officers against whom such relief was sought acted in excess of statutory authority or pursuant to an unconstitutional statute. Because there was no evidence that the legislature had statutorily waived the State's immunity, the first exception to the sovereign immunity doctrine was inapplicable. Additionally, since the foster parents sought monetary damages, the second exception was also inapplicable. Thus, neither exception to the sovereign immunity rule having been met, the doctrine of sovereign immunity protected the agency from having to litigate the claim.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted. The individually named agency employees were not addressed by the court's order.

Ventres v. Goodspeed Airport, LLC


X07CV01402085S, X07CV014025127S, X07CV075012545S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT HARTFORD


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1363



May 27, 2008, Decided 
May 27, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Ventres v. Goodspeed Airport, LLC, 301 Conn. 194, 2011 Conn. LEXIS 226 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Ventres v. Goodspeed Airport, LLC, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 936 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 29, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a town inland wetlands and watercourses commission, its members, and other related parties, filed motions for summary judgment in a civil rights action, a land trust action, and on counterclaims in an enforcement action, which were all interrelated and arose as a result of the cutting of trees by defendants, an airport, its member, and a contractor, and issuance of a cease and desist order under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-44.


OVERVIEW: Defendants cut many trees from property belonging to the town's land trust. An action was filed under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-44(a), and as a result, numerous other actions were filed by a variety of parties. Judgment was entered against defendants for violating a regulation of the commission and Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 22a-16 and 22a-42a(c)(1). Plaintiffs thereupon sought summary judgment in numerous other actions that were pending. The court initially determined that civil rights counterclaims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, alleging violations of the procedural and substantive due process clauses, were barred by res judicata from further review, as they had been previously disposed of in a summary judgment ruling in a prior, related federal action. As the cease and desist order under § 22a-44(a) was effectively terminated by the issuance of injunctive relief under § 22a-44(b), issues regarding a hearing thereon and requests for extraordinary remedies were deemed moot. As there was no taking of the property, an inverse condemnation claim under Conn. Const. art. I, § 11 and U.S. Const. amend. V failed. Multiple tort claims asserted in the actions all failed for assorted reasons.


OUTCOME: The court granted summary judgment to plaintiffs and entered judgment in their favor.

 

1270 of 1861 DOCUMENTS



Murrelle v. Sloane


CV075008945


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1324



May 19, 2008, Decided 
May 19, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff filed a personal injury action against defendants, a car rental company and its employee. The company filed a motion to strike the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The company sought to strike the complaint on the ground that 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106, the Graves Amendment, barred any personal injury or property damage action against rental car companies for whom the claim of negligence was imputed solely by virtue of their status as owner of a vehicle. Plaintiff argued that the Graves Amendment was an unconstitutional exercise of power under the commerce clause. The court found no facts in support of the company's negligence above and beyond the negligence alleged against the driver of the vehicle, an employee of the company. The court could plainly infer from the allegations in the complaint and the business name of the company that it was engaged in the trade or business of renting or leasing motor vehicles, and plaintiff did not attempt to argue otherwise. In the absence of any allegation that the company either was itself negligent or engaged in criminal wrongdoing, the court granted the company's motion to strike.


OUTCOME: The company's motion to strike was granted.


 

1271 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Neighborhood Builders, Inc. v. Town of Madison


X01CV044005268S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT WATERBURY


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1247



May 14, 2008, Decided 
May 14, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Neighborhood Builders, Inc. v. Town of Madison, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2711 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 12, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, limited liability companies, small businesses, and corporations, filed an action against defendant town, alleging violations of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 7-130i, 7-148, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUTPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110a et seq. The town filed a motion to dismiss the complaint for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs alleged that the revenues the town derived from building permit fees were significantly in excess of the cost relating to offering and regulating building activity and that the town unlawfully used the fees to fund its general operations, social programs, and other initiatives. The superior court held that plaintiffs did not have standing to pursue their § 7-130i claim. There was no private cause of action under § 7-130i, which did not relate in any way to building permit fees. Plaintiffs did not provide the superior court with a basis to conclude that the town's alleged violation of § 7-148(c)(2)(B) provided them with a private cause of action for money damages. They gave no support for their contention that Conn. Const. art. 10, §§ 1 and 2 provided for a private cause of action for money damages. Plaintiffs did not have a cause of action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 because the imposition of a fee did not give rise to a takings claim. There was no appellate or supreme court case that provided municipalities with blanket immunity against CUTPA claims. Therefore, on the face of CUPTA, plaintiffs had no issue with subject matter jurisdiction or with standing.


OUTCOME: The superior court granted the town's motion to dismiss in part but found that plaintiffs' CUTPA claim survived the motion.
