Avelino v. Williams


CV075010476


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1191



May 8, 2008, Decided 
May 8, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff driver filed a complaint against defendants, a driver, a vehicle owner, and an insurer, alleging, inter alia, a claim for negligence against the river and vicarious liability against the owner pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a. The owner filed a motion to strike the vicarious liability claim.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was operating a van when defendant driver, who was operating a vehicle owned by a car rental agency, lost control of her vehicle and stuck the van. In support of its motion to strike, the owner alleged that 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106, the Graves Amendment, prevented the imposition of vicarious liability on the vehicles of a commercial car lessor. The court first concluded that whether the owner filed a "speaking motion" as alleged by plaintiff was immaterial because the complaint alleged that the owner had a car rental business and that defendant driver had rented the vehicle she was driving at the time of the accident. Plaintiff also argued that the Graves Amendment was an unconstitutional exercise of power under the commerce clause. The court disagreed, noting that the authority relied on by plaintiff was neither binding on the court nor persuasive authority. The court did agree with the owner that the action was barred by federal law, as § 14-154a was abrogated by the Graves Amendment, as provided for in § 30106.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike was granted.

 

1273 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Booker v. Jarjura


CV074014260S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY AT WATERBURY


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1115



May 2, 2008, Decided 
May 2, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Booker v. Jarjura, 120 Conn. App. 1, 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 105 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Booker v. Jarjura, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1083 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 30, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff minority leader of a town's board of aldermen filed an action for quo warranto against a member of the Waterbury Inland Wetlands and Watercourses Commission (WIWWC member), an action for quo warranto against a member of the town's zoning commission (zoning commission member), and an action for mandamus against certain other members of the zoning commission (commission).


OVERVIEW: The trial court rejected the WIWWC member's claims that the 2002 charter revision commission's intent in inserting the word "party" into Waterbury, Conn., Charter ch. 4, § 4-2(b)(1) was to require the minority leader to recommend members of his or her own party, and that § 4-2(b)(1) applied to boards, but not commissions, as they could have been raised in a prior quo warranto action. The WIWWC member was ineligible to serve as he was not on the list of minority members proposed by the minority leader. The WIWWC member was ousted. Section 4-2(b)(2) did not require the board of aldermen or boards or commissions to consult the minority leader's list when making minority appointments. The last sentence of § 4-2(b)(2) referred to other charter provisions that clearly pertained to the zoning commission, and did not require that the boards or commissions consult the minority leader's list when making minority appointments to boards or commissions. Thus, the zoning commission member rightfully occupied her position on the zoning commission, even though she was not on the minority leader's list. The petition for a writ of mandamus as to the commission was denied.


OUTCOME: The application for a writ of quo warranto was granted as to the WIWWC member and he was ousted from his position. The application for a writ of quo warranto was denied as to the zoning commission member, and the petition for a writ of mandamus as to the zoning commission was denied.

 

1274 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Batey v. Comm'r, Dep't of Social Servs.


HHDCV074033927S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1127



May 2, 2008, Decided 
May 2, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff elderly client filed suit against defendant commissioner of the department of social services seeking declaratory judgments, injunctive relief, and attorneys fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 for alleged violations of the Medicaid Act, the Americans with Disabilities Act, the Rehabilitation Act, the Due Process Clause, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and the Connecticut Home Care Program for Elders (CHCPE), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17b-342 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner moved to dismiss. The trial court noted that the commissioner argued that he only had to provide funding for CHCPE benefits, and that the provider made an independent decision not to service the client. The case was not moot as it could be determined that the commissioner's obligations went beyond funding. The matter was ripe for adjudication. Whether the client was entitled to a private right of action was to be determined on a motion to strike. The client was classically aggrieved as she was in need of home health care. The deprivation of benefits gave the client a specific, personal, and legal interest. The client had standing to bring the action, regardless of whether the statutes allowed for a private right of action. The requests for declaratory and injunctive relief demanded a clarification of the commissioner's responsibilities. The request for attorneys fees was not barred as monetary damages under Eleventh Amendment immunity. The commissioner was a "person" under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The request for injunctive relief to compel the commissioner to provide benefits for the client did not implicate the doctrine of sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1275 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Halligan v. Town of Wallingford


CV075012748S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN AT NEW HAVEN


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 936



April 22, 2008, Decided 
April 22, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant rental car franchisee filed a motion for summary judgment in a negligence suit filed by plaintiff driver against the franchisee and defendants, an undercover police officer and a town, arising out of a motor vehicle accident.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that there was a rational basis for Congress to conclude that state statutes imposing liability on car rental agencies for the actions of lessees in the absence of negligence or wrongdoing would affect interstate commerce and have an effect on such commerce for purposes of the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8. The franchisee leased vehicles that could be used in interstate commerce and thus its business was inextricably bound up with that commerce. The rental agreement provided that permission was granted to operate the vehicle only in the state of rental and certain specified states and stated that operation in any other state or county would affect the lessee's liability and rights under the agreement. It was contemplated that the cars might be operated in interstate commerce. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154(a), by imposing added operational costs on car rental companies not imposed on other interstate travel providers, had an effect on interstate commerce that Congress could preempt. 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106(a) had a commercial nexus to the operation of car rental companies and their consumers in interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment motion was granted.

 

1276 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Jolley v. Bragdon


CV075012256


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1058



April 22, 2008, Decided 
April 22, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured inmate wished to raise a products liability action against certain pharmaceutical companies that provided a non-steroidal anti-inflammatory drugs (NSAIDS). He attempted to obtain information through a Freedom of Information Act (FOIA) request directed to the Correctional Managed Health Care (CMHC). He claimed that defendants, university employees, failed to comply with the request. The university employees moved to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The CMHC provided the inmate with medial care including treatment with the NSAIDS. The inmate was diagnosed with gastroesophageal reflux and scarring of the duodenal bulb, allegedly due to his consumption of NSAIDS and a failure to provide guides, labeling and/or package inserts. The court held the inmate failed to exhaust his administrative remedies because he did not follow the appellate procedures provided for in the FOIA. The employees responded that they checked with CMHC's drug wholesalers and found that it would be virtually impossible to identify specific data to support the FOIA request. In addition, there were a number of years where the pharmaceutical care of the inmates had been privatized and few records were available to the specifics. The inmate failed to comply with the procedural requirements of the FOIA. He failed to serve the Freedom of Information Commission or the Attorney General, and directed his suit solely at the university employees. Therefore, the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction because he failed to exhaust his administrative remedies. He neither alleged nor argued that the legislature statutorily waived the state's sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted.

 

1277 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Ackley v. St. Vincent's Med. Ctr.


CV010380851S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD AT BRIDGEPORT


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 828



April 7, 2008, Decided 
April 7, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff estate administrator sued defendant medical center. The jury rendered a verdict in favor of the administrator. The medical center's motion to set aside the verdict was denied. The administrator filed a motion for interest pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a. The medical center filed an objection to the motion for interest.


OVERVIEW: The medical center claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a was unconstitutional in that the statute (1) violated the fundamental rights of access to the courts and of trial by jury under Conn. Const. art. I, X, and XIX; (2) violated the medical center's right to due process under the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution; and (3) had no rational relationship to any legitimate governmental interest. The court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a was not unconstitutional because (1) the purpose of the statute was to conserve judicial resources by promoting settlements; (2) the medical center's right to access the courts and to exercise its right to a jury trial were not violated; (3) the statute did not violate the right to due process under the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution; and (4) the statute was rationally related to the legitimate governmental interests of promoting compromise and the conservation of judicial resources.


OUTCOME: The medical center's objection to the motion for interest was overruled and interest was awarded to the date the motion to set aside the verdict was denied and judgment was entered.

 

1278 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Delude v. Young


TTDCV075001903S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND AT ROCKVILLE


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 805



April 2, 2008, Decided 
April 2, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A trial court (Connecticut) treated a motion to strike filed by defendants, including a doctor (doctor), as a motion to dismiss, ordered a medical malpractice case dismissed, and sustained an objection to a request for leave to amend a complaint. Plaintiff patient's motion to reargue was granted to allow the patient to raise the issue of whether Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-190a, if so applied, was constitutional under Conn. Const. art. I, § 10.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the written opinion letter was insufficient, and that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the case. Medical negligence existed as a cause of action at common law prior to 1818 and thus became incorporated into the Connecticut Constitution by the adoption of Conn. Const. art. I, § 10. There was no alternative remedy. However, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-190a did not abolish the ability to bring a medical negligence case, but merely required the patient to document the fact that there was evidence to support such a claim before bringing suit. There was nothing insurmountable about this requirement. Second, it was certainly reasonable. Section 52-190a was enacted to discourage the filing of baseless lawsuits against health care providers. The patient could not claim a pre-constitutional right to have an attorney bring a groundless lawsuit. Accordingly, § 52-190a did not abridge or abrogate any pre-constitutional rights of action of the patient. The statute was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the case and sustaining the objection to the request for leave to amend the complaint were reinstated. The doctor's motion to strike was treated as a motion to dismiss. The case was dismissed, and the objection to the request for leave to amend complaint was sustained.

 

1279 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. Cortright


CV084009094S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT MERIDEN


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 827



April 2, 2008, Decided 
April 2, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother obtained a temporary injunction against defendant government officials to prevent them from suspending her 16-year-old son's right to attend high school until further order after efforts were made to suspend him following his off-campus arrest for marijuana possession. Defendant officials were directed to appear at a show cause hearing, which they attended, to explain why the temporary injunction should not be continued.


OVERVIEW: The son, a high school student, was arrested off campus and charged with marijuana possession offenses. One official, an assistant principal, confronted the son. A school resources officer joined the meeting to advise the son. The school administration made a decision to suspend him. The administration then notified the mother who obtained an injunction permitting the son to return to the school. The administration recommended Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-233d expulsion proceedings. The mother alleged, inter alia, that the son was suspended without a proper hearing, suspended without an "informal hearing" in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-233c, and that his criminal case had to be concluded before he was entitled to a school hearing. The trial court found that neither Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-233d nor Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-233c violated his rights because (1) the school was not required to give the son Miranda warnings, (2) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-233c protected the son's due process rights, (3) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-233c regarding suspensions was not unconstitutionally vague, and (4) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-233d regarding expulsions was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The trial court dissolved the temporary injunction and denied an application for a permanent injunction.

 

1280 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Short v. Ward


CV074022631S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD AT BRIDGEPORT


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 733



March 25, 2008, Decided 
March 25, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff operator filed an application for temporary injunction seeking an order pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-471 compelling the Commissioner of the Connecticut Department of Motor Vehicles to not continue past February 2008, the term of the operator's license suspension after her third suspension for drunk driving under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227b.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the operator complained of a three-year suspension imposed for a violation of § 14-227b due to the operator's refusal to submit to a blood, breath, or urine test as the operator was a multiple offender. Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 14-227a and 14-227b were clear under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-2z. The Commissioner could impose the three-year suspension and to refuse the use of an interlocking ignition device (IID) to the operator. The state action survived constitutional scrutiny. The suspension and the Commissioner's rejection of the operator's request to allow her to operate her vehicle with an IID were reasonable and necessary to achieve the goal of protecting the public safety. The Commissioner was acting within his statutory authority, and the decision was not arbitrary or an abuse of discretion. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a(i) permitted the Commissioner to allow the installation of an IID for a driver whose license was suspended only if the suspension was not for "any other reason." The suspension was for a Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227b violation, which constituted "another" reason. The operator's action was barred by the State's sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: The action was dismissed.

 

1281 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Maturo v. Comm'r of Dep't of Envtl. Prot.


CV910313753S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN AT NEW HAVEN


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 763



March 19, 2008, Decided 
March 19, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A gas station owner appealed an abatement order issued by the Connecticut Commissioner of Environmental Protection directing the station owner to investigate and remediate gasoline and chemical contamination at the subject site.


OVERVIEW: The station owner contended that the imposition of clean-up costs, exceeding the value of his property, constituted an unconstitutional taking; that the hearing officer's conclusion that the station owner was not an innocent landowner under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-452d was erroneous; and that the hearing officer's bias toward the Department of Environmental Protection's (DEP) witnesses deprived him of a fair hearing. The court concluded that the station owner did not establish an innocent landowner defense. Among other things, the station owner's inquiries of the seller were not adequate, the contamination addendum to the sale contract was a "red flag" that should have alerted the station owner to such issues, and the failure to contact DEP was relevant. The court further concluded that no taking of the property occurred and the owner was not entitled to compensation for the diminution of value of his property resulting from a valid exercise of police power. As for the DEP witnesses, the court found that counsel for the station owner was allowed to and in fact did demonstrate the possibility of bias given the employee-employer relationship between the witnesses and the DEP.


OUTCOME: The appeal was denied.

 

1282 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Conn. v. Henderson


CR9385061


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 17 AT BRISTOL


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 515



March 8, 2008, Decided 
March 11, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant inmate was convicted of forgery and larceny, and then pled guilty to committing the crimes while on release on bond and being a persistent larceny offender. The inmate was sentenced in abstentia to an enhanced sentence under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40b. He was not sentenced as a persistent larceny offender. The inmate's motion to correct an illegal sentence was denied. On remand after an appeal, the motion was again denied.


OVERVIEW: The ruling was affirmed by the Connecticut Appellate Court. The trial court rejected the inmate's claim that a prior conviction used to enhance a penalty was not allowed because he was not represented when he was out on bond and committed the subsequent crimes. The inmate was not "denied" counsel in the two earlier pending cases. He did not even request to have counsel appointed in those two 1993 arrests until April 26, 1994. The enhanced sentence imposed on him was not predicated upon his guilt or innocence in those earlier cases. It was specifically predicated upon the inmate's arrest for crimes (which he subsequently admitted) while out on bond in those two cases. Section § 53a-40b did not contemplate the need for a subsequent conviction of the prior charges in order for the sanction under § 53a-40b to be invoked. The text of § 53a-40b did not refer expressly to a prior conviction as a predicate act that triggered an enhanced penalty. It focused, instead, on the status of a defendant when he or she committed a second crime. The inmate's guilt or innocence as to those earlier pending charges was of no consequence to the applicability of § 53a-40b.


OUTCOME: The inmate's motion to correct his sentence was denied.

DeLude v. Young


TTDCV075001903S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND AT ROCKVILLE

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient filed a motion to reargue, and requested that the trial court (Connecticut) vacate its decision treating defendant doctors' motion to strike as a motion to dismiss, ordering the case dismissed, and sustaining the doctors' objection to the patient's request for leave to amend the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The motion to strike argued that the medical malpractice case should be dismissed because the patient failed to attach to her complaint a detailed written opinion from a similar health care provider finding evidence of medical negligence, as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-190a(a). The trial court held that the patient did not present a new argument or a persuasive reason for revisiting the findings that the opinion attached to the complaint was not detailed, and that § 52-190a(c) required dismissal. However, the motion to reargue was granted with respect to the new claim that the opinion letter requirement in § 52-190a was unconstitutional if used to dismiss her case with an insufficient opinion letter because it would deny the patient her right to seek redress in the courts.


OUTCOME: The motion to reargue was granted as to the patient's claim that § 52-190a was unconstitutional if applied to the patient's case. In all other respects, the motion to reargue was denied.

Claims of Racial Disparity v. Comm'r of Corr.


CV054000632S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT SOMERS


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 458



February 27, 2008, Decided 
February 27, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at State v. Hayes, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1034 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 19, 2010)
Appeal dismissed by In re Claims of Racial Disparity, 135 Conn. App. 756, 42 A.3d 401, 2012 Conn. App. LEXIS 239 (May 10, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Santiago, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 203 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 26, 2005)
State v. Rizzo, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1685 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 29, 2005)
State v. Breton, 264 Conn. 327, 824 A.2d 778, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 244 (June 24, 2003)
State v. Reynolds, 264 Conn. 1, 836 A.2d 224, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 556 (July 15, 2003)
State v. Cobb, 251 Conn. 285, 743 A.2d 1, 1999 Conn. LEXIS 407 (Dec. 7, 1999)
State v. Webb, 252 Conn. 128, 750 A.2d 448, 2000 Conn. LEXIS 19 (Feb. 15, 2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, death row inmates, filed an application for a writ of habeas corpus, contending that the death penalty in Connecticut was unconstitutional because it was imposed in a racially and geographically discriminatory basis. Respondent Commissioner of Correction filed a motion to dismiss on the grounds that petitioners failed to assert their claim with due diligence, and they advanced a claim that was patently devoid of evidentiary support.


OVERVIEW: The habeas court held that petitioners acted with due diligence in pursuing the litigation. No court orders had been violated, and no dates upon which pleadings were required had been missed. The habeas court concluded that petitioners stated a claim upon which it could grant relief. Petitioners could seek to demonstrate that the imposition of the death penalty in Connecticut violated the Constitution of the State of Connecticut, even though such a statistical attack could be unavailing on the federal level. The petition alleged that there was impermissible racial disparity and other impermissible factors that crept into the decisions to charge, to prosecute, to impose, and to inflict the death penalty. It clearly asserted that that was a violation of the Connecticut Constitution. The habeas court stated that the denial of the motion to dismiss would not prejudice the Commissioner's right to seek summary judgment or to renew a motion for judgment following petitioners' presentation of their case. However, petitioners stated a cognizable claim and averred that there was evidence to support that claim. Therefore, they were entitled to proceed with the trial of that claim.


OUTCOME: The habeas court denied the Commissioner's motion to dismiss.

Axson v. Graham


075100859


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON AT NEW LONDON


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 443



February 26, 2008, Decided 
February 26, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporation filed a motion to strike plaintiff's complaint, which alleged vicarious liability.


OVERVIEW: 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106(a) preempted vicarious liability claims based solely on an owner of a motor vehicle that rented the vehicle to another person under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a. The trial court held that there was no dispute that the owner of a vehicle was engaged in the trade of renting or leasing motor vehicles. Plaintiff did not allege that the corporation itself was negligent, and there was no allegation of any criminal conduct by the owner.


OUTCOME: The trial court granted the motion to strike.

 

1286 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Francis


HHDCV074032200


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 409



February 22, 2008, Decided 
February 22, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate filed a pro se complaint against defendant prison instructor alleging that the instructor made a replacement makeshift safety guard that malfunctioned, leading to the inmate cutting his thumb severely on a band saw. The instructor filed a motion to dismiss the complaint, which was granted. The inmate moved for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that although the complaint did not indicate in which capacity the instructor appeared, the inmate served the instructor through the Connecticut Attorney General's Office, which was the manner used for serving a state officer under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-64. The inmate stated that the Connecticut Attorney General was the appropriate agent to accept service for state employees. The marshal's return indicated that he served process at the Attorney General's Office. The inmate did not serve process under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-57. Therefore, the inmate sued the instructor only in his official capacity. The summons indicated that the inmate sought both money damages and other relief. Since the instructor appeared in his official capacity only, and the inmate failed to cite any statutory authority abrogating sovereign immunity for a money damages claim, sovereign immunity barred the monetary damages claim. The inmate did not allege that the instructor acted in excess of statutory authority or pursuant to an unconstitutional statute. Rather, the complaint sounded in negligence. Therefore, the case did not fit into the injunctive relief exception to sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted.

 

1287 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


McKinnon v. Jennings


CV075013953


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 408



February 20, 2008, Decided 
February 20, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, plaintiff inmate filed suit against defendants, a nurse and a correctional officer (CO), in their individual capacities, alleging violations of the Fourteenth Amendment. The nurse and the CO moved to dismiss the suit for lack of subject matter jurisdiction on the grounds that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165 barred the suit and that the inmate failed to exhaust his administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: Due to a disability, the inmate required medication. As the inmate was receiving his medication from the nurse, the CO was standing over her. Because of the CO's proximity to the nurse, the nature of the medication was disclosed to him. The inmate alleged that this information was confidential, and that the release of the information caused him humiliation. The trial court held that since 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 was a federal statute, the law of Connecticut required that federal immunity law be applied. Under federal law, qualified immunity was an affirmative defense. The defense did not attack the jurisdiction of the court, and, therefore, a motion to dismiss was not the proper motion for such a claim. The nurse and the CO's claim that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165 required any inmate suing a state employee to exhaust administrative remedies with the claims commissioner was rejected as federal law trumped state law, and a state statute could not provide governmental immunity from 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The trial court had jurisdiction to hear the case.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1288 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Day v. Smith


CV074027999S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN AT NEW HAVEN


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 319



February 11, 2008, Decided 
February 11, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate filed an action pursuant to state constitutional law and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 against defendants, a corrections officer and the Connecticut Claims Commissioner. He alleged violations of his state and federal rights to due process and equal protection of the law. Defendants moved to dismiss on the grounds that the commissioner was entitled to absolute immunity, and that both were entitled to sovereign and statutory immunity.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed that the officer and commissioner unlawfully disposed of his property and did not authorize him to file a suit against the State to recover the property. The court held that it was without subject matter jurisdiction to hear the case. The commissioner was entitled to absolute judicial immunity for actions undertaken in the performance of his adjudicative role. Neither the legislature nor the commissioner authorized suit against the commissioner and officer. Because the inmate failed to show that the officer or commissioner impaired his equal protection or due process rights the exception to sovereign immunity occasioned by a State agent violating constitutional imperatives did not apply. The inmate did not allege that the officer and commissioner operated outside the scope of their employment when adjudicating his property claim or that they acted wilfully or maliciously. Therefore, the court had no subject matter jurisdiction to hear the inmate's State claims because the officer and commissioner were cloaked in the immunity afforded by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165. The court concluded that there was no a violation of the inmate's federal constitutional liberties.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motions to dismiss.

 

1289 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Dibble Edge Partners, LLC v. Town of Wallingford


CV064006084S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT MERIDEN


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 332



February 4, 2008, Decided 
February 4, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner filed an action against defendants, a town, a planning and zoning commission, and a realty company, alleging, among other things, that the company conspired with the town and commission to deprive it of substantive property rights in violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The company's answer contained special defenses, stating that it had qualified immunity from liability. The landowner moved to strike the special defenses.


OVERVIEW: The company's property bounded on one side of the landowner's property. The commission approved the company's application for a subdivision. The landowner appealed. The company listed a portion of its property for sale. The landowner claimed that the company rejected its offer to purchase the property. It also argued that the town and company engaged in a conspiracy that culminated in the town's purchase of a portion of the land, which included a strip that cut off the landowner's only access to a road. As a result of the conspiracy, the landowner alleged that it was deprived of the value of its property, the town's zoning regulations were subverted, and the pending appeal of the commission's decision was rendered moot. The superior court held that the company's special defenses were legally insufficient because the protection afforded by the doctrine of qualified immunity applied only to municipal employees who were sued in their personal names. Qualified immunity did not protect a private defendant against § 1983 liability where that private defendant was alleged to have conspired with government officials to deprive another of federal rights.


OUTCOME: The superior court granted the landowner's motion to strike the company's special defenses.

 

1290 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Winot


CR02184460


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1574



January 22, 2008, Decided 
June 24, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of second degree kidnapping, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-94(a), attempt to commit kidnapping in the second degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-94(a), 53a-49(a)(2) and risk of injury to a child. Defendant was sentenced to 8 years' incarceration and 10 years of parole. The kidnapping and risk of injury to a child convictions were reversed. Further appellate review was still pending, but defendant sought revision of the sentence.


OVERVIEW: In two incidents four days apart, defendant stopped his car and walked toward the same 12-year-old victim. In both incidents, defendant told the victim to get into his car. The first time, the victim ran away. In second time, forcibly grabbed the victim, although the victim was able to fight herself free. Defendant was age 40 and was in the National Guard at the time of the offense. His record indicated that he was a good soldier. Defense counsel argued that the charges were overreaching. The sentence review division found that the sentencing court relied heavily on the fact that the evidence produced at trial demonstrated that defendant had attempted to abduct the same girl twice in the same week. This is serious and dangerous behavior. Society needed to be protected from defendant, and in particular young children needed to be protected from defendant. This could have had a catastrophic ending. The victim and her family were very fortunate. Taking all of the evidence adduced at trial and considered by the trial court, the sentence was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The sentence was affirmed.

 

1291 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Carmichael v. M.I.B. Enters.


CV066000370


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD AT BRIDGEPORT


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 159



January 11, 2008, Decided 
January 11, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a passenger in a rental car, filed a suit against defendants, the company that rented the car and the car's driver, seeking to recover damages for injuries that he allegedly received when the driver rear-ended a truck in Tennessee. The company moved for summary judgment, arguing that 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106 applied to shield it from liability and that it could not be held liable because the driver was not authorized to operate the car.


OVERVIEW: A third party rented the car from the company. She did not list any other authorized drivers in her rental agreement, and she promised not to allow anyone else to operate the vehicle. The company contended that it could not be held liable for the acts of an unauthorized operator and that 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106 applied to protect it from being held vicariously liable for the accident. The court agreed that § 30106 applied because the accident occurred after the statute's effective date, the company was engaged in the business of leasing motor vehicles, and the passenger did not allege that the company had engaged in any negligent or wrongful conduct in connection with renting the car to the third party. Section 30106 precluded the passenger from holding the company liable under Connecticut law. The court rejected the passenger's claim that § 30106 was unconstitutional. It disagreed with a New York court and a Florida federal district court, which had held otherwise. In addition, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a, the company could only be held liable for acts committed by authorized drivers. The driver was not an authorized operator of the car.


OUTCOME: The court granted the company's summary judgment motion.

 

1292 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Bd. of Selectmen v. Freedom of Info. Comm'n


CV074014299S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 10



January 8, 2008, Decided 
January 8, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Bd. of Selectmen of Ridgefield v. Freedom of Info. Comm'n, 294 Conn. 438, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 1 (2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a town board of selectmen, appealed from a decision of defendant Freedom of Information Commission (FOIC), declaring null and void the acceptance of a resignation by defendant town employee, and directing the board to comply with the Freedom of Information Act. The FOIC found that the board had violated portions of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-225(d), when the matter of the employee's resignation was addressed at an "emergency meeting."


OVERVIEW: The board failed to meet its burden of demonstrating that the term "emergency" Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-225(d) was overly broad. There was no constitutional violation for vagueness merely because the general term "emergency" was used in a statute, and it was left to a hearing to gather the specifics of whether an emergency existed. Also, the record supported the FOIC's finding that the meeting was not based on an emergency. The employee's "threat" occurred in the context of an argument between two lifelong friends (the employee and one of the town selectmen), no police protection was called for either during the meeting or after, and the dispute had been sufficiently resolved at the conclusion of the meeting. There was no need to have a meeting before 24 hours elapsed and on a Saturday morning. Further, the record established that the call of the meeting, initially at least, was not a careful reaction to an emergency, but just a follow-up to the argument itself. Finally, the FOIC's decision to declare the action taken at a meeting null and void was not undercut merely because the agency did not impose that remedy in other cases.


OUTCOME: The court found that the board's contentions were without merit and dismissed the appeal.

 

1293 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Vanderlip v. Vanderlip


FSTFA990172847S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK AT STAMFORD


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 19



January 8, 2008, Decided 
January 8, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The parties challenged the court's jurisdiction to review their case file to determine whether it was properly designated as sealed, whether the docket sheet could be displayed on the judicial branch website, and whether the motions and orders to seal the fire could be made publicly available.


OVERVIEW: The judicial branch had a practice of, upon court order, permitting the sealing of everything in a case file with the exception of the names of the parties and the case docket number. This was known as Level 2 sealing. The judicial branch, on its own initiative, announced a plan to review all files designated with a Level 2 sealing to determine if they were properly designated as sealed, if the docket sheets could be displayed on the judicial branch website, and if the motions and orders to seal the file could be made publicly available. The court concluded that it had continuing jurisdiction over the files to determine whether the continuation of the sealing orders was equitable in light of changes to law. After weighing the private interest in confidentiality and the public interest in disclosure, the court held that the case file in the instant case should be unsealed. The court rejected the parties' contention that Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 25-59A(f)(2) was unconstitutional because it encroached on the legislature's powers, noting that § 25-59A provided notice and a process codifying the Constitutional balancing required and did not make the court a party.


OUTCOME: The docket sheet was ordered to be disclosed with no redactions. Stipulation(s) to seal and order thereon was ordered unsealed with no redactions. The docket sheet was to be available online and the motions and orders which have been ordered disclosed will be available to the public at the courthouse.

Fordyce v. Fordyce


FSTFA010183491S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK AT STAMFORD


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 56



January 8, 2008, Decided 
January 8, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Connecticut Judicial Branch, on its own initiative, announced a plan to review all files that were designated with a Level 2 sealing to determine: (1) whether the cases were properly designated as sealed; (2) whether the docket sheets could be displayed on the Connecticut Judicial Branch website; and (3) whether the motions and orders to seal the file could be made publicly available. Objectants filed objections to the disclosure.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that it had continuing jurisdiction to hear the matter, even though more than four months had elapsed since the entry of judgment for purposes of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-212a. The trial court had inherent power over protective orders, and had supervisory power over its own files. A new practice book rule was not being retroactively applied as Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. §§ 25-59 and 25-59A only codified a constitutional process of weighing of the privacy interests against the First Amendment public right of access. The new rules did not create a new right in the public, nor did they dictate an outcome on the continued sealing of a file or any of its contents. A res judicata claim was rejected. Concerns about the parties' privacy interests were to be weighted in the constitutional analysis. Objectants did not show that Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 25-59A was unconstitutional. Section 25-59A provided notice provisions that were in furtherance of management of a case in which sealing was before the court. It then reiterated that which was already the law. It did not make substantive new law. A slippery slope argument was rejected.


OUTCOME: The docket sheet was to be disclosed. The motion to seal and the order granting it were ordered unsealed. The docket sheet that had been ordered to be disclosed would be available online, the decision and the motions and orders which had been ordered disclosed were to be available to the public at the courthouse. The memorandum of decision and orders were unsealed.

 

1296 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


D'Albero v. Town of E. Haven


CV064079953, CV064016654


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN AT NEW HAVEN


2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 9



January 2, 2008, Decided 
January 2, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner filed an administrative appeal of a decision of the East Haven Zoning Board of Appeals (board) (Connecticut) denying him a variance with respect to two pieces of property he owned.


OVERVIEW: The owner sought the variances under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-6(a)(3) to allow him to build single-family houses on the properties. The reviewing court held that there were numerous reasons for the denial of the variances, including the proximity of the proposed homes to existing ones, property values, and the need for new roads. The owner's claim that the lots had been taxed as building lots was a claim of financial hardship that did not constitute undue hardship. The owner's claim that his failure to be able to build homes on the properties rendered them worthless did not constitute undue hardship as the properties retained their original values as side yards. The board did not act arbitrarily, illegally, or unreasonably in denying the variances. Finally, the denials of the variances were not unconstitutional takings. The government took nothing from the owner except a potential profit from the increase in value of the land if the variances were granted. The properties retained their original value, and no practical confiscation occurred. There were numerous considerations on the side of the community to balance against the potential loss to the owner.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

1297 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Crespo v. Warden


CV054000380


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND AT ROCKVILLE


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3468



December 31, 2007, Decided 
December 31, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Crespo v. Comm'r of Corr., 292 Conn. 804, 975 A.2d 42, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 216 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Crespo, 246 Conn. 665, 718 A.2d 925, 1998 Conn. LEXIS 335 (1998)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate alleged in an amended complaint that his habeas corpus attorney was ineffective in his representation of his appeal from a habeas corpus trial. As relief, the inmate asked the court to grant his petition for a writ of habeas corpus and restore his right to appeal the denial of his petition for certification to appeal the denial of his previous petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's habeas corpus attorney admittedly failed to file a motion with the appellate court to pen the inmate's appeal after it was dismissed for failure to timely file an appellate brief. The attorney testified that said failure was due to personal and health issues. The court concluded that the inmate proved the first prong of the Strickland test--his counsel failed to file the appellate brief. There was no indication that the inmate waived his right to appeal and thus, that right was abridged by counsel's failure to file the appellate brief. The court further concluded that but for the attorney's failure to file an appellate brief, the appeal would have been considered on its merits. Thus, the inmate met the prejudice requirement and was entitled to relief.


OUTCOME: The petition seeking habeas corpus relief was granted and the inmate's right to appeal the denial of his petition for certification to appeal the denial of his previous petition for a writ of habeas corpus was restored. The inmate's attorney was to file a Petition for Certification to the appellate court within thirty days.

 

1298 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Long


CR308773


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3335



December 14, 2007, Decided 
December 14, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition granted by, Motion denied by State v. Long, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1690 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 7, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Long, 268 Conn. 508, 847 A.2d 862, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 192 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Acquittee was placed under the jurisdiction of a psychiatric security review board after he was acquitted of assault due to mental disease or defect. On remand from the Connecticut Supreme Court, the court considered the State's objection to acquittee's motion to dismiss the State's petition for continued confinement under Conn. Gen. Stat. §17a-593(c).


OVERVIEW: The parties agreed that acquittee's motion to dismiss raised the same general constitutional challenge to § 17a-593(c) as in his prior motion to dismiss. Acquittee claimed that the prior decision, though in a broad sense addressing the constitutionality of § 17a-593(c), was based on a very narrow factual and procedural scenario that precluded generalization of its holding and rationale to the wider range of claims that he now sought to advance. In the State's view, the change in the acquittee's basis of attacking the statute did not sufficiently differentiate his prior challenge from the current challenge. The superior court concluded that the procedural question could not be resolved in a summary fashion. The question could only be answered after the acquittee was afforded an opportunity to argue the merits of his current motion, delineate the precise factual and legal foundation for his claims, and attempt to distinguish those claims from the binding conclusions set forth in Long. With the relevant issues then clearly and squarely framed, a court could assess the merits of the objection and determine whether the principles of claim preclusion applied.


OUTCOME: The court overruled without prejudice the State's objection and its claim for summary relief.

 

1299 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Browne v. D'Alleva


FA064004782S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WINDHAM AT PUTNAM


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3250



December 5, 2007, Decided 
December 7, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sperm donor applied for visitation and shared custody of the minor child of defendant mother. Defendant moved to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, arguing that plaintiff lacked standing, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 46b-56, 46b-61, which governed custody and visitation of a minor child, because he was only the sperm donor and not the child's natural parent.


OVERVIEW: The parties alleged different agreements were made in advance of the donor procedure, none of which were reduced to writing. At the reproductive services center, plaintiff signed a waiver of his rights were a child to be conceived. Subsequent to the child's birth, the parties acknowledged paternity and plaintiff was listed on the birth certificate. Plaintiff refused to sign papers allowing for the adoption of the child by defendant's civil partner and litigation followed. The court reviewed other courts' decisions on similar matters finding that none of the cases was dispositive but the reasons in each were helpful. Connecticut's sperm donor statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-775, was ambiguous in the absence of definitions for the words "known" or "identified" sperm donor. The statute's purpose did not fit the case. Even if the statute were unambiguous, application would have violated plaintiff's due process rights. Based on the circumstances surrounding defendant's decision to be artificially inseminated by plaintiff's sperm, the parties' preconception intent, the evidence submitted and, in particular, the acknowledgment of paternity, plaintiff had standing to make his application.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss.

 

1300 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Ruegg v. Allis


HHBCV065001822


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3059



November 28, 2007, Decided 
November 28, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff filed a personal injury suit against defendants, a driver and the lessor of a car. The lessor filed a motion to strike on the ground that 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106 preempted Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a, which imposed vicarious liability upon lessors of motor vehicles.


OVERVIEW: The federal statute applied to suits commenced after the statute's enactment date, August 20, 2005. The suit here was commenced in 2006. Plaintiff argued that the federal statute was an unconstitutional attempt by Congress to extend its Commerce Clause power into an area reserved to the states. The court rejected this argument. Unlike potential lost work days, which the United States Supreme Court had found to have only a tangential relationship to interstate commerce, the highly mobile business of leasing cars was clearly one that was fully intertwined with interstate commerce. Therefore, there was no merit to plaintiff's Commerce Clause argument. The federal statute preempted state law and applied to plaintiff's complaint.


OUTCOME: The court granted the lessor's motion to strike.

 

1301 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ngobeni


CR060129997


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WINDHAM, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 11 AT DANIELSON


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3069



November 15, 2007, Decided 
November 16, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at In re Ngobeni, 2009 Mass. LEXIS 24 (Mass., Feb. 13, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with three counts of larceny in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-124, 53a-125, and 53a-125b, one count of forgery in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-140, and one count of practicing law while his license was suspended in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-88. He filed a motion to dismiss the complaint. The motion to dismiss was treated as having been brought pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 41-8(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a licensed attorney in the State of Connecticut whose license to practice law was suspended before the complainant alleged that she hired defendant to process an immigration matter through the United States Custom and Immigration Service. Defendant's services included a consultation, the quotation of a fee and the provision of a letter outlining the terms of the representation. Defendant then allegedly altered checks or money orders provided by the complainant. The court found that the State of Connecticut had authority to prosecute defendant for practicing law in the federal arena because the Supremacy Clause of the United States Constitution did not prohibit the State from exercising such authority. However, the purpose of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-88 was to enforce the prohibition against the unauthorized practice of law by persons who had not been admitted as attorneys. Because defendant was admitted to the Connecticut bar, and his admission had not been revoked, he continued to be an attorney. As such, he was exempt from the statute. Finally, defendant did not show grounds for vindictive prosecution or prosecutorial misconduct.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted as to the count of the information alleging practice of law by a person not an attorney. The balance of the motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1302 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Gooden v. Dep't of Corr.


CV020813590


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3073



November 13, 2007, Decided 
November 13, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Findings of fact/conclusions of law at, Judgment entered by Gooden v. Dep't of Corr., 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1624 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 20, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Commission on Human Rights and Opportunities (CHRO) issued a release of jurisdiction under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-100, plaintiff employee sued defendant Department of Correction (DOC), alleging racial discrimination in employment (count one), racial discrimination and retaliation in employment (count two), breach of contract (count three), and negligent infliction of emotional distress (NIED) (count four). DOC filed a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: DOC asserted lack of subject matter jurisdiction due to sovereign immunity, defects in the service of process, and the employee's failure to exhaust administrative remedies with the CHRO. The court held that as DOC failed to raise the personal jurisdiction issue within 30 days, this defense was waived pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. §§ 10-30 and 10-32. The employee's breach of contract claim (count three) failed, as (1) he did not assert any statute by which the State waived sovereign immunity, and (2) the claims commissioner did not authorize him to sue the State for money damages. Count three lacked any allegations that, if proven, would support his allegation that DOC acted in excess of its statutory authority in breaching its employment contract with him. Count four (NIED) failed because (1) he named no individual defendants; (2) he identified no statute by which the State waived sovereign immunity; and (3) he did not claim a violation of constitutionally protected rights or that the State acted in excess of its statutory authority. As to count two, DOC submitted no affidavits to support its claim that the issue of retaliation was never raised before the CHRO.


OUTCOME: DOC's motion to dismiss counts three and four of the employee's complaint was granted but its motion to dismiss count two was denied.

Thames River Apt. Tenants v. New London Hous. Auth.


X04CV064006233S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT MIDDLETOWN


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3041



November 13, 2007, Decided 
November 13, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenant sued defendants, a housing authority, its commissioners and executive director, a city, and the city's police chief and director of health. She claimed defendants engaged in negligent and unconstitutional conduct and violated their statutory duties with regard to providing safe and habitable low income housing. She moved for an order that the action proceed as a class action on behalf of all persons situated similarly to herself.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff claimed to represent all tenants of the authority's apartment complex. She alleged defendants failed to provide habitable housing, in violation of state law. The first eight counts sought money damages for personal injuries. Her ninth count sought an injunction directing some defendants to provide housing as required by statute and the appointment of a receiver. The court held plaintiff satisfied the numerosity, commonality, and typicality factors of Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 9-7. Defendants agreed that counsel was competent, and, insofar as only injunctive relief for present tenants was sought, there was no direct conflict of interest. The conditions of the premises, the ability to move residents, and the legal questions were subject to generalized evidence. However, individualized evidence would be required to prove each class member's damages. Therefore, the court found that Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 9-8's predominance factor was satisfied as to injunctive relief, as requested in count nine, but not as to items of damage alleged in the first eight counts. And as to count nine, a class action was superior to other available remedies.


OUTCOME: The court certified a class, limited to present tenants, as to count nine, seeking injunctive damages, but not as to the other counts for other types of claimed damages.

Columbia Air Servs. v. DOT


5001480


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON AT NEW LONDON


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3025



November 8, 2007, Decided 
November 8, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Columbia Air Servs. v. DOT, 293 Conn. 342, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 359 (2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff air services company filed an amended complaint against defendant state transportation agency alleging claims for breach of contract, breach of the covenant of good faith and fair dealing, fraud, unjust enrichment, quantum meruit, deprivation of constitutional rights, and violation of state antitrust law. The air services company also asserted an administrative appeal. The agency moved to dismiss the amended complaint.


OVERVIEW: The agency invited proposals for the construction, management, and maintenance of an aviation-related facility. The agency reserved the right in the proposal to terminate the proposal process prior to execution of a final agreement. The air services company submitted a bid and was then awarded the leasehold and development rights. However, the agency later terminated those rights without executing a final agreement. The air services company sued agency. On the agency's motion to dismiss, the trial court found that sovereign immunity barred the breach of contract, breach of covenant of good faith and fair dealing, unjust enrichment, and quantum meruit claims since those claims were against the state for money damages and the air services company did not overcome the presumption that sovereign immunity barred those action. It also found that fraud, constitutional, and antitrust claims were barred by sovereign immunity and no waiver of sovereign immunity was shown, and that no administrative appeal was involved because administrative remedies had not been exhausted.


OUTCOME: The trial court granted the agency's motion to dismiss.

 

1305 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Tayco Corp. v. Wallingford Planning & Zoning


CV064017351S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN AT NEW HAVEN


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2918



November 6, 2007, Decided 
November 6, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, in part, Remanded by Tayco Corp. v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n of Wallingford, 294 Conn. 673, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 21 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Tayco Corp. v. Wallingford Planning & Zoning Comm'n, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2091 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 11, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed an action by defendant Planning and Zoning Commission after their application was approved subject to conditions enumerated in a special permit. The property owners contended the conditions imposed were illegal and that they had a pre-existing non-conforming right to operate their business. They requested that the conditions be declared null and void.


OVERVIEW: The property owners filed an application for a special permit for fill and excavation, including screening, stockpiling and sale of earth products for an earth material processing center and landscaping material storage. The property was located partially in an industrial zone and partially in a residential zone. They had acquired title to the property after the enactment of the zoning regulations. Prior to the enactment of the regulations, the property had been used for sand and gravel operations, which included the screening, storing, excavating, stockpiling and selling of earth products, which included the sale of landscaping material. The property owners continued the same operations after their acquisition of title. The court held that the action of the Commission acting in a legislative function in establishing the zoning designation for the property divided the use of each portion to be governed by the particular zone that it was located within. The requirement of a special permit did not apply to the pre-existing non-conforming portion designated as industrial. Thus, the Commission abused its discretion as an administrative zoning agency.


OUTCOME: The conditions imposed exceeded the jurisdiction of the Commission and they were declared null and void.

Neighborhood Builders, Inc. v. Town of Madison


X01CV044005268S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT WATERBURY


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2711



October 12, 2007, Decided


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part Neighborhood Builders, Inc. v. Town of Madison, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1247 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 14, 2008)
Affirmed by Neighborhood Builders, Inc. v. Town of Madison, 294 Conn. 651, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 20 (2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, developers and builders, filed an action against defendant town, alleging violations of assorted statutes, including the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUTPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110a et seq., arising from the town's collection of alleged excessive building permit fees (BPFs). Plaintiffs filed a motion for class certification under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. §§ 9-7 and 9-8.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs alleged that the town required them to obtain building permits in order to conduct their trades, and that the fees collected were in excess of the cost relating to the service provided, were used for the funding of unrelated social programs, and constituted an illegal taking without just compensation. The court initially noted that it would not review claims that were not raised in the amended pleading. Further, plaintiffs had standing to assert the CUTPA claims, as they directly paid the allegedly excessive BPFs, whether the cost thereof was passed on to others or not. Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. §§ 9-7 and 9-8, class certification was proper in the circumstances. There were over 1,000 members of the class for purposes of numerosity under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 9-7(1), there was a commonality of issues under § 9-7(2), and the claim of excessive fees was typical of all putative class members under § 9-7(3). The named plaintiffs were adequate representatives under § 9-7(4), and the claims fell within the requirements for superiority and predominance pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 9-8.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion for class certification. The court directed that the class was to consist of entities that directly paid to the town the allegedly excessive BPFs during a set period of time.
