Carroll-Hall v. Rell


X09CV054019406


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT HARTFORD


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2478



September 17, 2007, Decided 
September 17, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, parents of public school students, filed an action alleging that the Connecticut system for funding public education was unconstitutional. Defendants, the governor and other state officials, moved to strike three of the four counts.


OVERVIEW: The parents argued that Connecticut students had a constitutional right to "suitable" educational opportunities which would prepare them to function as responsible citizens and advance through higher education, and that this right was denied by the state's maintenance of an unconstitutional system for funding public education. The parents sought to permanently enjoin defendants from operating the funding system and order them to create a public education system that would provide suitable educational opportunities for all children. The court could not find in the text of Conn. Const. art. 8, § 1, and Conn. Const. art. 1, §§ 1 and 20, the decisions of the Connecticut Supreme Court, the U.S. Supreme Court, the history and context of the constitutional guarantee of free public elementary and secondary schools, or appropriate economic, cultural, or public policy considerations any basis for concluding that there existed a constitutional right to "suitable" educational opportunities. The counts of the complaint which were premised on the existence of a constitutional right to a "suitable" education did not state a claim on which the court could grant relief and had to be stricken.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike counts one, two, and four was granted.

 

1309 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Whitehead v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV06-4021043


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


50 Conn. Supp. 453; 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2422; 937 A.2d 87



September 13, 2007, Decided 
September 13, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 27, 2007.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff filed an administrative appeal of the action of defendant planning and zoning commission. Plaintiff filed a motion requesting that the commission provide her with copies of documents in the return of record without cost to her. The commission contended that it was not obliged to pay the costs of copying the record.


OVERVIEW: The commission did not contest plaintiff's right to make copies of the record but argued it had to be done at her own expense. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8(i), which required a zoning authority to transmit the record to the court, was silent as to whether the record had to be served on the other party to the action. The court noted that the rules for the Connecticut superior courts applied to administrative appeals, because they were "civil actions." Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 7-6 required a certificate of service on all documents filed with the court, and Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 10-12(a) generally required counsel for a party to serve on all other parties any pleadings, motions, claims, notices, or similar papers. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8(i) did not indicate that filing the record with the court was intended to be the only requirement placed on zoning authorities regarding service, or that the courts' normal procedural rules as to service were not to be operative. Therefore, where a plaintiff appealed the decision of a zoning board, the record had to be turned over to the plaintiff without cost.


OUTCOME: Plaintiff's motion was granted and the commission was ordered to turn over the record to plaintiff without cost to her.

 

1310 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Honulik v. Town of Greenwich


X05CV04199882S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT STAMFORD


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2415



September 4, 2007, Decided 
September 4, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by, Modified by Honulik v. Town of Greenwich, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2987 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 8, 2007)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Honulik v. Town of Greenwich, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 20 (Conn., Feb. 24, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police lieutenant sought relief against defendants, a town, a police captain, a chief, and the town's former human resources director, after having been passed over for promotion to a position of captain. In a five-count amended complaint he sought injunctive relief and damages for breach of contract and promissory estoppel, enforcement of writs of mandamus and quo warranto, and relief pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: The court found that an injunction was appropriate, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-471, as the town and its personnel had by their actions in passing over the lieutenant demonstrated that absent some stay or other injunctive relief, they were likely to continue to cause harm to the lieutenant and others in the police department similarly situated. Such harm would be irreparable, and the lieutenant was likely to prevail on appeal. Under the circumstances, the lieutenant's expectation of promotion based upon his rank on a promotion list rose to the level of a constitutionally protected property interest under § 1983. In considering the lieutenant's due process claim under § 1983, the court found that the evidence clearly supported a finding that the town had a merit-based promotion program which was in part based upon the town charter; written rules, policies, and procedures; a written collective bargaining agreement; and in part upon a well-established past practice of promoting persons by rank order on the promotion list. Accordingly, defendants' failure to promote the lieutenant in accordance therewith was an unwarranted deprivation of his fundamental property rights without due process.


OUTCOME: Among other orders, judgment was entered in favor of the lieutenant on counts one, three, and four of the amended complaint, and for defendants on counts two and five. The captain was ordered to cease occupying the office of police captain in the police department. The lieutenant was promoted to occupy the office of captain, with seniority dating therefrom, together with all back pay, benefits, as well as prejudgment interest thereon.

 

1311 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Rosztoczy v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n of Darien


FSTCV0640009426S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK AT STAMFORD


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2412



September 4, 2007, Decided 
September 6, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff abutting landowners appealed a decision of defendant town planning and zoning commission, in which the commission granted an application filed by defendant executrix of a decedent's estate to subdivide a parcel of property.


OVERVIEW: The commission approved five waivers of the town subdivision regulations in approving the application. The reviewing court held that the landowners were statutorily aggrieved. The appeal was timely and service was proper. The commission's decision was proper. The regulations specified adequately the conditions under which a waiver of the specific regulations would be granted, and Darien, Conn., Subdivision Regs. art. I, § B set forth many criteria to be considered by the commission in evaluating whether to approve subdivision applications. Those criteria guided the commission and allowed those affected to know their rights. The landowners did not show that the subdivision regulations were vague and invalid. The commission could waive the requirement contained in Darien, Conn., Subdivision Regs. art. IV, § E9. Both parties offered a plausible definition for the word "certain" in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-26. Requiring the commission to single out each requirement that was subject to waiver would not facilitate the commission's operational function. Finally, the claim that a commission member's wife spoke on behalf of her husband was rejected.


OUTCOME: The appeal of the commission's decision to grant the executrix's subdivision application was dismissed.

 

1312 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Gonzalez v. Surgeon


CV074032320


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2356



August 29, 2007, Decided 
August 29, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by, Certified question answered by Gonzalez v. Surgeon, 284 Conn. 141, 931 A.2d 833, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 377 (2007)
Affirmed by, Certified question answered by Gonzalez v. Surgeon, 284 Conn. 554, 937 A.2d 13, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 494 (Conn., Sept. 19, 2007)
Affirmed by Gonzalez v. Surgeon, 284 Conn. 145, 931 A.2d 835, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 376 (2007)
Affirmed by Gonzalez v. Surgeon, 284 Conn. 573, 937 A.2d 24, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 493 (Conn., Sept. 19, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, plaintiffs, candidates for local office and their petition circulators, challenged the rejection pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-410 of certain nominating petitions by defendants, the Democratic registrar of voters and a city clerk. Plaintiffs, inter alia, asserted that § 9-410 was unconstitutionally vague and that it violated the First Amendment as well as Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 4, 5, 10, 14.


OVERVIEW: The petitions were rejected because the circulators had circulated nominating petitions for more than one candidate for the same office. The court ruled in favor of defendants, holding that 1) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-410(c) was violated regardless of the fact that the circulators did not circulate petitions for more than one candidate simultaneously; 2) the fact that one of the candidates was acting as a placeholder candidate and that he intended to withdraw after the ballot was set had no bearing on the application of § 9-410(c) as he was a "candidate" at the times relevant to the case; 3) § 9-410(c) was not void for vagueness as it provided clear boundaries regarding the circulation of nominating petitions for two candidates for the same office; and 4) § 9-410(c)'s limitations on petition circulators placed only a slight burden on a circulator's right of association and free speech and the state interest in discouraging unfair tactics and the sponsoring of weaker rival candidates for strategic reasons justified that slight restriction. Section 9-401(c) did not violate either the U.S or state constitutions.


OUTCOME: Judgment was entered in favor of defendants in both cases on all counts of the two complaints.

 

1313 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Delgado v. Comm'r of Corr.


CV044000164


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT SOMERS


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2218



August 21, 2007, Decided 
August 21, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Delgado v. Comm'r of Corr., 114 Conn. App. 609, 970 A.2d 792, 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 183 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Delgado, 247 Conn. 616, 725 A.2d 306, 1999 Conn. LEXIS 15 (1999)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, an inmate, filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus challenging his convictions of murder and commission of a felony with a firearm. In the petition, the inmate argued that he received ineffective assistance of counsel in violation of the Sixth Amendment.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that his trial counsel was ineffective because she failed to have the inmate testify at the suppression hearing, offer an alibi defense, and for other actions. The court held that the Sixth Amendment guaranteed reasonable competence, not perfect advocacy judged with the benefit of hindsight. The court found the inmate's claim that counsel was ineffective for failing to have the inmate testify at a suppression hearing to be without merit. The inmate's claim that he signed a blank sheet of paper, and that the police later filled in the confession, was not credible, as the inmate also initialled several strikeouts throughout the document. The court further found that trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to present an alibi defense. There was no credible support for an alibi other than testimony by the inmate and his brother, and there was no reasonable probability that the result of the trial would have been different had the alimony testimony been presented. Given the state of the evidence presented at the habeas trial, there simply was no basis upon which the court could conclude that there was any unreliability in the conviction.


OUTCOME: The habeas corpus petition was denied.

 

1314 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rosario


CR05138326


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2324



August 21, 2007, Decided 
August 30, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at State v. Rosario, 118 Conn. App. 389, 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 524 (2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with crimes and filed a motion to dismiss the charges against him based upon a claim that he had been deprived of a speedy trial. The trial court then held a hearing on the motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested on criminal charges and was arraigned. For five months, his case was the subject of multiple judicial pretrials. The case was then placed on the firm jury list, where it remained for a year until he filed a motion to dismiss alleging that his speedy trial rights had been violated. During the entire pendency of the matter, defendant was incarcerated in lieu of bond. The trial court then held a hearing on the motion. Defendant suggested in the motion that state statutes dealing with speedy trials, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 54-82m and 54-142a(c), were unconstitutional because they set forth specific time limits whereas the Sixth Amendment speedy trial right contained no specific time limit. The trial court rejected his argument because it found that the states were free to prescribe a reasonable period consistent with constitutional standards. The trial court then applied the four-part Barker test to determine whether defendant's speedy trial rights had been violated and, accordingly, considered length of delay, the reason for the delay, his assertion of the right, and prejudice to defendant. It then determined that his speedy trial rights had not been violated.


OUTCOME: The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss.

 

1315 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Crawford v. Warden


TSRCV044000210S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND AT ROCKVILLE


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2182



August 10, 2007, Decided 
August 10, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Crawford v. Comm'r of Corr., 294 Conn. 165, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 478 (2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought a writ of habeas corpus against respondent warden.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner first argued that the trial court failed to properly advise him of the constitutional rights he was waiving by pleading guilty. The court noted that petitioner had not sought to withdraw his plea and had not sought permission to file an untimely appeal. Thus, procedural default applied to this claim. Petitioner had not shown that ineffective assistance of counsel was the cause and prejudice, as it was uncontroverted that he wanted to plead guilty and that he had received the agreed-upon sentence. Petitioner's next claim, that the State had violated the plea agreement, thereby violating due process, was not only procedurally defaulted, but without merit. He had not proven that there was an agreement as to presentence confinement credit. Next, the court had no authority to award petitioner a credit under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-98d(a)(2)(A). Petitioner had not requested such a credit in the trial court or alleged that the failure to make such a request was ineffective assistance of counsel. Finally, there was no Practice Book or statutory requirement mandating that a defendant be provided with a notice of the right to appeal from a conviction arising from a guilty plea.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

 

1316 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hogan v. State Dep't of Children & Families


CV064012236S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2125



August 3, 2007, Decided 
August 3, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, in part, Remanded by Hogan v. Dep't of Children & Families, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 29 (Conn., Mar. 10, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a hearing officer with defendant, the State of Connecticut Department of Children and Families (Department), held in a final decision that a child abuse incident involving plaintiff, a former shift supervisor at the New Haven Detention Center (employee), required the employee's name to be placed on the child abuse registry list was substantiated, the employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee contended that: (1) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-101k, as amended by the registry list provision, was unconstitutionally vague, represented an overly-broad delegation to the Department by the legislature, and constituted a bill of attainder; (2) the substantiation of physical abuse was not supported by substantial evidence; and, (3) the act of placing his name on the registry list was not supported by substantial evidence. As to the first two claims, the court disagreed. First, the statute met constitutional standards. Similarly, the Connecticut legislature, setting forth its concern for children at risk, did not violate the separation of powers doctrine in enacting § 17a-101k. Third, the statute was one of general application which happened to have an adverse impact on the employee. Hence, the statute did not amount to a bill of attainder. As to the employee's second claim, the employee's actions likely resulted in the child being injured, and his act of using one child to discipline another was an intentional or grossly negligent act. But, it was apparent that the finding of chronicity was unsupported by the evidence. Hence, remand as to this issue was ordered.


OUTCOME: Because support for the hearing officer's finding as to the specific "chronicity" factor of the employee's using a child, more than once, to intimidate another was not reflected in the record, the matter was remanded to the Department for further consideration of whether the employee's name should appear on the registry list. But, in all other respects, the judgment was affirmed.

State v. Hankerson


HHBCR060226416T


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1923



July 24, 2007, Decided 
July 24, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by State v. Hankerson, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1906 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 26, 2007)
Decision reached on appeal by State v. Hankerson, 118 Conn. App. 380, 983 A.2d 898, 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 517 (2009)
Related proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Apodaca, 303 Conn. 378, 33 A.3d 224, 2012 Conn. LEXIS 5 (2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with, inter alia, felony murder. Defendant filed a motion to suppress statements made to police in New York and Connecticut.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was detained in New York with fugitive proceedings pending. The police from a Connecticut city went to New York and spoke to defendant. The Connecticut officer then took custody of defendant and transported him to Connecticut, where he was again interviewed. Defendant contended that the statements he allegedly made in New York and Connecticut should have been suppressed because they were obtained without an adequate advisement and waiver of Miranda rights, and the police officers had no extra-jurisdictional authority to conduct custodial interrogations in New York. Among other things, the court concluded that defendant was advised of his Miranda rights in New York, and knowingly and voluntarily waived those rights; there was no evidence that defendant's decision was anything other than the result of his free, considered, and unconstrained choice. The court also found that defendant was given his Miranda rights again in Connecticut and again voluntarily waived those rights. Contrary to defendant's contention, defendant had no Sixth Amendment right to counsel at the extradition hearing, as such a right would only have attached at the time of arraignment.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion to suppress was denied.

 

1318 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hoskie v. Comm'r of Corr.


CV030004097


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT SOMERS


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1905



July 20, 2007, Decided 
July 20, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Hoskie v. Comm'r of Corr., 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 485 (Conn. App. Ct., Oct. 21, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Hoskie, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1289 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 25, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate, who had been convicted of kidnapping and unlawful restraint, filed a habeas corpus action against the Commissioner of Correction. Petitioner alleged that the prosecutor had failed to divulge exculpatory evidence in violation of Brady. The court held a trial on the habeas petition.


OVERVIEW: Before the time of the crimes in question, petitioner had been involved in several incidents with the victim where he was the aggressor. Most of the incidents had been reported to the police and later prosecuted, but there had been one incident, revealed in a conversation between the victim and the prosecutor, that was never reported to the police. The prosecutor did not reveal this incident to petitioner's defense counsel or mention it at trial or at sentencing. Petitioner claimed that this incident was exculpatory. The court stated that for there to be a Brady violation, the undisclosed evidence had to be exculpatory. Here, there was no basis upon which the court could conclude that the undisclosed material was exculpatory; the most logical interpretation of the material was that it was inculpatory. Accordingly, there had been no Brady violation. Furthermore, there was no basis on which the court could conclude that there was any unreliability in petitioner's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court denied the habeas corpus petition.

 

1319 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Poirier v. Papadopoulos


CV065001333S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX AT MIDDLETOWN


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1842



July 19, 2007, Decided 
July 19, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the owner and lessor of a vehicle involved in an accident, filed a motion for summary judgment in plaintiff cyclist's personal injury action against the owner and defendant lessee. The cyclist's complaint alleged negligence and recklessness against both defendants.


OVERVIEW: At the time of the accident, the lessee was driving a vehicle he had leased from the owner. The owner based its motion for summary judgment on 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106 and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a(b). The court granted the motion. As of August 10, 2005, 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106 preempted Connecticut law regarding the vicarious liability of the owner of a leased vehicle. Under § 30106, the owner was not liable for personal or property damage arising from the operation of its vehicle so long as it was in the business of leasing motor vehicles, there was no negligence on the owner's part, and there was no criminal wrongdoing on the owner's part. There was no dispute that the owner was in the business of leasing vehicles and there were no allegations of negligence or criminal wrongdoing by the owner itself. Further, even if § 30106 did not apply, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a(b) precluded any recovery against the owner because the driver had leased the vehicle for more than one year and had insured the vehicle for bodily injury liability in the amount of $100,000 per person and $300,000 per occurrence.


OUTCOME: The motion for summary judgment was granted.

Cimino v. Town of Woodbridge


CV064019092


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN AT NEW HAVEN


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1837



July 17, 2007, Decided 
July 17, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Cimino v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals of Woodbridge, 117 Conn. App. 569, 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 450 (2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Zoning Board denied plaintiff property owner's request for a variance. The property owner appealed claiming the Board's decision was illegal, arbitrary, and in abuse of discretion. The property owner argued, inter alia, that the decision of the Board was not supported by the record and that without the variance no reasonable use of the property could be made.


OVERVIEW: The property owner noted that the Board took the position that the property was not part of any approved subdivision and that only a four-lot subdivision was approved with the subject property being entitled as "remaining land." The court held that, if that was true, then Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-26a(b) did not apply. The subject lot was never an approved buildable lot. The zoning commission could not have approved the property as a buildable lot given the important state policy regarding inland wetlands and watercourses. Nothing as to value was presented before the Board. It was difficult for the court to conclude the property was worthless or of no value because of the enactment of the regulations and the failure to grant the variance. The property owner knew or should have known of the Inland Wetland problem when the property was acquired. The town had an interest in making zoning changes it deemed necessary for health and safety and for protecting the environment. The property owner did not meet her burden of proving the variance she sought would not substantially affect the comprehensive plan.


OUTCOME: The appeal was denied.

 

1321 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Goines v. Safeco Ins. Co.


CV065005684S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1863



July 16, 2007, Decided 
July 16, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant lessor of a motor vehicle filed a motion to strike count three of plaintiff's complaint in which plaintiff alleged that she was involved in a motor vehicle accident with defendant lessee and that the lessor was liable for damages pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a based on vicarious liability.


OVERVIEW: The lessor claimed that § 14-154a was preempted by 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106. The court agreed, finding that a condition of preemption under § 30106 was that there was no negligence on the part of the lessor. Because plaintiff failed to allege specific negligence on the lessor's part, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a was preempted by 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106. The court also concluded that § 30106 was not unconstitutional as it applied to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a because plaintiff failed to establish that 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106 was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt and failed to raise the issue of constitutionality in her complaint. Therefore, the court struck count three from the complaint.


OUTCOME: The court granted the lessor's motion to strike count three of the complaint.

 

1322 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Peeler


CR99148396


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD AT BRIDGEPORT


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1772



July 10, 2007, Decided


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Peeler, 271 Conn. 338, 857 A.2d 808, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 394 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss a capital penalty hearing. Defendant's motion attacked the constitutionality of the capital felony statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a.


OVERVIEW: Most of defendant's grounds had been rejected by either the U.S. Supreme Court in the Walton v. Arizona decision or by the state supreme court in the Rizzo and Ross decisions. The argument that the statute violated the Sixth, Eighth, and Fourteenth Amendments because it gave prosecutors unfettered discretion to seek or decline to seek a death sentence had been rejected by the U.S. Supreme Court in Gregg v. Georgia. Defendant's Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 8, 9, claim on that point failed because the state supreme court had upheld the constitutionality of several death sentences resulting from the very prosecutorial discretion of which defendant complained. The fact that the statute placed the burden of proving mitigating circumstances on defendant was not a violation of his rights. Finally, the claim that race had an arbitrary, capricious, impermissibly discriminatory and disproportionate effect on capital sentencing both in Connecticut and elsewhere, in violation of both the federal and state constitutions, was a claim that had to be presented in a habeas corpus proceeding.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion was denied.

State v. Chapulis


CR060121351S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD, GEOGRAPHIC AREA 18 AT BANTAM


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1429



June 4, 2007, Decided 
June 5, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the information that charged him with engaging as a real estate broker without a license, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-325. The motion was filed pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 41-8(5), (8), (9).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested on a warrant after he sold a piece of real property at an auction. He had been engaged to sell the property by the executor of an estate. Defendant alleged that there was insufficient evidence to show that he was a real estate broker or real estate salesperson engaged in the real estate business pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-311 and that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-325 was unconstitutionally vague as applied to him. The court denied the motion, holding inter alia that 1) dismissal was denied on the lack of probable cause ground because defendant was arrested on a warrant for which a previous judge found probable cause; 2) Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 20-311, 20-325 were not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant as he had a reasonable opportunity to know that he could not list or sell property without a license, and in fact, had received a warning from the state realtor board that he should not conduct the auction sale; and 3) as there was no evidence that defendant was acting as an agent or fiduciary for the executor, the exemption from liability in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-329 did not apply.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1324 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


New Organics Co. v. Bloomfield Bakers, Inc.


CV020815943


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1256



May 23, 2007, Decided 
May 23, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Third-party defendant, an organic cooking oil manufacturer, filed a motion to dismiss the third-party complaint filed by third-party plaintiff baking company. The baking company asserted that the manufacturer provided it with defective organic canola oil, which the baking company used in cookies and crackers it produced for plaintiff company. Plaintiff filed suit against the baking company alleging the cookies and crackers were defective.


OVERVIEW: The manufacturer asserted that the court lacked personal jurisdiction over it under the long-arm statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 33-929(f). The court agreed. The clear language of the statute stated that a foreign corporation could be sued in Connecticut only by a resident of the state or by a person having a usual place of business in the state. The baking company was not a resident of the state and did not have a usual place of business in the state. Further, there was no evidence that the manufacturer had minimum contacts with the state. The mere fact that it placed organic canola oil into the stream of commerce did not create such contacts. The baking company's claim that § 33-929 was unconstitutional was rejected as the baking company failed to offer proof of unconstitutionality beyond a reasonable doubt. Contrary to the baking company's claim, if any tortious act was committed by the manufacturer, it was committed in California, not Connecticut. Finally, under the doctrine of forum non conveniens, the proper venue for resolution of the third-party dispute was California, the home state of the two entities.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted.

Gallimore v. Comm'r of Corr.

PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Gallimore, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1244 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 28, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a prisoner, filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus in the Superior Court, Judicial District of Tolland, Connecticut, seeking to have the court set aside his convictions and return his case to the docket for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner alleged that he was deprived of the effective representation of trial counsel and appellate counsel as guaranteed by the Sixth Amendment to the United States Constitution. Most of the evidence produced at the habeas trial focused on the prisoner's complaints regarding his trial counsel. Despite the laundry list of counsel's shortcomings, the prisoner's evidence failed establish that counsel's alleged deficiencies, even if proved, prejudiced him in any way. Consequently, the court concluded that the prisoner was not deprived of the effective assistance of counsel at any stage of the proceedings.


OUTCOME: The petition for writ of habeas corpus was denied.

1327 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Bristol Hosp., Inc. v. Smith


CV065002055


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1094



May 4, 2007, Decided  
May 4, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hospital filed an action against defendants, a patient and his wife, to recover for unpaid hospital bills. The wife filed a motion to strike the second count of the complaint on the ground that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-37, which made married couples responsible for each other's hospital expenses, violated the equal protection clauses of the federal constitution and Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 1 and 20.


OVERVIEW: The court first rejected the wife's argument that the statute treated married couples differently from similarly situated civil union partners. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-38oo indicated that when statutes used a term denoting a spousal relationship, a party to a civil union should be included in such use or definition. Therefore, under § 46b-38oo, a civil union partner could be substituted in § 46b-37 in place of either "husband" or "wife"; thus, the statute applied to civil union couples as well as married couples, and there was no equal protection violation. The court next rejected the wife's argument that the statute imposed an unfair burden on a person's right to marry by not imposing a similar burden upon unmarried individuals. Connecticut did not recognize the validity of nonmarital relationships between heterosexual couples. As such, the participants in such relationships were not similarly situated to the participants in traditional opposite sex marriages. As there was no equality of status between the two groups of individuals, equal protection was not implicated by the requirement that married spouses be responsible for each other's hospital expenses.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to strike.

 

1328 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Booker v. Jarjura


UWYC0V064011301S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY AT WATERBURY


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1083



April 30, 2007, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Booker v. Jarjura, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1115 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 2, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the minority leader of a city board of aldermen, brought an action in quo warranto under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-491 and for mandamus against defendants, the city's mayor and various board and commission members. Plaintiff claimed that the members were not properly appointed to their positions and that the mayor made the appointments in disregard of Waterbury, Conn., Charter ch. 4, § 4-2(b)(1).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a member of the Independent party, in his capacity as minority leader submitted a list of individuals to the Democratic mayor for appointments to boards and commissions; however, the mayor submitted his own list to the board of aldermen. Plaintiff claimed that the mayor had to follow plaintiff's list of recommendations. While defendant argued that the mayor was constrained by plaintiff's list only if he wished to appoint someone who belonged to the same political party as plaintiff, the court held that the addition of the word "party" to § 4-2(b)(1) in a 2002 charter revision was to prevent the mayor from appointing the maximum number of people from the mayor's own political party and then appointing additional people belonging to a different political party than that of the minority leader. Thus, three board members had to be ousted. However, two commission members were not ousted as § 4-2(b)(1) did not apply to the finance and audit review commission under Waterbury, Conn., Charter ch. 6, § 6B-1(b) as no more than three members of the seven-member commission could be from the same political party and also did not apply to the civil service commission.


OUTCOME: The court ousted three board members as they were minority party members and did not appear on plaintiff's list of recommendations. However, two commission members were not ousted as Waterbury, Conn., Charter ch. 4, § 4-2(b)(1) did not apply to the commissions on which they served. The court also granted the writ of mandamus and directed the mayor to make board and commission appointments as required by § 4-2(b)(1).

 

1329 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. Oneto


CV055001528


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN AT NEW HAVEN


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1025



April 26, 2007, Decided  
April 27, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff accident victim sued defendants, the lessee and the lessor, for personal injuries arising from an auto accident. The victim sued the lessee under a claim of negligence, and the lessor under a claim of vicarious liability pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a. The lessor filed a motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The plaintiff's vehicle and a vehicle operated by the lessee collided. At the time of the accident, the lessee was operating a private passenger motor vehicle owned, and leased to him, by the lessor. The lessor argued that it was entitled to judgment as a matter of law because, as an owner of a vehicle leased for a term of more than one year and insured for bodily injury liability in the amount of $ 100,000 per person and $ 300,000 per accident, it was exempted from liability under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a(b)(1). In support of its motion, the lessor submitted a signed and sworn affidavit of its assistant vice president accompanied by a copy of the lease agreement between the lessor and the lessee. The court found that the affidavit with an attached copy of the lease agreement, submitted by the lessor in support of its motion for summery judgment, was sufficient to establish that the lease term was for more than one year and that the leased vehicle was insured for bodily injury liability in amounts of not less than $ 100,000 per person and $ 300,000 per occurrence. Consequently, the lessor was exempted from vicarious liability under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a(b)(1).


OUTCOME: The motion for summary judgment was granted.

 

1330 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Nappe v. E. Haven Bd. of Police Comm'rs


CV054008609


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN AT NEW HAVEN


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1767



April 16, 2007, Decided 
April 16, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Berchem, Moses & Devlin, P.C. v. Town of E. Haven, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 212 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 25, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Nappe v. Town of East Haven, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1678 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 31, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a former police officer (FPO), filed a mandamus action, seeking to compel defendant, a town board of police commissioners, to reinstate him to his former position pursuant to 2004 Conn. Acts 241 and 2005 Conn. Acts 200 (now at Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-294aa). The board claimed that it was not the appropriate entity to grant reinstatement and that the FPO was not entitled to a position as a police officer.


OVERVIEW: The FPO requested a leave of absence from the board in order to serve as a civilian police officer in Iraq. Although the board denied the request and denied reconsideration thereof, the FPO informed the board of his intention to take early retirement in order to serve in Iraq. After his retirement, the FPO was appointed as a supernumerary police officer. Upon his return, his request for reinstatement was not acted upon, and he sought judicial relief. The court held that the board was the proper municipal entity to request reinstatement from, as it was responsible for all appointments to the town police department. The court found that the duty imposed by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-294aa was mandatory, and that it applied to the FPO based on the date that he left his employment with the police department and despite the fact that he received payment for his work in Iraq. Although he took retirement rather than having resigned from his police position, § 7-294aa was applicable to him. The court found that § 7-294aa withstood challenge under Conn. Const. art. 1, § 1, and that the FPO was entitled to reinstatement to his position on the day before he took retirement.


OUTCOME: The court granted the FPO's requested relief and ordered the board to reinstate him to his former position.

 

1331 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Iljazi v. Dugre


CV065002684S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY AT WATERBURY


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 984



April 13, 2007, Decided  
April 13, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff accident victim sued defendants, the operator and the lessor of a rental automobile, for personal injuries sustained in an automobile accident. The lessor of the rental automobile filed a motion to strike the accident victim's vicarious liability count under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a as legally insufficient.


OVERVIEW: The lessor of the rental automobile contended that the Graves Amendment, 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106, barred vicarious liability of an owner engaged in the trade or business of renting or leasing motor vehicles in the absence of negligence or criminal wrongdoing. The accident victim countered that the Graves Amendment violated the Commerce Clause of U.S. Const. art. 1, § 8. The court found that the accident victim did not sustain the burden of proving that the federal statute was unconstitutional. The accident victim alleged that the motor vehicle driven by the operator was a rental automobile, while the lessor of the rental automobile submitted a copy of the rental agreement evidencing its engagement in the business of renting motor vehicles. The accident victim did not plead any negligence or criminal wrongdoing on the part of the lessor of the rental automobile. Accordingly, on the basis of the pleading and the facts alleged, the Graves Amendment barred recovery for vicarious liability against the lessor of the rental automobile.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike the vicarious liability count against the lessor of the rental automobile was granted.

Billie v. Warden


CV030004146S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, GEOGRAPHIC AREA 19 AT ROCKVILLE


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 980



April 13, 2007, Decided  
April 13, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Billie v. Comm'r of Corr., 111 Conn. App. 905, 959 A.2d 1092, 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 557 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Billie, 250 Conn. 172, 738 A.2d 586, 1999 Conn. LEXIS 279 (1999)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed an amended petition, seeking a writ of habeas corpus against respondent warden based on four counts. The warden sought dismissal of two counts and also asserted affirmative defenses. He was convicted of intentional manslaughter under accessory liability as lesser offenses, carrying a pistol without a permit, and commission of a felony with a firearm, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-55(a)(1), 29-35, and 53-202k.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was charged with multiple offenses arising from the shooting deaths of victims who were erroneously believed to be rival gang members. After a jury trial, he was convicted of lesser charges as to murder offenses and of other charges, and he was sentenced to imprisonment. On appeal, the felony conviction under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-202k was vacated. In a prior habeas corpus petition, all claims were denied except as to sentence review, which was restored. However, review thereof resulted in a sentence affirmance. The inmate filed another habeas petition, and dismissal was sought as to ineffective assistance of trial counsel and cumulative error claims. The court found that there was no factual basis for the ineffective assistance claim based on an improper information, and the claim regarding expert testimony was barred by res judicata. There was no relief available for a cumulative error claim based on unspecified allegations against the prosecutor. The affirmative defense of procedural default was inapplicable to the claims of ineffective assistance of appellate counsel and actual innocence. However, the former claim lacked merit and the latter was deemed abandoned.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed two counts of the petition and denied the request for the writ.

 

1333 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Benton v. Benton


FA030733378S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1138



April 5, 2007, Decided 
April 5, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The paternal grandmother and aunt (moving parties) of a child moved for leave, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-57, to intervene in a custody matter and to apply for court-ordered visitation with the minor child. Plaintiff mother, who had sole custody of the child, filed a motion to dismiss those motions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant father's visitation rights had been suspended. However, prior to the suspension, the moving parties had been involved with the child during the father's visitations. They alleged that the father believed their continued visitation was in the child's best interest and that their relationships with the child were close. The court granted the motion to dismiss. Parenting was a fundamental right. Under Roth, basic constitutional protections required that any request for visitation contain factual allegations supporting contentions that a petitioner had a parent-like relationship with a child and that denial of the requested visitation would cause harm to the child parallel to the harm and damage contemplated by the Connecticut neglect and abuse statutes. The best interests of the child was not a standard for judicial consideration. None of the moving parties' pleadings set forth the required jurisdictional allegations. Also, while the memorandum in support of the motions purported to support claims of a "parent like" relationship and harm to the minor child, the facts provided did not suffice to establish a basis for either of the requirements dictated by Roth.


OUTCOME: The mother's motion to dismiss was granted, and consequently, the motions to intervene and for visitation were dismissed.

 

1334 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Sienkiewicz v. Ragaglia


CV030401770S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 834



April 3, 2007, Decided  
April 3, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Sienkiewicz v. Ragaglia, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 501 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 2, 2011)
Related proceeding at Sienkiewicz v. Ragaglia, 2016 Conn. App. LEXIS 330 (Conn. App. Ct., Aug. 1, 2016)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents, individually and on behalf of their sons, filed suit against defendants, employees of a department of children and families (DCF), seeking monetary damages, injunctive relief, and attorneys fees for torts, statutory vexatious litigation, a violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and a violation of their state constitutional rights. Defendants moved to dismiss the suit for a lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The parents argued that in serving the employees, the claims were alleged in the employees' official and individual capacities. The trial court held that the summons did not refer to the employees' job titles, but listed their addresses as "c/o Office of the (Connecticut) Attorney General." Each employee was a state employee. The suit concerned their representation of the State. The State was the real party in interest. Any finding against the employees would effect DCF's procedures. Thus, the employees were sued only in their official capacities. The monetary claims were barred by sovereign immunity as it had not been waived, and the parents did not receive permission to bring their claims. The injunctive relief claims were barred as the allegations did not support the claim that the employees' actions exceeded their authority. The employees were not shielded from liability for money damages for the § 1983 claims. Under federal law, it was possible to read the complaint as seeking monetary damages against the employees as individuals. Finally, the injunctive relief claim under § 1983 was barred as only the State could provide the relief sought: that DCF expunge its records.


OUTCOME: The employees' motion to dismiss was granted as to all of the parents' claims except for their claims for monetary damages under § 1983.

 

1335 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


In re Melody L.


H12CP02008534A


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, CHILD PROTECTION SESSION AT MIDDLETOWN


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 840



March 30, 2007, Decided  
March 30, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: In re Melody L., 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 841 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 30, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court (Connecticut) terminated a mother's parental rights. Even though the commissioner of children and families voluntarily continued to provide visitation to the mother, the children moved to continue visits with their mother while the mother appealed the termination of her parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The children argued that their visitation with the mother should continue. The trial court held that the attorney for the children did not allege any special need, reason, or circumstance that would require a continuation of visitation. Further, there was not an automatic stay of the termination of parental rights decision as there was a clear policy determination that the status quo was not automatically expected to remain in place pending any appeal. The motions to stay filed by the mother and the children had been denied. Even assuming that the children could utilize Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-59 as a basis on which to seek continuation of visitation with their mother, any visitation order entered after the termination of the mother's parental rights would be inconsistent with such termination. The purpose of a termination of parental rights was to vest legal authority over the children with the statutory parent or the guardians and to grant such entities or individuals the right to make decisions about the children's future life and their contact with others.


OUTCOME: The children's motion for visitation was denied.

Kuehl v. Koskoff

The law firm and attorneys moved to enforce a purported settlement agreement.

The trial court denied the motion upon concluding that the supposed agreement was not clear and unambiguous because the attorneys and law firm believed that it went into effect when she was allowed to file her claim, but she contended that she had to obtain a hearing on the merits.

Brodach Builders, Inc. v. Town of Cheshire


CV064017472S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 775



March 15, 2007, Decided  
March 15, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an owner and purchasers, applied for final design approval of a feasibility plan for the construction of a sanitary sewer system. Defendant water pollution control authority approved the plan. The authority adopted an amendment to its regulations that provided that no application for the extension of sanitary sewers should be granted for plaintiffs' property. Plaintiffs brought an administrative appeal. The authority moved to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The authority argued that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction because there was no statutory right to appeal from a decision by the authority to amend its regulations. The right to take an appeal from Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-247 actions by a water pollution control authority only applied to certain actions under that statute. The court found that the authority's decision to amend its regulations did not fall within any of the categories for which an appeal could have been brought under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-246a. Plaintiffs, in their opposition to the motion, catalogued their grievances against the process surrounding their feasibility plan for the construction of a sanitary sewage system. Monies were spent on the supposition that the project would have been approved based on what were claimed to be misleading actions by the authority. By adopting the regulation, there was a functional equivalent of a denial of the application. Therefore, an unconstitutional taking was perpetrated. However, assuming all of this was true, no appeal was statutorily provided from the authority's action in amending its regulations so the court had no jurisdiction to hear the purported appeal.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted.

 

1338 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Adams v. Korta


CV055000226S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 686



March 12, 2007, Decided  
March 13, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff pedestrian filed a two-count complaint against the commissioner of transportation (commissioner) alleging that he breached his statutory duty pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-144 by not keeping the street safe for public use after she slipped and fell on snow and ice which had accumulated on a private driveway. The commissioner moved to dismiss count one of the complaint on sovereign immunity grounds. This matter followed.


OVERVIEW: Upon a review of the facts, the court noted that presumptively, the commissioner was protected under the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The pedestrian was thus required to show that the commissioner had a duty to keep the driveway she was injured on in repair, but she failed to do so. Despite this, she argued that the commissioner was subject to suit under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-144 because the Department of Transportation (DOT) was maintaining the driveway. But, she cited no authority for the proposition that an agreement with a private entity could create a duty sufficient to trigger § 13a-144. Further, a DOT district maintenance director stated that the driveway was not part of the state highway system. Moreover, because § 13a-144 was an exception to sovereign immunity and was to be construed strictly in favor of the state, the fact that the DOT agreed to maintain a privately-owned driveway did not create a legal duty.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss count one was granted.

 

1339 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Turgeon v. Town of E. Lyme


054002613


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 690



March 9, 2007, Decided  
March 9, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner filed an administrative appeal under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-43 against defendants, the East Lyme Conservation Commission (Connecticut), the Town of East Lyme, and the Connecticut Department of Environmental Protection, after the Commission denied plaintiff's application to conduct regulated activities on a residential lot containing wetlands.


OVERVIEW: The court first held that the Commission's denial of the application was not capricious, unreasonable, and inconsistent with the regulations. The denial was, however, an unlawful taking in violation of the Fifth Amendment and Conn. Const. art. I. The record supported the Commission's finding that no feasible and prudent alternative existed that would allow plaintiff to construct a building on his lot, and the Commission's denial of the application established the requisite finality to assert a takings claim. Plaintiff had a reasonable investment-backed expectation of development for this property. He had bought other wetland lots and developed them; the lot here was zoned for a residential lot; and houses had been built on smaller lots within the same neighborhood. There had been a practical confiscation of the land because it could be used only in its natural state. The Commission's decision also resulted in a taking under the balancing test. The wetlands here were of poor to fair quality, and surrounding properties were already developed. Thus, the public benefit was not strong enough to outweigh the harm to plaintiff that would result from the denial of the application.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the appeal. Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-43a(a), it remanded the application to the Commission for it to approve the application with such conditions as it found reasonably necessary to protect the wetlands on and adjacent to the site.

 

1340 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Helenese v. Allstate Ins. Co.


FSTCV065001076S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK AT STAMFORD


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 623



March 7, 2007, Decided  
March 7, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs lessee and driver of a motor vehicle brought an action against defendants insurer and state insurance department, seeking damages arising out of a traffic accident involving the vehicle. The state insurance department moved to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The state insurance department argued that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction because, inter alia, the claim was barred by sovereign immunity. The court found, however, that the most cogent reason for a finding of lack of jurisdiction was the lack of justiciability. The lessee and the driver conceded that they were not seeking liability from the state insurance department. The lessee and the driver admitted there was no real controversy or adversity between them and the state insurance department. The only reason for involving the state insurance department was to explain why none of its employees had not supported the lessee and the driver in their claims against the insurer. This was not a basis for a claim. Even assuming that the matter was justiciable, the claim was barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The lessee and the driver neither alleged nor argued that the legislature statutorily waived sovereign immunity, and failed to allege or argue that the state insurance department acted in excess of statutory authority, or pursuant to an unconstitutional statute. The lessee and the driver did not refer to the state insurance department in their complaint.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted.

 

1341 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Waterbury City Emples. Ass'n v. WFPAB


CV064010047S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 503



February 22, 2007, Decided  
February 22, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the Waterbury City Employees Association (the Union), moved to vacate an arbitration award imposed by defendant, Waterbury Financial Planning and Assistance Board (the Board), on the Union and defendant, the City of Waterbury. The award was issued, pursuant to 2001 Conn. Spec. Acts 01-1 (the Act), which was enacted in response to a fiscal crisis facing the City. The award resolved a labor relations dispute.


OVERVIEW: The Union requested the court to find that the Board, sitting as the arbitrator of the labor relations dispute, pursuant to the Act, issued the award in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-418 and common law principles. The court rejected the union's claim that the powers granted to the Board were unconstitutionally over broad. The court found that the Connecticut Legislature clearly stated the public policy behind the Act and properly laid down an intelligible principle and standard for the Board to follow that was reasonable and appropriate to the circumstances and necessary to fulfill the urgent and legitimate governmental purpose of restoring financial stability to the City. The court determined that the Union failed to meet its burden to show that there was any basis for vacating the award since the Union received proper notice of the issues as well as was provided multiple opportunities to present evidence in opposition. The court further found that the Union failed to show any well defined, explicit, and dominant public policy that the Board violated as well as failed to show any impermissible delegation of authority.


OUTCOME: The court denied the Union's application to vacate the award.
