Stone v. Comm'r of Revenue Servs.


CV044001070S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN, TAX SESSION AT NEW BRITAIN


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 288



February 7, 2007, Decided  
February 7, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer filed an appeal contesting the decisions of defendant commissioner that disallowed the taxpayer's deduction of gambling winnings and the imposition of additional income tax assessments against the taxpayer for the two taxable years at issue.


OVERVIEW: During most of the taxable years at issue, the taxpayer was a full-time salaried employee until he retired towards the end of the second taxable year at issue. He was also the sole proprietor of a part-time seasonal business. Moreover, he owned and managed commercial income-producing real estate. The taxpayer claimed to be a professional gambler, that is, a person who was in the trade or business of gambling, and so indicated on the federal tax forms he filed during the taxable years at issue. However, during the first taxable year he only played the slot machines for a total of 43 days; for the second taxable year, he only played the slot machines for a total of 22 days. On his state income tax forms for the two taxable years at issue, he reported his federal adjusted gross income for each respective year. The commissioner disallowed the taxpayer's deduction of gambling losses against gambling winnings for the two taxable years at issue, and imposed additional income tax assessments against him for each of those years. On his appeal, the trial court found that his gambling activities for the two years did not constitute a "trade or business" permitting the deductions he sought.


OUTCOME: The trial court entered judgment for the commissioner denying the taxpayer's appeal for the taxable years at issue.

 

1343 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Shelton Yacht & Cabana Club, Inc. v. Voccola


CV010075380S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF ANSONIA-MILFORD AT MILFORD


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2402



January 30, 2007, Decided 
February 2, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a country club and sole stockholder, filed a revised complaint eventually containing six counts and alleged that defendants, a police chief, two police officers, and city violated their constitutional rights, intentionally inflicted emotional distress on the sole stockholder, committed an abuse of process, and acted negligently in attempting to drive the country club out of business. They moved for summary judgment as to all counts.


OVERVIEW: The country club and sole stockholder believed that there existed a policy of the city and its police department to harass the operation of the country club and to drive it out of business. To pursue that policy, they believed, the city, police chief, and two police officers either engaged in or allowed excessive or harassing police enforcement activity, as well as institution of a public nuisance action. The country club and sole stockholder filed a revised complaint. They alleged actions pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 that asserted their federal free speech and assembly rights, and their equal protection rights had been violated, that the conduct intentionally inflicted emotional distress on the sole stockholder, that an abuse of process was committed, and that negligent acts were performed. The city, police chief, and two police officers moved for summary judgment. The trial court found that the sole stockholder had not shown sufficiently severe conduct to prevent entry of summary judgment on the intentional infliction claim, but also found that the city, police chief, and two police officers had not submitted sufficient to preclude summary judgment as to the other claims.


OUTCOME: The trial court granted the motion for summary judgment filed by the police chief, two police officers, and city as to the country club and sole stockholder's revised compliant, count four, alleging intentional infliction of emotional distress. It denied the motion as to the remaining five counts of the revised complaint.

 

1344 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Lopes v. Farmer


CV054008743


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 250



January 29, 2007, Decided  
January 29, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Y'Isiah v. Farmer, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 127 (Conn., Apr. 15, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a school resource officer and another police officer, filed a motion for summary judgment in the malicious prosecution action filed by plaintiff substitute teacher as a result of his arrest for allegedly stalking defendant student.


OVERVIEW: In November 2000, the student went to the resource officer, stating that a person later identified as the teacher had been stalking and threatening her. The same allegation was made to the other officer. The teacher was arrested, however, all of the charges against him were dismissed in July 2002. The teacher filed suit in April 2005. The officers argued that they were entitled to summary judgment because the statute of limitations had run. The court agreed. In addition to is malicious prosecution claim, the teacher claimed a violation of his Fourth Amendment rights via a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action. The general tort statute of limitations found at Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-277 applied to both actions. Contrary to the teacher's assertion, the three-year statute of limitations began to run on the date that the last acts committed by the officers concerning the teacher's arrest were completed and not on the date that the criminal prosecution ended in his favor. The last actions by the officers occurred in November 2000. Thus, the teacher's April 2005 action against them was untimely.


OUTCOME: The court granted the officers' motion for summary judgment.

 

1345 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. Rell


HHDCV054014739


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 267



January 29, 2007, Decided  
January 29, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state prisoner filed a complaint against defendant government representatives alleging violations of multiple laws, statutory and constitutional, related to the resources allocated to deciding claims that he had filed and the administration of the judicial system. The government representatives filed a motion to dismiss asserting statutory, sovereign, and judicial immunity, as well as insufficiency of service of process.


OVERVIEW: The state prisoner filed a complaint in the trial court against the government representatives alleging that he has two habeas corpus cases, and several petitions, pending before the trial court judges that have not been resolved. He also alleged that the government representatives had not assigned enough judges to pending habeas corpus petitions, that they wilfully underfunded both the court system and the public defender's office, and that they created and maintained a policy depriving the state prisoner of prompt resolutions to his claims. The state prisoner claimed that the alleged conduct violated his rights under state and federal constitutional law, and state statutes. The trial court granted the government representatives' motion to dismiss. It found that the government representatives in their individual capacities had not been served with process. It then found that the remaining claims against the government representatives in their official capacities were against the State, that the state prisoner had not followed the proper approach pursuant to statute for suing the State, and that the State had not consented to be sued.


OUTCOME: The trial court granted the government representatives' motion to dismiss as to all claims against all government representatives in all capacities.

 

1346 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Danso v. Univ. of Conn.


CV-06 4006110S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


50 Conn. Supp. 256; 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 191; 919 A.2d 1100



January 17, 2007, Decided  
January 17, 2007, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Application Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a student, applied for a temporary injunction requiring respondent, a university, to reinstate the student as a full-time student in good standing at the university.


OVERVIEW: The student was suspended as a result of stalking, intimidation, and threatening of a female student. The court concluded that both the notice and hearing procedures employed by the university with respect to the suspension satisfied the minimum requirements of procedural due process and that the student failed to show that he was substantially prejudiced by these procedures. The university sent the student a letter notifying him of the date of the hearing. The student never complained at the hearing that evidence of multiple incidents concerning the female student was a surprise or caused him to be unprepared to defend himself. The court found that the student knew what claims had been made against him by virtue of two letters and a conference with a university official. The court further held that the admission of hearsay evidence at the hearing did not constitute a violation of due process, as due process did not require that a student at a disciplinary hearing be afforded a right to cross-examine witnesses or compel testimony. The court further held that evidence of earlier incidents was properly admitted to add context and for the purpose of assessing adequate sanctions.


OUTCOME: The motion for a temporary injunction was denied.

 

1347 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Greater New Haven Prop. Owners Ass'n v. City of New Haven


CV064020494S, Opinion No.: 96756


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 156



January 17, 2007, Decided  
January 17, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Greater New Haven Prop. Owners Ass'n v. City of New Haven, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 295 (Conn., July 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Greater New Haven Prop. Owners Ass'n v. City of New Haven, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2625 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 24, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a voluntary association representing owners and managers of residential rental properties, filed an action against defendant city in which plaintiff challenged the city's Residential Rental Property Licensing and Inspection ordinance. Plaintiff, which sought declaratory and injunctive relief, argued that the ordinance violated statutory and constitutional law.


OVERVIEW: The court first held that the ordinance did not conflict with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-148(c). The legislature had purposefully used broad and general terms to allow municipalities to address safety, health, morals, and general welfare issues. The ordinance did not conflict with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 47a-57. The city had not adopted the provisions of the statute; furthermore, the ordinance did not conflict with the statute, but complemented it. The ordinance did not violate procedural due process under the Fourteenth Amendment or Conn. Const. art. I, § 8. Even if there was a property interest in certificates of occupancy and other permits, the ordinance contained an appeals provision. The ordinance did not violate substantive due process. Plaintiff had not shown that the regulations were unreasonable. As for equal protection under the Fourteenth Amendment and Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 1 and 20, exempting certain properties allowed the city to allocate its limited resources to property most likely to be susceptible to health, safety and building violations. Finally, the licensing fees were reasonably proportionate to the cost of administration and were not a unconstitutional tax.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment in favor of defendant.

 

1348 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Newlan v. State


X04CV020103313S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET, AT MIDDLETOWN


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 94



January 16, 2007, Decided  
January 16, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administratrix sued defendant State alleging that prison medical, administrative, and service providers were deliberately indifferent in their care of decedent, a pretrial detainee, in violation of U.S. Const. amend. VIII and XIV. The administratrix also alleged negligence and violations of the patients' bill of rights, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-540 et seq. The State moved for summary judgment on all but the negligence claims.


OVERVIEW: The decedent hanged himself while in an infirmary cell of a correctional facility. He died despite the efforts of medical personnel, who asserted that, in taking the decedent off suicide watch, they considered his risk of suicide. The facts, mostly not disputed, regarding the actions of each defendant who was directly involved in the decedent's treatment, taken together, indicated that, while there may have been questions regarding standard of care, defendants did not act with deliberate indifference with respect to their treatment of the decedent in violation of his Eighth and Fourteenth Amendment rights. Because the decedent's constitutionally protected rights were not violated, in that he was not treated with deliberate indifference to his health and safety needs, thee defendants who did not directly deal with him were not subject to supervisory or policy-making liability under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. No defendants were liable under the patients' bill of rights, which did not apply to prisons.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment was entered in favor of defendants on all but the negligence count.

 

1349 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Ware v. State


CV064023567S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 115



January 16, 2007, Decided  
January 16, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument granted by Ware v. State, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 825 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 22, 2007)
Reversed by, Remanded by Ware v. State, 118 Conn. App. 65, 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 501 (2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former state employee filed an action for wrongful termination of employment against defendant State of Connecticut. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the complaint, primarily on grounds of sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff in her first count alleged that she had been treated as a temporary employee in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 5-196, 5-236, and 5-239. The court stated that by codifying the State's obligations to its employees under these statutes, the legislature had waived sovereign immunity, at least by necessary implication. Furthermore, plaintiff's allegation that defendant had violated these statutes necessarily implied that the State had acted in excess of its statutory authority. As for the second count, alleging employment discrimination in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-60, the State was an employer under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-51(10). Sovereign immunity did not apply. Furthermore, plaintiff had exhausted her administrative remedies under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-100. The court also declined to dismiss plaintiff's punitive damages claim, as the language of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-104 was sufficiently broad to include punitive damages. Finally, in plaintiff's contract claims, she sought reinstatement, which the court construed as seeking injunctive relief. The State could not use sovereign immunity as a defense in an action for declaratory and injunctive relief.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss.

 

1350 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Burgess v. State


File Nos. CV-03 0520679S, CV-03 0520681S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


50 Conn. Supp. 271; 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 55; 920 A.2d 383



January 8, 2007, Decided  
January 8, 2007, Memorandum filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected April 17, 2007.
Motion to strike denied by Piotrowski v. State, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1675 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 1, 2008)
Motion to strike denied by Burgess v. State, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1760 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 7, 2008)
Judgment entered by Burgess v. State, 52 Conn. Supp. 562, 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2068 (Conn. Super. Ct., 2012)



DISPOSITION: Motions granted in part and denied in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hikers filed claims with the Connecticut Claims Commissioner that were denied. The Connecticut legislature granted the hikers permission to sue the State. The hikers filed suit alleging negligence, willful negligence, willful and malicious conduct, and nuisance. The State moved to dismiss the counts alleging willful misconduct and nuisance.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the Commissioner had authority to grant permission to sue only for simple negligence and that the legislature could not do more than that. The trial court held that as the Commissioner had authority to grant permission to sue for intentional torts and suits alleging negligence, the Commissioner could grant permission to sue for conduct that fell in between. Thus, the Commissioner could grant permission to sue for willful and malicious actions. The legislature had the same authority to grant permission to sue as did the Commissioner, and the resolution authorized the hikers to raise the willfulness claims that they presented to the Commissioner. The State could raise recreational use immunity if a private person could do so. Further, if the actions of any state employee were willful and malicious so as to constitute acts beyond the scope of their employment, the State would not be liable under respondeat superior. The hikers alleged willful and malicious behavior and negligence in their claims, but did not mention nuisance. As neither the claims nor the resolution mentioned nuisance, the legislature did not waive sovereign immunity for the nuisance claims.


OUTCOME: The motions to dismiss were granted with respect to the nuisance claims. The motions to dismiss were denied in all other respects.

 

1351 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Jacewicz v. DeFilippo


CV044001582


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 43



January 5, 2007, Decided  
January 5, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Jacewicz v. DeFilippo, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 379 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 7, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff motorist filed a declaratory judgment action pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-175 and Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 17-54 against defendant, the Commissioner of the Connecticut Department of Motor Vehicles, seeking a determination that the manner in which the Department implemented motor vehicle operators' license suspensions under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 14-227a and 14-227b which arose from the same incident was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The motorist was arrested for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of alcohol or drugs, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a. Due to a finding that the motorist had refused to submit to a blood alcohol test, his license was administratively suspended for a period of time pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227b(i). After that suspension was fully served, the motorist was convicted of a criminal offense arising from the same incident. The Department imposed a criminal license suspension under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a(g). The Department refused the motorist's request for "credit" for the administrative suspension period. On review of the motorist's claims, the court found that the motorist was not similarly situated to motorists who were serving one suspension when the other was imposed. Accordingly, the equal protection argument under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Conn. Const. art. I, § 20 failed. The motorist's due process claims under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Conn. Const. art. I, § 8 also failed, as he was given notice prior to the administrative suspension, and the criminal suspension was imposed in accordance with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a.


OUTCOME: The motorist's request for a declaratory judgment was denied, and the court entered judgment in favor of the Commissioner.

Sheff v. O'Neill


X07CV890492119S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 44



January 4, 2007, Decided  
January 4, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff aggrieved parties and defendant school representatives entered an agreement covering certain school years that had the main goal of improving the educational experience for the aggrieved parties, who mainly were public school minority students residing in or near intervenor applicant city. After it appeared the agreement's goals were not being met, the city filed a motion to intervene.


OVERVIEW: The state supreme court 10 years earlier issued an opinion declaring that a school districting program as applied to the aggrieved parties violated their state constitutional rights by abridging their fundamental right to a substantially equal educational opportunity that was free from substantial racial and ethnic isolation. The trial court directed the legislative and executive branches to put the search for appropriate remedial measures at the top of their respective agendas. A few years later, the aggrieved parties sought further judicial assistance. The result was an agreement covering four school years, which set forth certain goals for improving the educational process. The agreement reached its last year, the goals were apparently not being met, and the parties were involved in further negotiations. The city moved to intervene. The trial court looked to the pleadings and accepted the allegations as true. It then found that the city had substantial interests in almost every aspect of the case and, as a result, it had to be made a party to the case.


OUTCOME: The trial court granted the city's motion to intervene.

 

1353 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Townsend v. Rell


CV0604024457


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3863



December 29, 2006, Decided  
December 29, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate filed a pro se 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action against defendants, the governor, the chairman of the Board of Pardons and Paroles, and various other individuals, in which plaintiff challenged the denial of his application for a pardon. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, who was serving a 60-year sentence for murder, argued that the Board, which had not stated a reason for denying his application for a pardon, was required to articulate the specific criteria for obtaining a pardon. He also claimed that the Board granted pardons disproportionately to white inmates. The court noted that the United States Supreme Court had stated that pardon and commutation decisions were rarely, if ever, appropriate subjects for judicial review. A decision whether to commute a long-term sentence depended not only on objective fact-finding, but on purely subjective evaluations and on predictions of future behavior. Plaintiff here sought information on how the Board operated in making pardon decisions and requested that the Board grant him a pardon. The court lacked the ability to substitute its judgment for that of the Board when it made decisions on whom might be granted a pardon. Accordingly, the action would be dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motion to dismiss.

 

1354 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Oakbridge Holdings, LLC v. Town of Seymour


CV064005491S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF ANSONIA - MILFORD, AT DERBY


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3843



December 22, 2006, Decided  
December 27, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff developer filed an application with defendant town inland wetlands commission to obtain approval for the construction of a commercial and office building. The town inland wetlands commission effectively voted to deny the application. The developer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The developer wanted to develop the land at a certain location. It entered into an agreement to purchase the tract conditioned upon obtaining approval for the construction of a commercial and office building. The developer filed an application with the town inland wetlands commission to obtain approval for the contemplated construction as set out in several site plans as submitted to the town inland wetlands commission. The town inland wetlands commission vote to deny the application did not carry, and, thus, the application was effectively denied. The developer appealed and claimed that the town inland wetlands commission failed to state a reason for its denial and ignored expert evidence presented by the developer which indicated that the proposed construction would have no harmful effect on the existing wetlands. The trial court, in reviewing the record before it, concluded that the record as a whole adequately supported the town inland wetlands commission's action in ruling upon the application and, thus, found that the appeal had to be dismissed.


OUTCOME: The trial court dismissed the appeal.

 

1355 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Vasquez v. Comm'r of Corr.


CV040004441


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT SOMERS


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3774



December 15, 2006, Decided  
December 15, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Vazquez v. Comm'r of Corr., 944 A.2d 429, 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 154 (Conn. App. Ct., Apr. 22, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Vazquez, 87 Conn. App. 792, 867 A.2d 15, 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 89 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, an inmate, filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, alleging that his conviction of robbery in the first degree and the resultant sentence was defective under both the United States Constitution and the Constitution of the State of Connecticut and that as a result he was entitled to have his convictions and sentence set aside.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that his trial counsel rendered ineffective assistance by failing to raise a potential alibi defense at the inmate's trial. Given that the police did not recover the gun used in the robbery, the case hinged upon the identification of the inmate as the perpetrator by the victim. The inmate claimed that he was asleep in his apartment with his girlfriend at the time the robbery occurred. The court found that no evidence had been presented to undermine the credibility of the inmate or his girlfriend as to the claimed alibi. Given the significance of this potential alibi testimony and its propensity to induce reasonable doubt in the minds of the jury, the court found that the reliability of the inmate's conviction had been undermined and that the inmate thus satisfied the prejudice prong of the Strickland test for ineffective assistance of counsel. The court held that defense counsel clearly should have called the inmate and his girlfriend in order to establish an alibi defense that might well have led a jury to find reasonable doubt as to the inmate's guilt. The jury members were entitled to hear this testimony before they made the finding of guilty.


OUTCOME: The petition was granted, the verdict was set aside, and the inmate was granted a new trial.

 

1356 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Conde v. Warden


CV030348408S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DANBURY, AT DANBURY


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3776



December 14, 2006, Decided  
December 14, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Conde v. Comm'r of Corr., 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 37 (Conn. App. Ct., Feb. 3, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Conde, 67 Conn. App. 474, 787 A.2d 571, 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 643 (2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, petitioner prisoner, who was convicted of murder and conspiracy to commit murder, claimed that his court-appointed lawyer was ineffective so that he was denied his right to the effective assistance of counsel and to due process of law. He argued, inter alia, that counsel did not object to his being tried in leg irons and did not file a petition for sentence review. The conviction had been affirmed.


OVERVIEW: The victim, who was a member of a gang, was shot by three men. The prisoner was the president of the gang. A witness was present at a meeting where two other gang members expressed anger to the prisoner. The prisoner, who was also angry at the victim, told the members to kill the victim. The prisoner confided to another witness that he was involved in the murder. The court held that defense counsel's actions were based quite properly on information supplied by the prisoner. There was no evidence presented that the prisoner ever informed his trial defense counsel that the victim was not a gang member. Thus, there was no reason for defense counsel to have asked the State's witnesses that question. Further, defense counsel made the strategic choice of attempting to convince the jury that the meeting had not taken place. The court found that under all the circumstances the prisoner failed to rebut the presumption that such action was sound trial strategy. There was no credible evidence presented that trial defense counsel could have done anything to have the shackles removed. However, the prisoner was denied his right to have his sentence reviewed by the Sentence Review Division.


OUTCOME: All of the prisoner's claims under the writ of habeas corpus other than the claim regarding sentence review were dismissed. The prisoner was restored his right to apply for sentence review.

 

1357 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Conklin v. Estate of Depino


CV054013792S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3730



December 11, 2006, Decided  
December 11, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion for summary judgment granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant estate filed a motion for summary judgment, seeking to dismiss the negligence suit brought by plaintiff, an injured woman. The single count complaint alleged that plaintiff sustained injuries in a motor vehicle collision with defendant's decedent. Defendant's decedent died nine days before the statute of limitations to bring a claim of negligence against him would have expired.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff's complaint was commenced on August 5, 2005, by service of process and alleged that on March 23, 2001, defendant's decedent negligently drove through a red light, striking plaintiff's vehicle in an intersection through which plaintiff was lawfully driving. As a result of the collision, plaintiff alleged that she sustained various injuries causing her pain and requiring medical care. Defendant's decedent died on March 14, 2003. In February 2004, the estate was opened. Plaintiff presented the estate attorney with written notification of her claim on February 4, 2004. Defendant filed its motion, claiming plaintiff did not file her claim within the applicable statute of limitations. Plaintiff relied on the notice to defendant's counsel apprising him of the claim and that the same was never rejected. The court examined the relevant statutes and held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-375(c) limited the time period for the tolling of a case to two years from the date of the decedent's death. Even viewing the facts in a light most favorable to plaintiff, her suit was still outside the provision of § 45a-375(c).


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's motion for summary judgment.

 

1358 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Health Net v. Freedom of Info. Comm'n


CV064010428S, CV064010429S, CV064010430S, CV064009521S, CV064009522S, CV064009534S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3589



November 29, 2006, Decided  
November 29, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Complainants sought certain records from plaintiff contractors, which had entered into agreements with the Connecticut Department of Social Services (DSS) under the Freedom of Information Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-200 et seq. The Freedom of Information Commission (Connecticut) ordered DSS to obtain the records from the contractors and to provide them to the complainants. The contractors appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under their agreements with DSS, the contractors provided health care to Medicaid and public assistance recipients. The contractors argued that the records were not subject to disclosure because they did not perform a governmental function under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-218. The court held that the contractors' managed care operations were "programs" of DSS under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-200(11). The division of care among the contractors was not a bar to each of their operations constituting a program. Furthermore, although some management decisions were left to DSS, the contractors retained authority over provider fees; thus, they made high-level decisions and "administered or managed" their operations. Because the establishment of provider fees, preferred drug lists, and prior approval lists involved a high level of decision-making by a contractor, those matters were subject to disclosure. Next, the court rejected the contractors' argument that in ordering amendments to their contracts with the DSS, the Commission had violated the Commerce Clause. There could be no violation of the Contracts Clause when a party had contracted to be bound by subsequent extracontractual decisions.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeals.

 

1359 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Carmon v. Warden


CV030474044S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3465



November 14, 2006, Decided  
November 14, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Carmon v. Comm'r of Corr., 114 Conn. App. 484, 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 191 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Carmon, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2126 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 24, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner was convicted in connection with the shooting of a grandmother and the killing of her seven-month-old granddaughter. The prisoner's convictions were upheld on appeal. The prisoner then filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, which was denied. Subsequently, the prisoner filed a second petition for writ of habeas corpus. Respondent warden filed a return.


OVERVIEW: The petition raised claims of ineffective assistance of trial counsel, ineffective assistance of counsel with respect to his first habeas corpus petition, and "actual innocence." The prisoner asserted that trial counsel was ineffective, inter alia, in failing to properly investigate certain fingerprint evidence. However, in rejecting that argument, the court held that it was sheer speculation that effective counsel could have used the prints. In addition, trial counsel was not ineffective in any other manner, including by his failure to object to an identification and his failure to object to comments by the prosecutor, which were not of such a nature as to have caused a denial of due process. Further, although the prisoner was entitled, pursuant to his right to file a habeas corpus proceeding under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-296, to raise the issue of ineffective assistance of habeas corpus counsel, his claim failed because the prisoner had failed, as a threshold matter, to show that his trial counsel's representation was ineffective. Further, the petition fell far short of the meeting the burden required to establish "actual innocence" as a basis for granting the writ.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

 

1360 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Rizzi v. Inland Wetlands & Watercourses Comm'n of Winchester


LLICV064004257


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD, AT LITCHFIELD


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3312



November 8, 2006, Decided  
November 8, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-43, plaintiff property owner appealed a decision of defendant, Inland Wetlands and Watercourses Commission (IWWC) (Connecticut), which denied the owner's application for an exception under Winchester, Conn., Ord. 162 to install an aluminum dock on a strip of his waterfront property.


OVERVIEW: The owner claimed that a dock had previously existed on the property, establishing a pre-existing use. The court denied the appeal, finding that the owner improperly attempted to bring a declaratory judgment action with his statutory appeal under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-43. Further, there was strong evidence that the drafters of the ordinance intended that only those docks available for use on the ordinance's effective date were deemed authorized. There was no evidence that the owner's aluminum dock was installed on the effective date. Additionally, the court found that the due process and equal protection arguments were not fully briefed because they were unaccompanied either by legal analysis or citation to authority. No constitutional due process rights existed, and the only requirement in administrative proceedings was that the conduct of the hearing should not violate the fundamentals of natural justice. Finally, the court found that the decision of the IWWC was not clearly erroneous under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-183(j). There was substantial evidence to show that the proposed dock would be a navigational hazard, impede navigation, or impede ingress and egress from the shore.


OUTCOME: The court denied the appeal.

 

1361 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Kubera v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals


CV054002290S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3234



October 30, 2006, Decided  
October 30, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed a decision of defendant Zoning Board of Appeals of the Town of Old Saybrook (Connecticut), in which the Board denied the owners' request for certain variances.


OVERVIEW: The owners requested variances with respect to lot size and setback from side property lines. The reviewing court held that the owners were aggrieved. Service complied with the statutory prerequisites. The denial of the variances did not amount to a confiscation. The property had uses other than for a single family home. Ownership of the property entitled the owners to membership in a beach club and access to a beach area that the general public was prohibited from using. Many people had purchased permanently vacant lots for the sole purpose of gaining beach rights. Thus, the property had value to potential purchasers. Additionally, the property could be used as a side yard to one of the three adjoining lots. The owners purchased the property due to anticipated ownership of an adjoining lot. Although the owners never gained complete ownership of the adjoining lot, their initial interest in the property was indicative of potential value to other adjoining landowners. The owners also did not show that they would be unsuccessful in selling their property to an abutting landowner. The Board acted within its discretion and based on the evidence before it when it denied the variances.


OUTCOME: The owners' appeal was dismissed.

 

1362 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


DaimlerChrysler Corp. v. Law


CV054007725S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN, TAX SESSION AT NEW BRITAIN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3191



October 25, 2006, Decided  
October 25, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by DaimlerChrysler Corp. v. Law, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 509 (Conn., Dec. 18, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: DaimlerChrysler Corp. v. Law, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1718 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 9, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff vehicle manufacturer filed a tax appeal under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 12-422 and 12-425, seeking a refund of sales taxes that it allegedly paid to consumers as required by the Lemon Law, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-179 et seq. Defendant Connecticut Commissioner of Revenue Services filed a motion for dismissal of the action on the basis of sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: The manufacturer sought a refund of sales taxes paid under the Lemon Law, which was disallowed based on the lack of statutory authority. An administrative appeal resulted in an affirmance of the disallowance, as the vehicle sales were completed transactions that were properly subjected to sales tax. The manufacturer sought judicial review, and the Commissioner sought dismissal of the action based on lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The manufacturer alleged that the Commissioner's failure to have asserted sovereign immunity as an affirmative defense pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. §§ 10-31 and 10-32 constituted a waiver thereof. The court initially noted that Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 10-33 was the appropriate rule regarding dismissal. The manufacturer was not a taxpayer under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 12-418, 12-421, and 12-425, as it did not pay the sales tax. Further, it was statutorily responsible for reimbursing the consumers for the tax and accordingly, there were no constitutional violations. As the State had not waived sovereign immunity and there were no constitutional violations, dismissal was proper.


OUTCOME: The court granted the Commissioner's motion to dismiss the action.

 

1363 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


S.D. Williams, LLC v. Town of Coventry Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV054003940S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3228



October 23, 2006, Decided  
October 23, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a limited liability company and the company's principal and sole member, appealed from the decision of defendant, the planning and zoning commission of a town, which denied an application to resubdivide a 13.6-acre lot that had been modified pursuant to a lot line revision.


OVERVIEW: The commission denied the application on the ground that it failed to comply with the open space design provisions of the town subdivision regulations. Plaintiffs argued that the denial violated the commission's powers because each of the six proposed lots complied with the applicable subdivision regulations. Town of Coventry, Conn., Zoning Regs. 20.4(2) stated that an open space subdivision consisted of a parcel or parcels of land containing no less than a total of 15 contiguous acres. It was uncontested that the commission had approved a lot line revision on the property. Hence, under the modified subdivision plan, the lot in question was a 13.6-acre parcel. Thus, the court held that the lot in question did not meet the open space general eligibility requirements because substantial evidence in the record showed that the lot contained less than 15 contiguous acres. Because the record did not contain substantial evidence demonstrating that plaintiffs' application for resubdivision was subject to the open space design requirements, the court found that the reasons for the commission's denial were unreasonable, arbitrary, and illegal.


OUTCOME: The appeal was sustained, and the denial of the subdivision application was reversed.

 

1364 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Halibozek


CR05200065


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 12 AT MANCHESTER


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3939



October 20, 2006, Decided


NOTICE: THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved to dismiss a charge of risk of injury in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 against him in that the count as applied was unconstitutionally vague. The motion was reviewed under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 41-8(8).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was swearing in front of children at a wedding, throwing beer bottles at the wedding cake, and asking the children to follow him outside to take "shots" of alcohol. The children included a nine-year-old child (child). The trial court held that defendant was not the child's parent, guardian, or spouse. Published judicial opinions gave fair warning to defendant that his conduct was prohibited. The fact that the child did not accept the delivery of the alcoholic beverage from defendant did not distinguish prior cases. The intent for required under § 53-21 was the general intent to do that which the law prohibited, or the intent to cause or permit a situation to arise that was likely to injure the health or impair the morals of a child under the age of 16. A specific intent to cause harm to the victim was not an element of the offense. While it was assumed that serving alcoholic beverages to a minor was customary in certain religious services, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 30-86(b), such service or delivery had to be made by a parent, guardian, or spouse of the child. Section 53-21, as applied, gave fair warning to defendant that his actions violated the law.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1365 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Foran


HHBCR040216603


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3007



October 5, 2006, Decided  
October 6, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved the court to suppress the evidence seized from his residence during the execution of a search warrant. Defendant was charged with three counts of risk of injury to a child, two counts of promoting a minor in an obscene performance, and over 100 counts of possession of child pornography.


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendant arose from photographs and conduct he engaged in with his 12-year-old former sister-in-law. Defendant asserted that the seizure of a Hewlett Packard computer and various computer data storage devices from his apartment constituted a violation of his rights under the fourth and fourteenth amendments to the United States Constitution, as well as Conn. Const. art. I, § 7. After taking the seized items into custody and later viewing their contents, the police discovered over 200 images of the minor victim changing in and out of clothing and other child pornography images. The court held that the issuing judge was justified in concluding that there was probable cause to believe that the conduct of defendant was criminal in nature in that the affidavit indicated defendant created a situation in which a child was endangered and photographing a nude or seminude minor was a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21. Further, no staleness was found since the warrant affidavit supported a finding of an ongoing pattern of activity, and the fact that a Compaq computer was cited in the affidavit did not limit the search to only a computer by that name.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to suppress.

 

1366 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Friends of Animals, Inc. v. United Illuminating Co.


CV064018257


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2850



September 20, 2006, Decided  
September 20, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff environmental group filed an action against defendant electric utility. Plaintiff sought a declaratory judgment under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-16 that defendant was violating the Connecticut Environmental Protection Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-14 et seq. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the action for lack of subject matter jurisdiction or to strike the action for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had previously captured and killed monk parakeets that nested on its utility lines and poles. Defendant had stopped doing this but had not implemented measures to stop the birds from building their nests. Because of this, plaintiff argued, defendant was likely to resume killing the birds. The referee rejected defendant's argument that the action was not ripe. The "reasonably likely" language in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-17 allowed plaintiffs to challenge future conduct. Plaintiff had alleged circumstances under which, given the past conduct of defendant, it was reasonable to conclude that defendant was likely to engage in similar conduct in the future. Thus, the referee denied the motion to dismiss. As for the motion to strike, plaintiff had not judicially admitted that killing the birds was allowed under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 26-92 by stating that the birds' future conduct was a "potential public hazard." This was not an unequivocal statement that the birds constituted a public safety hazard. Finally, defendant had not shown that federal law would preempt Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-16, to the extent that the state law could be interpreted to prohibit the killing of monk parakeets.


OUTCOME: The referee denied the motion to dismiss and/or strike the action.

 

1367 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Perez v. Beaulieu


FA910105291S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2800



September 6, 2006, Decided  
September 6, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother filed a child support petition for a minor child. The trial court (Connecticut) granted the petition and a garnishment/wage withholding issued. The trial court granted a motion filed by defendant father, through the Connecticut Support Enforcement Division, to modify his child support order, and reduced the father's support obligation to zero. The child appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that he had no income due to his incarceration. The appellate court held that a deviation from the presumptive amount under the child guidelines was not warranted. The parent/child relationship did not factor significantly into the "best interest" analysis since the father's relationship with the child was likely to continue regardless of the disposition of the motion. Maintaining the support order was in the child's best interests. The father would owe approximately $ 13,400.00 after his incarceration, but he would be able to return to his former position as a union carpenter after he was released from prison in less than 11 months. Thus, a large, uncollectible arrearage would not accrue. The father testified that the child support arrearage would not interfere with his ability to see or have a relationship with his child. It was unlikely that the additional accrual of approximately $ 3,500.00 would result in a psychological hurdle of hopeless debt that would impede the parent/child relationship. As the statutory goals were not furthered and there were no equitable reasons that supported a reduction in the support order, equitable relief for the child was proper.


OUTCOME: This matter was remanded for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

 

1368 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Kelly v. State


CV054003595


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2660



August 30, 2006, Decided  
August 30, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the State of Connecticut, filed a motion to dismiss plaintiff patient's action on the grounds of lack of subject matter jurisdiction and on the prior pending action (PPA) doctrine. The patient filed suit, alleging medical negligence, and battery and lack of informed consent, arising from his treatment by a physician employed at a health care facility operated by the State.


OVERVIEW: The patient was treated by the physician for kidney problems, which included surgical intervention. Thereafter, he experienced blood in his urine for a period of years until it was discovered that laser fibers were left in his ureter. The patient underwent numerous surgeries to treat his condition, and he was granted permission to file suit against the State. Although initially dismissed as untimely, the patient obtained permission under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-148(b) to resubmit the claim through 2005 Conn. Acts 05-4, § 1 (Spec. Sess.). The State sought dismissal of the action. The court reviewed the analysis necessary to determine the constitutionality of a special act under Conn. Const. art. I, § 1. Analogizing the limitations period under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-148(a) to that of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-584, the court found that the patient's claim was untimely, as he should have discovered it when he was informed about the fibers and underwent surgery for their removal. There was no evidence that a state actor's procedural mistake precluded the timely filing of the complaint. Further, the special act did not serve a public purpose. Determination of the PPA doctrine was unnecessary.


OUTCOME: The court granted the State's motion and dismissed the action.

State v. Ward


CR05229868, CR05229902, CR05229942


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT MERIDEN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2606



August 25, 2006, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was charged with various crimes concerning the possession and distribution of narcotics, possession of paraphernalia, and illegal delivery of alcohol to a minor, made an application pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-693, for an examination to determine drug dependency and for an order to suspend prosecution pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-695.


OVERVIEW: The court found that (1) defendant was alcohol and/or drug dependent at the time of the alleged offenses; (2) defendant, at the time of the evaluation, was in need of and would have benefit from treatment for his dependency; (3) defendant was receiving long-term inpatient residential substance abuse treatment, as a result of his sentence in a youthful offender case; (4) defendant successfully completed the inpatient program; and (5) defendant was no longer in need of inpatient treatment for his dependency but rather, was in need of aftercare relapse prevention which would have include approximately two hours per week. The court concluded that suspension of prosecution would not have advanced the interest of justice. The offenses which defendant allegedly committed were egregious and troubling, taking place while he was awaiting sentencing. Further, a seventeen-year-old girl was nearly killed by the alleged acts of defendant in procuring, preparing, and injecting a dose of heroin into her arm. Thus, the interest of justice would not have been well served from a suspension of the prosecution under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-696.


OUTCOME: The motion to suspend prosecution was denied.

 

1370 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


In re Reginald H.


T11CP04012123A


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, CHILD PROTECTION SESSION AT MIDDLETOWN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2744



August 25, 2006, Decided  
August 25, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, Clarified by In re Reginald H., 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2677 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 6, 2006)
Judgment entered by In re Reginald H., 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3746 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 5, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court considered petitioner Connecticut Department of Children and Families' (DCF) two so-called "Romance motions" filed in a termination of parental rights case seeking disclosure of certain of respondent mother's confidential medical and substance abuse treatment information.


OVERVIEW: The DCF filed motions to have disclosed to it the mother's alcohol and drug abuse treatment records and her mental health, therapy, and counseling records. It sought to present subsequent testimony concerning such records. The mother asserted that the DCF's motion, by its own terms, sought records that were confidential based on state statutory privilege. The court found that given the type and number of the protections provided both by federal law relating to alcohol and drug abuse services and by state law for a variety of mental and physical health and related services, and given the carefully crafted and delineated federal and state law exceptions to disclosure of such confidential documents and information, neither the DCF nor anyone other than Congress or the General Assembly were authorized to create exceptions in addition to those specifically provided in federal and state law. Since the positions advanced by the DCF were not set forth as exceptions to disclosure in the applicable federal or state law or regulations, they were not available to the DCF as a basis for disclosure of the mother's legally protected confidential and privileged documents and information.


OUTCOME: The motions were denied.

Santoro v. Town of Hamden


CV040488583


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2418



August 18, 2006, Decided  
August 18, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents sued defendants, a town, the town's board of education (board), and three school officials (defendants), alleging that their son was subject to severe bullying behavior within the school system and that the school officials refused to take meaningful action to redress the problem. Defendants moved to strike the parents' first and second counts of their amended complaint.


OVERVIEW: The parents alleged in the first count that the defendants' actions denied their child equal educational opportunities. The defendants responded that such statement was conclusory and that the board was entitled to sovereign immunity because it was acting as an agency of the state. The instant court concluded that while there was a sufficient factual basis to support the claim, the board was immune, as the defendants were being sued in their capacity as agents of the State. As to the second count, in the absence of any applicable precedence directing a contrary outcome, the court found insufficient indicia that the legislature intended to create a private cause of action pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-222d. Hence, the second count was also stricken. Finally, the manner which a school district established its educational system, and the manner in which it implemented its bullying policy, were discretionary and contingent upon a multitude of variables, too numerous to permit any court to fashion a simple enjoinder which would not unduly interfere with governmental function.


OUTCOME: The motion was granted.

 

1372 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Kinney v. State


DNCV010456273S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2560



August 16, 2006, Decided  
August 18, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Kinney (Estate of Kinney) v. State, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 73 (Conn., Mar. 4, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Kinney v. State, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1610 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 29, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State moved for summary judgment in plaintiff administratrix's negligence action; the State claimed that the administratrix's claim was not timely under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-148(a).


OVERVIEW: After a judge died from a heart attack, the administratrix, inter alia, filed a workers' compensation claim against the State alleging that his condition was causally related to work-induced stress. The state supreme court decided that the judge was not an employee for purposes of entitlement to workers' compensation benefits. Thereafter, the legislature enacted 1994 Conn. Spec. Acts 13, § 1, allowing the administratrix to file an untimely action against the State. The court found that the administratrix's action was untimely because she was forced to litigate her claim to benefits when the State appealed the workers' compensation award. However, the authorization in § 1 conveyed a right to only the administratrix. It did not change the notice provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-148(a) and did not create relief from those requirements for others similarly aggrieved. There was no showing that the State had any action, involvement, or participation in the administratrix's failure to comply with the requirements in Chotkowski III. Consequently, because the act served no "public purpose" and was unconstitutional under Conn. Const. art. I, the State was entitled to summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The motion was granted.

Harris v. Coppetto


CV054013059


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2438



August 14, 2006, Decided  
August 15, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Harris v. Comm'r of Corr., 86 Conn. App. 903, 859 A.2d 979, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 517 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff arrestee sued defendants, who were trial referees, judges, attorneys, an investigator, court clerks, and court reporters, in their individual capacities, for violation of his civil and constitutional rights under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983 and 1985, resulting from an alleged false arrest and wrongful imprisonment of the arrestee. The defendants filed a motion to strike the arrestee's complaint.


OVERVIEW: The arrestee was apprehended on criminal charges of which he was convicted by a jury. His petition for habeas corpus was denied. He subsequently claimed that the parties against whom he brought his lawsuit were involved in the wrongful arrest and imprisonment of him in violation of his civil and constitutional rights. The court found that (1) the arrestee could not claim that his conviction and sentence were invalidated; (2) the principle of collateral estoppel prohibited the action; (3) the complaint was time-barred by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-577; (4) the prosecutor was entitled to absolute prosecutorial immunity; (5) the investigator and the court clerks were entitled to qualified immunity; (6) there was no indication that either of the court reporters knowingly violated the arrestee's constitutional rights; (6) the public defender was not subject to suit under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 as he was not acting under color of state law while performing as counsel to the arrestee; (7) the arrestee failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1985; and (8) the general doctrine of respondeat superior was not sufficient to state a claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike was granted.

 

1374 of 1861 DOCUMENTS



Loring v. Town of N. Haven Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV054014343


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2564



August 14, 2006, Decided  
August 14, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Loring v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n, 287 Conn. 746, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 279 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed the decision of defendant, a town planning and zoning commission, which denied plaintiff's application for a change of use. The form presented by plaintiff indicated that the use of the building at issue was a vacant barbershop and karate studio. The proposed use was to be a retail-adult book and video store with video preview booths.


OVERVIEW: The commission denied the change of use based on two reasons: video preview booths were not a permitted use and there was no suitable or adequate parking for a use which included 15 such booths. The court found that the first reason for the denial of plaintiff's application was illegal and arbitrary based on a proper construction of the town's own ordinances. The court noted that it was permitted to do nothing else but to try to give a neutral interpretation to the language of the town regulations, none of which were directed specifically at the type of adult entertainment use sought. Further, the court determined that the commission itself had not held that the operation of an adult book store was an unpermitted use. The court also found that the second reason for the denial failed to afford plaintiff fundamental fairness in the manner in which it was arrived at in that counsel for plaintiff was prepared to answer any questions regarding the parking issue, as would his engineer, but they were not given the opportunity by the commission.


OUTCOME: The court sustained plaintiff's appeal.

Wells Fargo Bank v. Bednarz

SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF ANSONIA - MILFORD, AT MILFORD

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bank filed an objection to defendant borrowers' application for judicial reformation of a mortgage; the bank claimed that the borrowers did not quality for protection under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-31f.


OVERVIEW: The borrowers owed a lender $ 305,600, as evidenced by a promissory note. As security for the note, the borrowers executed a mortgage on their property. The mortgage was later assigned to the bank. The bank thereafter exercised its option to declare the balance due and payable by virtue of nonpayment. The borrowers filed an application for judicial reformation of mortgage. The court determined that the borrowers' application was, in fact, an application for protection from foreclosure pursuant to § 49-31f. However, the borrowers failed to provide the court with any financial information as to earned income during the 12-month period preceding the foreclosure action or the two years preceding that 12-month period. Consequently, it was not possible to determine their eligibility for relief under § 49-31f.


OUTCOME: The application was denied without prejudice; the borrowers were ordered to refile with proper financial background within 15 days.


 

1376 of 1861 DOCUMENTS



Thomas v. Guyette


CV030081427


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2522



August 11, 2006, Decided  
August 11, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, four supervisors in their individual capacities, moved for summary judgment on all claims brought by plaintiffs, three employees. Plaintiffs brought a 10-count complaint, asserting claims pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, including violations of their constitutional rights to free speech, equal protection, and substantive due process rights as guaranteed by the first and fourteenth amendments to the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs worked for the Department of Transportation of the State of Connecticut in various positions and were working on a camera project together. One plaintiff had commented about an employee of Palestinian descent that he was engaged in blowing up cars. The employee complained and that plaintiff was reprimanded. Three months later, that plaintiff was removed from the camera project and claimed that his removal was as a result of the comment he made, which was protected by the first amendment. Another plaintiff had called the police when he discovered that a computer was missing and claimed that his call was speech that addressed a matter of public concern and was protected by the first amendment. The court found that the calling of the police was not speech that touched a matter of public concern. As to plaintiffs' equal protection claim counts, the court found that one plaintiff had shown genuine issues of material fact existed as to whether his comment about the other employee was being treated differently than others similarly situated but that the other two plaintiffs failed to show any genuine issue of material fact with regard to the police call.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' motion for summary judgment as to the first amendment and equal protection claims alleged by one plaintiff and granted the motion as to that plaintiff's substantive due process claim. The court granted defendant's motion as to all claims alleged by the other two plaintiffs.

Colon v. State Judicial Branch


CV065002208


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2389



August 8, 2006, Decided  
August 8, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by Colon v. State, 129 Conn. App. 59, 19 A.3d 699, 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 305 (2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former employee filed a five-count complaint against defendant State of Connecticut Judicial Department, his former employer. The Department filed a motion to dismiss the last four counts, which were for negligent and intentional infliction of emotional distress, breach of contractual rights, and wrongful discharge. The employee sought injunctive relief and damages.


OVERVIEW: The first count, which the Department did not seek to dismiss, was for retaliatory termination pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-290a. The Department argued that the other counts were barred by sovereign immunity. The court stated that one claiming to fall within any of the exceptions to the bar of sovereign immunity had to clearly show that the exception applied. The employee here had not done so. He had not pointed to any statutory authority whereby the legislature had waived the State's sovereign immunity as to the claims in counts two through five, and he had not expressly claimed or clearly demonstrated an incursion upon constitutionally protected rights or claimed that the State acted in excess of its statutory authority. The only argument the employee had made was that his complaint could reasonably be construed as one against his supervisor individually. The supervisor, however, had not been named as a defendant or referred to as one. Accordingly, the court granted the motion.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to dismiss the second through fifth counts of the complaint.

 

1378 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. McCullough


CR100074098


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2327



August 3, 2006, Decided  
August 3, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Connecticut filed a motion for the extension of the commitment of an acquittee who in 1985 had been placed under the jurisdiction of the Connecticut Psychiatric Security Review Board. The acquittee filed a motion to dismiss the commitment extension motion and a motion to strike the Board's report to the court.


OVERVIEW: The acquittee was committed in 1975 after he was acquitted on an assault charge by reason of mental disease or defect. The motion to strike the Board's report was rejected by the court. The court was required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593(d) to obtain the Board's report making it admissible as evidence. Admission of the report did not violate due process as the acquittee had a full opportunity to be involved in the hearing the Board conducted prior to making the report. The acquittee's Sixth Amendment cross-examination rights were satisfied when he cross-examined the Board's expert. There was no substantive due process violation. The motion to dismiss, based on the constitutionality of § 17a-593(c), was denied. The fact that the statute did not provide the same rights as were afforded in civil commitment proceedings was not an equal protection or other procedural due process violation. Finally, the state's motion was granted. The acquittee was mentally ill and had required antipsychotic medication since 1975. Without medication, which he would discontinue taking if left on his own, the acquittee rapidly decompensated and his violent behavior made him a threat to himself and others.


OUTCOME: The acquittee's motion to strike and motion to dismiss were both denied. The state's motion for continued commitment was granted.
