Gold v. Rowland


CV02813759


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2837



July 26, 2006, Decided  
July 26, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Gold v. Rowland, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 190 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 18, 2007)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by, Appeal dismissed by Gold v. Rowland, 296 Conn. 186, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 164 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Gold v. Rowland, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 68 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 10, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee of defendant State of Connecticut brought suit on his own behalf and that of persons similarly situated in connection with alleged misdelivery to and taking by the State of stock in defendant corporation, the parent of defendant insurer, which the employee claimed the corporation should have delivered to him and the other class members upon the insurer's conversion from a mutual insurance company to a stock insurance company.


OVERVIEW: Defendants in the action were (1) the State and its former Governor, ("State defendants"), who allegedly caused the State to sell the misdelivered stock despite conflicting claims as to its ownership, and thereafter to retain all proceeds from its sale for the use of the State; and (2) four related entities of the insurer. The State defendants filed a motion to dismiss. The employee alleged that the State defendants' sale of disputed stock and continuing retention of the proceeds constituted a taking under Conn. Const. art. I, § 11. Because the court was bound by supreme court precedent, it had to reject the State defendants' initial challenge to its subject-matter jurisdiction over the employee's constitutional takings claims. The court found that when the record was viewed in the light most favorable to the employee, there was at least a genuine issue of material fact as to whether he could establish that his and his fellow class members' "group as a whole" had a collective right under a conversion plan to receive stock or cash upon the demutualization of the insurer. The employee also based his takings claims upon a legitimate entitlement to a discrete property interest.


OUTCOME: Among other orders, the State defendants' motion to dismiss was granted as to all claims presented in counts three, four, five, six, seven, eight, nine, fourteen, fifteen, sixteen and seventeen of complaint II-A, and denied as to all claims based upon the employee's second (group as a whole) theory of entitlement to the disputed stock and stock sales proceeds, in counts ten, eleven, twelve and thirteen of complaint II-A.

In re Aaron B


W10CP02008469D, W10CP03009076D


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, CHILD PROTECTION SESSION AT MIDDLETOWN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2244



July 21, 2006, Decided  
July 21, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Commissioner of the Connecticut Department of Children and Families (DCF), filed a motion for modification of disposition by transfer of guardianship of a brother who had previously been adjudicated as neglected from DCF to his maternal grandmother. The Commissioner also filed a petition against respondents, mother and stepfather, to adjudicate a sister as neglected under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-120(9), (10) and for disposition.


OVERVIEW: At the neglect trial, DCF presented evidence of a lengthy history of intervention in respondents' family, which included four younger half-siblings. Child welfare workers, relatives, a court-ordered evaluator, and others testified that both respondents had personality disorders, that they did not or could not support themselves or their children, that they had histories of transience and substance abuse, that the stepfather was cruel, sadistic, and violent, and that the brother and sister had been parentified and abused. Both children had lived with the grandmother, who had temporary custody of the sister, for several years. They wished to continue to do so. The court granted the motion to transfer the brother's custody to the grandmother. The transfer was in his best interest and necessary for his safety, stability, security, and permanence, and return to respondents was not in his best interest. The court found that DCF had established by a fair preponderance of the evidence that the sister was neglected under § 46b-120(9), (10). It was in her best interest to be committed to DCF's custody, to remain in the grandmother's care, and to continue to live with her brother.


OUTCOME: The court found that the sister had been neglected and committed her care, custody, and guardianship to DCF until further order. The court vacated an order of temporary custody in favor of the grandmother with the expectation that DCF would allow the sister to continue to reside with the grandmother and the brother. The court granted the motion for transfer of care, custody, and guardianship of the brother to the grandmother.

 

1381 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Harris v. Comm'r of Corr.


CV030004038


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2198



July 21, 2006, Decided  
July 21, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Harris v. Comm'r of Corr., 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 241 (Conn. App. Ct., May 20, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Harris, 28 Conn. App. 474, 612 A.2d 123, 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 305 (1992)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was convicted of robbery in the first degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, and possession of a sawed-off shotgun. He filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, alleging ineffective assistance of counsel under the Sixth Amendment and violation of the Double Jeopardy Clause.


OVERVIEW: While brandishing a sawed-off shotgun, the inmate, assisted by two accomplices, robbed a man. When the inmate was apprehended, he had a sawed-off shotgun in his possession. The inmate argued that his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to object to the admission of the shotgun into evidence, for failing to prevent the State from joining the robbery charge with the possession of the shotgun charge, and for permitting a joint trial with the other two co-defendants. The trial court disagreed. Any attempt by defense counsel to try to limit the use of the shotgun would have been unsuccessful. While there was a remote possibility that the shotgun defendant possessed was not the one used in the robbery, there was more than enough circumstantial evidence to permit the jury to conclude that it was. Further, there was no basis on which defense counsel could have successfully resisted the joinder of defendants and offenses. Defendant's conviction of robbery and conspiracy to commit the same robbery did not violate the Double Jeopardy Clause. There was no basis to conclude that there was any unreliability in the inmate's conviction.


OUTCOME: The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

 

1382 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Washington v. Warden


CV030004300S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2222



July 21, 2006, Decided  
July 21, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Washington v. Comm'r of Corr., 287 Conn. 792, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 280 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner filed a pro se petition for a writ of habeas corpus and raised several claims. The prisoner asserted, inter alia, that respondent warden incorrectly calculated the prisoner's presentence confinement credits, that the alleged illegal lengthening of his confinement violated due process because it deprived him of the benefit of his plea bargain, and ineffective assistance of trial defense counsel.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner entered pleas in two dockets with an agreed upon total effective sentence of three years, to run concurrent with the sentences in two other dockets. In accordance with a plea agreement, he was sentenced to seven years to serve in the other two dockets. The judgment mittimus contained no order pertaining to presentence confinement credit. The prisoner insisted that the removal of 532 days of presentence confinement credit from one docket lengthened the seven-year sentence imposed in that docket. The appellate court held the prisoner's allegation that the 532 days were not applied to any docket was without merit. The prisoner was not deprived of any presentence confinement credits. Neither the State nor the judge made any promises regarding presentence confinement. The appellate court could not conclude that the State's conduct in any way implied that the State shared in the prisoner's understanding that he would receive the 532 days of presentence confinement credits at issue. The warden's calculations did not deprive him of the benefit of his plea bargain. The prisoner did not make a sufficient showing as to the performance or prejudice prong in regard to counsel.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

 

1383 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Kerrigan v. State


File No. CV-04 4001813


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


49 Conn. Supp. 644; 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2127; 909 A.2d 89



July 12, 2006, Decided  
July 12, 2006, Memorandum Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected October 31, 2006.
Reversed by, Remanded by Kerrigan v. Comm'r of Pub. Health, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 385 (Conn., Oct. 1, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Kerrigan v. State, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 618 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 3, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment denied; defendants' cross motion for summary judgment granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff same-sex couples filed an action against defendants, state and local agencies and officials, in which they sought a declaratory judgment and an injunction compelling defendants to issue them marriage licenses. Plaintiffs argued that the denial of a marriage license to same-sex couples violated Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 1, 4, 8, 10, 15, 14, and 20. Both parties filed motions for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The court noted that while the case was pending, the legislature had enacted 2005 Conn. Acts 10, allowing civil unions for same-sex couples but reserving marriage for opposite-sex couples. The act created an identical set of legal rights in Connecticut for same-sex and opposite-sex couples; thus, plaintiffs had failed to show that they had suffered legal harm. The court rejected plaintiffs' argument that their civil rights were still impaired under the new act. The new act conferred the legal benefits of marriage upon same-sex couples; it was to those rights, not with the nomenclature used to define them, that was of constitutional concern. Furthermore, nothing in the act could be read as giving same-sex couples a lesser status than opposite-sex couples. Next, the use of the terms "marriage" and "civil union" was a mere difference in nomenclature that was not enough to invoke an equal protection or due process analysis. Even if the term "civil union" was not generally accepted in common parlance, this did not amount to legal harm. Finally, although most other states did not recognize same-sex civil unions, this was not caused by the nomenclature used in the Connecticut act.


OUTCOME: The court denied plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment. It granted defendants' motion for summary judgment.

Martin v. Armstrong


CV020819915


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2081



July 7, 2006, Decided  
July 7, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former inmate filed an action against defendants, the former commissioner of the Connecticut Department of Correction (DOC) and a former warden, alleging that his constitutional rights were violated when unnamed DOC personnel listened to the inmate's conversations in his cell. The inmate sought $3,500 in damages. Defendants sought dismissal pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 10.30.


OVERVIEW: The inmate did not state whether he was suing defendant in their individual or official capacities. The court found that the inmate's lawsuit needed to be characterized as an official capacity lawsuit because defendants were employees of the state at the time the lawsuit was commenced and the inmate was suing for conduct that related to defendants' employment. The court found that the state was the real party against whom relief was sought because the inmate sought to change conduct and policies with respect to the operation of a prison facility. Because the court concluded that the complaint was an action against defendants in their official capacity, the court found that the lawsuit was barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The state had not consented to suit under the circumstances alleged in the lawsuit and had not waived its sovereign immunity. Additionally, even if the complaint could be construed as an action against defendants in their individual capacities, the statutory immunity conferred by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165 applied. The inmate had not alleged that defendants acted wantonly or maliciously or outside the discharge of their duties or scope of employment.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motion to dismiss.

State v. Dickinson


CR840023695


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2046



July 7, 2006, Decided  
July 7, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the State of Connecticut, filed a petition, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593(c), for an order of continued commitment of respondent acquittee. The acquittee filed a motion to strike the Connecticut Psychiatric Security Review Board's report, which recommended that the acquittee be recommitted for a period not to exceed four years. The acquittee also filed a motion to dismiss the State's petition for recommitment.


OVERVIEW: The Board recommended that the acquittee be recommitted for a period as it believed that he remained an individual with psychiatric disabilities to the extent that his discharge would have constituted a danger to himself or others. The court found that the admission of the report did not violate the acquittee's constitutional rights under the Sixth Amendment and Conn. Const. art. I, § 8 as (1) the acquittee had the opportunity to take part in the Board's hearing and present his own witnesses; (2) the acquittee, at the hearing before the court, cross-examined the State's psychiatrist, the sole witness at the Board's hearing; and (3) the admission of the report did not violate the acquittee's substantive due process rights. The court noted that none of the psychiatrists was able to testify that the acquittee would be a substantial or imminent danger to himself or others if he were let out of confinement. Thus, the court found that the State did not meet its burden of proving, by clear and convincing evidence, that the acquittee was mentally ill and a substantial danger to himself or to others, that he was gravely disabled, or that he was an imminent danger to himself or others.


OUTCOME: The acquittee's motions to dismiss and to strike were denied. In addition, the petition for an order of continued commitment was denied.

Wright v. Comm'r of Corr.


CV030004054


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT SOMERS


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2047



July 6, 2006, Decided  
July 6, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Wright v. Comm'r of Corr., 106 Conn. App. 342, 942 A.2d 438, 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 93 (Mar. 11, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Wright, 77 Conn. App. 80, 822 A.2d 940, 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 233 (May 27, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus after his convictions in the Superior Court, Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), for being an accessory to murder, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a; use of a firearm in the commission of a Class A Felony, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-202k; and carrying a pistol without a permit, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35(a). Defendant was sentenced to confinement. His appeal was denied.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of shooting the victim during an altercation at a party. He made numerous allegations that he was denied the effective assistance of counsel guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. VI. After considering all of the evidence presented at the habeas trial, the court found that defendant was not deprived of the effective assistance of counsel as the court was not persuaded that defendant met his burden of proving ineffective assistance of counsel. Specifically, the court found that (1) trial counsel was not at fault for failing to move to suppress a jacket found at the scene of the crime when there was no viable basis to so do; (2) trial counsel's failures to employ experts was neither deficient performance nor prejudicial; and (3) while the trial evidence clearly supported a finding that defendant and his brother were engaged in a joint adventure such that, if nothing else, defendant could have been held vicariously liable for the murder of the victim, trial counsel made sufficient efforts to cast doubt upon the government charges. Thus, there simply was no basis upon which the habeas court could conclude that there was any unreliability in defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

 

1387 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Sullivan v. McDonald


CV064010696


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2073



June 30, 2006, Decided  
June 30, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Request granted, Request denied by, On reconsideration by, Reargument denied by Sullivan v. McDonald, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2551 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 24, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a justice of the state's highest court, filed suit against defendants, the chairmen of a legislative committee, seeking an ex-parte temporary injunction to quash a subpoena, a temporary and a permanent injunction, and an order to temporarily quash the subpoena. Intervenor, Connecticut Judicial Department was allowed to intervene. The trial court (Connecticut) supplemented its decision for the justice from the bench with this opinion.


OVERVIEW: Whether a legislative committee could obligate a sitting judicial officer to testify by way of a subpoena was a matter of first impression. The trial court noted that the subpoena was issued under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 2-46, which the Connecticut Attorney General had opined vested the Connecticut legislature with the broadest possible subpoena authority consistent with legislative powers. However, in the absence of express constitutional authority, the legislative branch's authority to subpoena members of the judiciary was not coterminous with its broad legislative authority. Under the separation of powers doctrine, the legislature could not subpoena a judicial official to give testimony relating to his official duties or functions, except where the Connecticut Constitution expressly permitted it, such as in the impeachment process. The subpoena was not issued pursuant to the appointment process. The trial court was confident that much of the information sought could be produced through voluntary cooperation. Further, the disciplinary process through the Connecticut Judicial Review Council created a very significant remedial framework to address the allegations of judicial misconduct.


OUTCOME: The trial court granted the motion to quash the subpoena and issued a temporary injunction barring any further requisite attendance at the hearing on the part of the justice.

 

1388 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Anamasi v. State


CV054016000S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1943



June 27, 2006, Decided  
June 27, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, State of Connecticut, Judicial Branch, filed a motion to strike plaintiff judicial marshals' complaint for injunctive relief and damages for violation of the Connecticut Fair Employments Practices Act, Conn. Gen. Stat.§ 46a-58. The basis of the motion was the failure of the judicial marshals to name a necessary party to the action.


OVERVIEW: The marshals were members of a union local, working under a contract negotiated with the Judicial Branch by the union. The marshals were denied promotions because they were unable to obtain commercial driver's licenses, which the marshals blamed on their physical disabilities. The promotion qualifications were part of a contract negotiated by the union with the Judicial Branch. The Judicial Branch asserted that the union was a necessary party the union would have to work with the Judicial Branch if modifications to the contract were ordered by the court. The marshals denied that the union was a necessary party. The motion to strike was denied, but the court directed that the union be cited in as a party. The union was not an indispensible party in the employment discrimination case because its absence would not prejudice its rights. Any liability the Judicial Branch owned to the marshals was separable from the union's interest. However, the union did have an interest in the litigation, which made it the type of party whose presence was necessary to do complete justice by adjusting all the rights involved, particularly in light of the marshals' claim for injunctive relief.


OUTCOME: The Judicial Branch's motion to strike was denied, however, its alternative request that the marshals be ordered to revise their complaint to add the union as a party was granted. The marshals were ordered to cite in the union as a party within 30 days.

Vacirca v. Town of Brookfield Inland Wetlands Comm'n


DBDCV044000381S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DANBURY, AT DANBURY


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1945



June 27, 2006, Decided  
June 27, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed two decisions of defendant Inland Wetlands Commission which denied the property owner's request to build a barn. The court consolidated the first and second appeal.


OVERVIEW: The parcel in question consisted of 0.36 acres and had wetlands running diagonally across it, comprising 57 percent of the entire parcel. The court found overwhelming support for the decision of the Commission. In fact there was scant evidence to support the proposition that the proposed use of the property would not have an adverse impact on the wetlands. Therefore, there was sufficient substantial evidence in the record to support the Commission's conclusion that the proposed activity would have an adverse impact on the wetlands as to both applications. The court also concluded that sufficient substantial evidence existed to support the Commission's conclusion that there were reasonable and prudent alternatives available to the property owner and the Commission's denial of the applications on that basis. Insofar as the language of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-41(b)(2) was directory and not mandatory, the court found the actions of the Commission and the written record sufficient to comply with the provisions of § 22a-41(b)(2).


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

1390 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Int'l Motorcars, LLC v. Sullivan


HHBCV054005168


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1956



June 20, 2006, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company filed a one-count complaint alleging negligence against defendant state marshal for alleged property damage to a vehicle that the company purportedly owned when the state marshal seized the vehicle in connection with a matter pending in a trial court. The state marshal filed a motion to dismiss the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The company filed a complaint alleging that the state marshal was negligent for property damage to the company's vehicle that occurred when the state marshal seized the vehicle in connection with a matter pending before a trial court. The allegations of the complaint only alleged the state marshal's conduct acting as a state marshal, and did not assert any conduct that the state marshal took outside of his position as a state marshal. The state marshal filed a motion to dismiss and alleged that the company's lawsuit was barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity, which meant that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to hear the case. The trial court granted the state marshal's motion to dismiss. The trial court found that the Spring test dictated that the lawsuit was one against a state official, that the state lawsuit concerned a matter in which the state official represented the state, that the state was the real party in interest, and that a judgment against the state marshal would hinder the activities of the state marshal commission. As a result, the trial court found that company's lawsuit was barred by the sovereign immunity doctrine.


OUTCOME: The trial court granted the motion to dismiss.

Morgan v. Bubar


562555


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1828



June 15, 2006, Decided  
June 15, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Morgan v. Bubar, 115 Conn. App. 603, 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 319 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Morgan v. Bubar, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2404 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 29, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state employee brought an action in four counts against defendants, a co-worker and two supervisors, in their individual capacities, alleging defamation per se, and a violation of her equal protection and due process rights that the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution guaranteed and that 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 protected. Defendants filed a motion for summary judgment, alleging qualified, absolute, and sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: The employee claimed that the co-worker accused her of an assault under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-61 and that the supervisors did not investigate her claims, thus violating her equal protection rights by selectively enforcing certain workplace policies. Defendants argued that the statements were immune because they were made in quasi-judicial proceeding, that of an affirmative action investigation. The court concluded that genuine issues of material fact existed as to whether an affirmative action investigation existed or whether the meeting at which the statement was made was part of an investigation. While defendants argued a lack of proof of harm to the employee's reputation, but the court ruled that the alleged statement was defamation per se because an assault carried a jail sentence. Thus, the employee did not have to plead or prove harm to her reputation; it was presumed. As the parties disputed whether the workplace policy, which was based on a state order on workplace violence, was selectively applied, summary judgment was not due; that was particularly true when intent was an issue. There was also a genuine issue as to whether defendants' conduct was objectively reasonable.


OUTCOME: Defendants' motion for summary judgment was denied.

 

1392 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


DaimlerChrysler Corp. v. Law


CV054007725S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN, TAX SESSION AT NEW BRITAIN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1718



June 9, 2006, Decided  
June 9, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Dismissed by DaimlerChrysler Corp. v. Law, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3191 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 25, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's request for leave to amend its 9/23/05 complaint denied and the defendant's objections to paragraphs 28 through 37 of the proposed amended complaint sustained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff motor vehicle manufacturer sought permission, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 10-60(a), to amend its one-count complaint, by adding an additional ten paragraphs. Defendant, the Connecticut commissioner of revenue services, filed objections. The manufacturer was seeking a refund of certain sales and use tax payments.


OVERVIEW: The sales and use taxes were paid in conjunction with certain vehicles that the manufacturer had to repurchase from consumers under the Connecticut Lemon Law, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-179(d). The court denied the request for leave to amend, sustaining each of the commissioner's objections. The amendments improperly alleged a standard of review under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-183 as tax appeals were de novo appeals that did not fall under § 4-183. One paragraph's vague references to threatened rights fell because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-422 provided the manufacturer with an adequate remedy at law for preserving its rights. The manufacturer's attempt to raise the constitutionality of the Lemon Law failed as it could not seek the relief provided by the Lemon Law while at the same time raising questions of constitutionality. One proposed new paragraph fell for failure to comply with Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 10-1. Finally, the manufacturer could not invoke Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-29s or claim it was unconstitutional as the court was without authority to evaluate the merits of the commissioner's decision regarding the refund claim.


OUTCOME: The request for permission to amend the complaint was denied. The commissioner's objections to the requested amendment were sustained.

 

1393 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Duquette v. Corradi


CV054002769, Opinion No.: 93881


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1804



June 9, 2006, Decided  
June 9, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff arrestee brought an action against defendant state troopers pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-592, alleging that the troopers used excessive force in arresting her and that they subjected her to certain indignities and deliberate injury. The troopers filed a motion to dismiss counts two, three, and four, based on the doctrine of common-law sovereign immunity and the statutory provision for personal immunity in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165.


OVERVIEW: The arrestee claimed in part that the officers stomped on her chest and ordered a dog to attack her, which it did. The court denied their motion to dismiss, concluding that their conduct showed a wanton and reckless disregard for the arrestee's rights and safety, that it went beyond the scope of their official duties, and that § 4-165 thus did not bar the claims. The court also concluded that the troopers had been sued in their individual capacities. There were for criteria to determining whether a suit was against a state or against state employees personally. While the officers were state employees, and the suit concerned an arrest in which they represented the state, the state was not the real party against which relief was sought, and the judgment would not subject the state to liability. Because the complaint sufficiently alleged actions from which wanton, reckless, or malicious conduct could be inferred, the challenged counts fit within an exception to § 4-165. The court also ruled that under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 5-141d and 29-8a, the State of Connecticut had to "save harmless" and indemnify a state officer only if the officer's conduct was not wanton, reckless, or malicious.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss.

 

1394 of 1861 DOCUMENTS



Czeczotka v. State


CV054002599, Opinion No.: 93711


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1667



May 30, 2006, Decided  
May 30, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured persons alleged in counts three and four of their complaint, that defendant state trooper was liable for injuries they incurred due to the trooper's operation of her cruiser in a reckless manner and in excess of her statutory authority as a state police officer. The trooper moved to dismiss those counts as they were for monetary damages against her in her official capacity and were barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: The injured persons' truck collided with the trooper's state police cruiser. The injured persons filed a request to amend so as to remove the references they made to the trooper's official capacity and to add language to clarify that they intended to allege their claims against the trooper in her individual capacity. They argued that the mistake was a misnomer, which they should be permitted to correct pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-123. The injured persons sought monetary damages and did not seek a waiver from the claims commissioner before bringing their action. The court found that the essential nature of injured persons' allegations regarding the trooper was more akin to the nature of "official capacity" claims rather than "individual capacity" claims. Clearly, the injured persons alleged in counts three and four claims for monetary damages against the trooper in her official capacity. In light of that conclusion, the injured persons were required to seek the permission of the claims commissioner to bring the action. Thus, the doctrine of sovereign immunity barred the claims.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted.


 

1395 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Fiamengo v. Fox


CV065001957S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1658



May 26, 2006, Decided  
May 26, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant special public defender filed a motion to dismiss plaintiff client's action alleging that he breached a contract and failed to properly represent the client in a habeas corpus or criminal proceeding. The public defender claimed that he had official immunity and that the client had failed to exhaust administrative remedies under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165.


OVERVIEW: The pro se client's complaint consisted of one count alleging legal malpractice and the infliction of emotional distress. The client did not allege that the public defender's actions resulted in any conviction or that a conviction had been invalidated before the action was filed. The court granted the motion to dismiss the action. Taken in the light most favorable to the plaintiff, the complaint's allegations did not establish that the public defender acted in a wanton, reckless, or malicious manner or that his state of mind or his conduct rose to the requisite level of egregiousness. He was therefore immune from suit under § 4-165. Under § 4-165, any person seeking damages against a state employee who was immune from suit could file a claim with the Connecticut State Claims Commission, and failure to exhaust this remedy was grounds for dismissal for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The complaint did not allege that any claim had been filed with the Commission or that the Connecticut Claims Commissioner had authorized a civil action pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-160. The complaint was therefore subject to dismissal for failure to exhaust administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The court granted the public defender's motion to dismiss the client's complaint.

 

1396 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Gresczyk v. Landis


HHDCV044004887


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1593



May 25, 2006, Decided  
May 25, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Gresczyk v. Landis, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 303 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 31, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's motion to strike the defendant's three special defenses are granted and all of those items stricken. Defendants' counterclaim dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Commissioner of Agriculture filed an action for declaratory and injunctive relief against defendant trustees to enjoin them from developing land as a golf course. The Commissioner filed a motion to strike the trustees' new special defenses and a motion to dismiss the trustees' counterclaim.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner had purchased development rights from the trustees' predecessor in interest pursuant to the farmland preservation program in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22-26aa et seq. The court first held that when it granted the trustees' motion to amend their answer, this did not bar the Commissioner from filing motions to strike and to dismiss. It was usually inappropriate in ruling on a motion to amend to address the merits of the underlying action that was the subject of the motion. Turning to the special defenses, the court stated that the farmland preservation program was not inconsistent with the state plan of conservation and development set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16a-27. The trustees' attack on the administration of the program was not an appropriate special defense. The trustees' argument that a golf course was a "turf farm" was unconvincing. As for the counterclaim alleging inverse condemnation, to survive a motion to dismiss on the ground of sovereign immunity, it had to allege sufficient facts to support a finding of a constitutional taking. The trustees had alleged nothing more than a diminution in value. This was insufficient to show a constitutional taking.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to strike the special defenses. It dismissed the trustees' counterclaim.

 

1397 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


DeMartino v. DeMartino


FA064018875S, Opinion No.: 93674


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1524



May 23, 2006, Decided  
May 25, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father, as next friend of his minor child, filed an application for a restraining order against defendant mother pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-15. The mother filed a motion to dismiss the application, or, in the alternative, to consolidate with a pending dissolution of marriage action.


OVERVIEW: The court was required to decide whether a pending dissolution action between the father and the mother required dismissal of the action for a restraining order. The court was also required to decide whether the appointment of a guardian ad litem for the minor child divested the father of standing to bring the action for a restraining order on behalf of his minor child. The court noted that the father brought the action not in his own right, but on behalf of the minor child, who, because of age, was incompetent under the law to bring suit on his own. The court could find no reason why the minor child was not entitled to the procedures and protections of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-15. Thus, dismissal of the restraining order action on the grounds of a prior pending action was not proper. Additionally, the dissolution and the restraining order actions did not involve identical parties. Moreover, the legal and factual issues were distinctly different. Thus, the granting of the motion to consolidate was not proper. Finally, a hearing was necessary to determine whether the guardian ad litem was the proper person to bring the § 46b-15 application on the minor child's behalf at that time.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied, and the motion to consolidate was denied. Further, the clerk was directed to schedule a hearing to determine whether a guardian ad litem was to be substituted for the father as next friend for the minor and, if not, whether the father was the proper person to maintain the action.

 

1398 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Northrup


CR030023375


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1478



May 18, 2006, Decided  
May 18, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who pled guilty to risk of injury to a minor and sexual assault in the fourth degree, moved for a reduction of his sentence. Defendant was sentenced to a total effective sentence of six years, execution suspended after two years, and 10 years' probation. The parties agreed that the primary issue was one of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a motion to modify his sentence seeking to suspend the execution of the remainder of the two-year sentence he was serving. Defendant contended that the court possessed both a rule-based and an inherent jurisdiction to modify the sentences it previously imposed. Given that the defendant's sentence consists of a "top" number of greater than three years and a "bottom" number of less than three years, the question of whether Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-39(a) or (b) applied necessarily depended on the part of the split sentence which was properly characterized as the "definite sentence" referred to in § 53a-39. The court held that the sentence imposed upon defendant was a "definite sentence" of six years and that, accordingly, § 53a-39(b) applied. Under § 53a-39(b), the court lacked jurisdiction to entertain a motion to modify a sentence unless the state's attorney agreed to defendant's request for review. It was undisputed that the state's attorney did not agree. Also, defendant did not meet his burden of proving that the statutory scheme for sentence modification was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion for a reduction of his sentence was dismissed.

 

1399 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Warner v. Town of Salisbury Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV054001847S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD, AT LITCHFIELD


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1364



May 15, 2006, Decided  
May 15, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a neighbor, appealed from a decision of defendant, a city planning and zoning commission, which ruled that the application by defendant, a seller, to subdivide her commercial real property and sell a portion thereof to defendant, a purchaser, was a so-called "first cut" and was, therefore, not subject to the town's subdivision regulations.


OVERVIEW: In his appeal, the neighbor not only challenged the decision concerning the subdivision, but sought to overturn an alleged change of zone granted on July 21, 2000. The seller argued that any review by the court of the July 21, 2000, decision was barred by General Statutes § 8-8(r). The court initially noted that the neighbor failed to plead aggrievement regarding the 2000 decision. The neighbor did not own his abutting property at the time of the 2000 decision, so he was not classically aggrieved. The court further held that the fact that the neighbor held a first mortgage on the property at the time of the decision did not render him statutorily aggrieved under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8. The neighbor failed to show that he would be denied the ability to recover the full amount of the principal remaining on the mortgage through foreclosure. Therefore, the neighbor failed to establish aggrievement as to the 2000 decision. The court further held that his appeal of the 2000 decision was time-barred under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8(r). The court held that this statute acted as a statute of limitations, and the appeal was not filed in a timely fashion.


OUTCOME: The neighbor was barred from challenging the July 21, 2000 decision of the commission.

 

1400 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Peruccio v. Comm'r of Corr.


CV040004450


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT SOMERS


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1376



May 9, 2006, Decided  
May 9, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Peruccio v. Comm'r of Corr., 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 144 (Conn. App. Ct., Apr. 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Peruccio, 47 Conn. App. 188, 702 A.2d 1200, 1997 Conn. App. LEXIS 523 (1997)



DISPOSITION: The Petition for a Writ of Habeas Corpus is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a prisoner, sought a writ of habeas corpus challenging his convictions of manslaughter in the 1st degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55(a)(3), and risk of injury to a minor in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21, and the resultant sentence to 20 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted after a child that had been left in his care died of injuries indicating that the child had been shaken. The prisoner argued that he received ineffective assistance of counsel in violation of both the United States and Connecticut Constitutions. The court held that trial counsel's decision not to hire a hiring a neuropathologist to advise on the case did not constitute ineffective assistance of counsel. There was an abundance of circumstantial evidence that pointed to the conclusion that the fatal action occurred during the time in which petitioner was the only adult with access to the child. Nothing at the habeas trial in any way attacked that evidence. The court found that trial counsel mounted a spirited attack on the evidence through the use of another expert witness. The court further held that the prisoner failed to show that the failure to call a neuropathologist prejudiced him. Based on the evidence presented at trial, the prisoner was unable to show a reasonable probability that hiring the neuropathologist would have changed the outcome of the trial.


OUTCOME: The habeas corpus petition was denied.
